People v. Majewski


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


78 Misc. 2d 52; 355 N.Y.S.2d 548; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1326



May 9, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought a motion to dismiss the indictment charging him with possession and sale of methadone, each an A-I felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession and sale of methadone, each an A-I felony, and brought a motion to dismiss the indictment. Defendant assailed the constitutionality of part of N.Y. Penal Law § 220. He claimed his right to equal protection of the laws under U.S. Const. amend. XIV had been violated by reason of differentiation in weight standards by which guilt for sale and possession of various substances was determined, namely, aggregate weight of substances containing one or more ounces of a narcotic drug, as against pure weight of other drugs. The court denied the motion, holding that convenience or practicality was not the objective of N.Y. Penal Law § 220 and related statutes, and that the intention of the legislature was to alter the provisions of the existing laws for the purpose of airing defects which experience had disclosed, all within the framework of the objective to stem the flow of dangerous drugs to the illicit market.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- dangerous drugs sale and possession of drugs -- weight classification -- differentiation in weight standards contained, in article 220 of Penal Law, by which guilt for sale and possession of various substances is determined, is constitutional and does not violate defendant's Fourteenth Amendment right to equal protection of laws.

The defendant was indicted for possession and sale of methadone. The provisions of article 220 of the Penal Law which contain differentiation in weight standards by which guilt for sale and possession of various substances is determined, namely by classifying narcotic drugs by aggregate weight as against pure weight of other drugs, are constitutional and do not violate defendant's Fourteenth Amendment right to equal protection of the laws. Police convenience is not the objective of the statute. The need for classification of the various drugs and substances according to their intrinsic qualities, mode of use and abuse, manner of distribution, degrees of addiction or dependence, the reasons for general classification of "hard" and "soft" drugs, the interests to be protected of both the individual and of society,  [***2] and the need for conformity, where possible, to Federal and uniform acts, all amply support a finding that in no way are the statutes unconstitutional. ( People v. Daneff, 37 A D 2d 918, affd. 30 N Y 2d 793, mot. to amend remittitur granted 31 N Y 2d 667, rearg. den. 31 N Y 2d 709, cert. den. 410 U.S. 913 followed.)

 

1462 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Beaudouin v. Board of Trustees


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


78 Misc. 2d 258; 356 N.Y.S.2d 736; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1377



May 6, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officers filed an action for declaratory relief and for coercive action against defendants, by which they sought a declaration that the legislature in enacting New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § B18-4.0(j), which provided for a full pension after 35 years of service, did not intend to exclude from pension benefits those who attained the age of 63 prior to completing 35 years of service.


OVERVIEW: The police officers filed a suit for declaratory relief against defendants in which they argued that the legislature, in enacting New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § B18-4.0(j), which provided for a full pension to members of the police pension fund who completed 35 years of service, did not intend to exclude from the benefit of a full pension those who attained the age of 63 years prior to completing 35 years of service. New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 434a-21.0 provided that no member of the police force who was eligible and obtained 63 years would have continued to serve as a member of the police force, and pursuant to this statute defendants forced police officers to retire at 63. The police officers sought a declaration that defendants' actions in implementing the provisions were unconstitutional. The court found for defendants, holding that neither the intent nor the extent of New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code §§ B18-4.0(j) and 434a-21.0 were ambiguous. It was assumed that the legislature in enacting New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § B18-4.0(j) was aware of the mandatory retirement age of 63. Thus, the legislature did not envision benefits greater than those expressed.


OUTCOME: The court rendered judgment in favor of defendants on the police officers' suit seeking a declaration that the legislature did not intend to exclude police officers who attained the age of 63 prior to completing 35 years of service from receiving a full pension and that such exclusion was invalid and unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil service -- retirement -- members of New York City Police Pension Fund, Article 1, subject to compulsory retirement at age 63, have no right to complete 35 years of service in order to qualify for additional benefit, where retirement occurred prior to amendment of section 434a-21.0 of Administrative Code -- there is no proof of contrary legislative intent -- there is no violation of constitutional provisions.

1. Plaintiffs were or had been members of the police force of the City of New York and were members of the Police Pension Fund, Article 1, which allows, under section B18-4.0 (subd. j) of the Administrative Code of the City of New York, a pension at full pay to retirees completing 35 years of service. Section 434a-21.0 of the code mandates retirement for members of the police force at 63 years of age who are eligible for pension benefits. Plaintiffs who retired prior to completing 35 years of service have no right to either a prorata share of full pay or reinstatement. As to those plaintiffs who are still members as of the effective date of amended section B18-4.0 (subd. j), which allows completion of 35 years of service, this case is moot.

2. There has been no [***2] offer of proof of a legislative intent to benefit those members with less than 35 years of service who are forced to retire at age 63, nor has there been prompt subsequent legislative action which would manifest such an intent. It is reasonable to assume that the Legislature intended only to confer additional benefits on those with more than 35 years of service.

3. There is no breach of either the due process and equal protection clauses of the Constitution or the contractual relationship of pension membership established by the New York Constitution, since it is long settled that section 434a-21.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York violates no constitutional provision. Accordingly, the defendants are declared to have acted lawfully and reasonably.

 

1463 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Koutrakos v. Long Island College Hospital


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Kings County


78 Misc. 2d 39; 355 N.Y.S.2d 718; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1323



May 3, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Compensation of plaintiff's attorney was to be determined following presentation of an order of compromise in a wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's wrongful death suit was settled, and an order of comprise was submitted, with the determination of compensation owed to plaintiff's counsel to be determined by the court. Noting that an attorney's fee was usually based on the net amount recovered after deducting expenses without regard to claims that others may assert against plaintiff's recovery, the court concluded that to repay the workers' compensation carrier in full required the plaintiff to bear the entire cost of attorneys fees. As such, N.Y. Workers' Comp. Law § 29(1) was unconstitutional and unenforceable, as it violated the due process and equal protection guarantees of the federal and state constitutions. Had plaintiff not sued and the insurance carrier exercised its option to do so, it would have been required to sue for plaintiff's pecuniary loss at its own expense. To require plaintiff to pay the attorneys fees out of the net recovery required her to pay the expense of recovering the carrier's money and lessened her rightful recovery.


OUTCOME: Compensation of plaintiff's attorney was to be made in accordance with the percentage formula established by the appellate division's rules, but the court concluded that a state workers' compensation law was unconstitutional and unenforceable in requiring plaintiff to solely bear the burden of attorneys fees without requiring the workers' compensation carrier, reimbursed from the settlement amount, to bear any obligation therefor.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Workmen's compensation -- attorney's fees -- carrier's lien -- upon compromise of wrongful death action against third party after plaintiff received workmen's compensation award, subdivision 1 of section 29 of Workmen's Compensation Law declared unconstitutional to extent that it required plaintiff's settlement be reduced by full amount of her attorney's fees -- requiring plaintiff to pay out of net recovery fees paid to her attorney and to give carrier "free ride" at plaintiff's expense limits plaintiff's right of full recovery in wrongful death action contrary to section 16 of article I of New York State Constitution.

1. After receiving a workmen's compensation award, the compromise of a wrongful death action against a third party resulted in a settlement for plaintiff in the amount of $ 150,000. The insurance carrier liable for payment of the compensation award has a lien against any recovery against a third party "to the extent of the total amount of compensation awarded * * * and to such extent such recovery shall be deemed for the benefit of such fund, person, association, corporation or carrier." (Workmen's Compensation Law, § 29, subd. 1.) The amount of the lien was [***2] fixed at $ 20,870. To the extent that the provisions of subdivision 1 of section 29 of the Workmen's Compensation Law require the plaintiff to reduce her recovery by the full amount of the attorney's fee, including the part that should equitably be chargeable to the collection of the carrier's lien, they are unconstitutional and unenforceable as violating the due process and equal protection guarantees of the Federal and State Constitutions.

2. To require plaintiff to pay out of the net recovery the fees paid to her attorney and to give the carrier a "free ride" at her expense is not only unconscionable but, in limiting and lessening plaintiff's right of full recovery in a wrongful death action, it is contrary to section 16 of article I of the State Constitution.

 

1464 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


North Hempstead v. North Hills


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


78 Misc. 2d 54; 355 N.Y.S.2d 940; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1327



April 30, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The complaint is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff town's complaint on the ground that the town was barred from bringing this action by N.Y. Village Law § 7-706, that the town had no standing to sue, that the town was not an aggrieved person, and that the complaint was merely conclusory.


OVERVIEW: The town filed an action against the village following the village's rezoning of a certain residential area. Zoning was amended from allowing one residence per every two acres to fours residences per acre. The court held that the town was a creature of the state legislature and had only such powers and authority as the legislature granted it by statute, and no more. The court noted that town failed to show affirmative statutory authority to bring its action and that the town failed to show how the town or its residents would be aggrieved by this change in zoning. The town also failed to show, by its various citations, that it had affirmative case authority to sue as an aggrieved party, nor did the town establish how or why the amended zoning rules were unconstitutional. The court noted that merely labeling a proceeding an "action" and alleging unconstitutionality did not remove the legislated requirements and prohibitions of N.Y. Village Law § 7-706(1) and § 7-712(3). The court therefore held that the town was not an aggrieved party and that it had no authority to bring its action.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the town's complaint holding that it was not an aggrieved party.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- plaintiff town's complaint attacking validity of defendant village's cluster zoning ordinances is dismissed; town had no authority to bring suit, had no standing, and was barred by section 7-706 of Village Law.

1. Plaintiff town's complaint attacking the validity of the defendant village's cluster zoning ordinances is dismissed. The town, having only such powers and authority as the Legislature grants by statute, has failed to show affirmative statutory authority to bring this action.

2. The town has also failed to show that it has authority to sue as an aggrieved party.

3. The town is barred from bringing the action by section 7-706 of the Village Law which states that "Such * * * town * * * shall not have the right of review by a court as hereinafter provided."

 

1465 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hodgkins v. Central School Dist.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Broome County


78 Misc. 2d 91; 355 N.Y.S.2d 932; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1337



April 29, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teachers filed motions seeking a preliminary injunction and summary judgment in their action against defendant school district, that sought an injunction invalidating disciplinary proceedings brought against the teachers pursuant to N.Y. Educ. Law § 3020-a and a declaratory judgment that suspension or termination of the teachers pursuant to § 3020-a constituted a denial of their constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner of Education (commissioner), in light of a United States district court case declaring the procedures established for the discipline of tenured teachers unconstitutional, modified those regulations to correct the constitutional defects noted by the district court. The teachers argued that the commissioner exceeded his authority in amending the regulations. The teachers also argued that the school district could not have denied pay to a tenured teacher pending a hearing under § 3020-a and that it was a violation of their due process rights to suspend and remove a tenured teacher from the classroom prior to a hearing. The court granted the motions in part. The court found that the commissioner was acting within his lawfully delegated authority in amending the regulations and was giving effect to the general policy and underlying intent of the legislature when it enacted § 3020-a. The court noted that it was a due process violation to have denied compensation to a suspended teacher with tenure until after a meaningful hearing, but that it was not a due process violation to suspend a teacher and remove him from the classroom pending such a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment in favor of the teachers, enjoined the school district from suspending their pay and compensation pending a hearing, and directed the school district to pay the teachers the compensation due them from the date of suspension. The court granted summary judgment in favor of the school district declaring their right to suspend the teachers and remove them from their teaching duties pending a hearing.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Schools -- teachers -- Board of Regents and Commissioner of Education acted within their lawfully delegated authority when, to overcome constitutional defects found by Federal court to exist in section 3020-a of Education Law, establishing procedures for discipline of tenured teachers, they amended regulations to require that employing board of education be provided with copy of transcript of disciplinary proceedings and findings and recommendations of hearing panel and to further require that board's decision be based solely on record in proceedings before hearing panel and set forth reasons and factual basis for determination -- tenured teacher charged with using excessive physical force upon students may be suspended pending hearing and determination on charges, but must be paid during period of suspension -- since complaint in action by teachers and teachers' association, for declaratory judgment invalidating disciplinary proceedings against teachers, alleges no present or potential wrong to association as result of acts complained of, its action is dismissed.

1. After a Federal court declared that section 3020-a of the Education Law, which establishes procedures for the [***2] discipline of tenured teachers by the employing board of education, was unconstitutional in the absence of administrative regulations requiring that the board's decision be based upon evidence elicited before the hearing penal and that it set forth the reasons and factual basis for the decision, the New York State Board of Regents approved amendments to the regulations of the Commissioner of Education, which required that the board be provided with a copy of the transcript of the disciplinary proceedings and the findings and recommendations of the hearing panel, and further required that its decision be based solely upon the record in the proceedings before the hearing panel and set forth the reasons and the factual basis for its determination. In providing these additional regulations to overcome the constitutional defects found to exist in section 3020-a, the Regents and the Commissioner were acting within their lawfully delegated authority and giving effect to the general policy and underlying intent of the Legislature when it enacted that section. The regulations do not conflict with the specific direction of the section which gives the Commissioner the power to establish necessary [***3] rules and procedures "for the conduct of hearings", without expressly granting him power to supply "due process" procedural safeguards in the post-hearing stages, but, rather, they supplement and carry out the legislative scheme of which that specific direction is a part.

2. A tenured teacher charged with using unwarranted and excessive physical force upon students may be suspended and removed from his teaching duties pending a hearing and determination on the charges, but must be paid his regular salary during the period of suspension.

3. Since the complaint in an action by teachers and their teachers' association, for a declaratory judgment invalidating disciplinary proceedings brought against the teachers, alleges no present or potential wrong to the association as a result of the acts complained of, its action is dismissed.

 

1466 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Velazquez


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


77 Misc. 2d 749; 354 N.Y.S.2d 975; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1237



April 24, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the foregoing reasons, the loitering charge is dismissed and the motion to suppress the seized contraband is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss a loitering charge on the grounds that N.Y. Penal Law § 240.35(8) was unconstitutional and a motion to suppress contraband seized when he was arrested.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in the men's room of the suburban concourse of at a bus terminal and charged with loitering in a transportation facility in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 240.35(8). During defendant's arrest, he was searched and methadone, a controlled substance, was found in his coat pocket. Defendant was then also charged with criminal possession of a controlled substance in the seventh degree. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the loitering charge and a motion to suppress the seized contraband. The court found that the absence of any ascertainable standards governing arrest and conviction rendered fair, even-handed administration of the law a virtual impossibility. The court determined that loitering was a word in common usage whose meaning was well understood, however, it concluded that the word was never designed or intended to render innocent conduct criminal. The court held that the loitering statute was unconstitutionally vague on its face and as applied.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motions to dismiss the loitering charge and to suppress the seized contraband.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- loitering -- "loitering * * * in any transportation facility * * * and * * * unable to give a satisfactory explanation" (Penal Law, § 240.35, subd. 8), too vague and therefore unconstitutional and void; charge dismissed -- since such arrest was unlawful, incidental search was unlawful -- hence, methadone found in defendant's pocket is suppressed.

Defendant was arrested by a Port Authority police officer, in the men's room of one of the concourses of the Port Authority bus terminal in Manhattan, apparently on the ground that he was not using the facilities. The charge is dismissed, since the provision of the Penal Law ( § 240.35, subd. 8) making it unlawful for a person to loiter in a "transportation facility" when "unable to give a satisfactory explanation of his presence" is too vague and hence is unconstitutional and void. It follows that the arrest was unlawful and that the incidental search of defendant's person was likewise unlawful and that therefore the methadone (a "controlled substance") found in his pocket must be suppressed from [***2] evidence.

 

1467 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Jamaica Sav. Bank v. Toomey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


77 Misc. 2d 887; 355 N.Y.S.2d 268; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1265



April 23, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion is granted but only to the extent that the entire report of the referee appointed to ascertain and compute the amount due plaintiff for principal and interest on the bonds, mortgages and extension agreement is confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee made a motion to confirm the referee's report only as to the amount found due from the mortgagor for principal on the bonds, mortgages, and extension agreement and to disaffirm the computation of interest at the rate of six percent. The mortgagee also sought a declaration that N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5004, which set a fixed rate of six percent interest on judgments, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee filed an action to foreclose a mortgage on real property. The referee determined the amount due for principal and computed interest due at the rate of six percent as provided in Rule 5004. The mortgagee contended that it was entitled to a higher rate of interest computed under N.Y. Gen. Oblig. Law § 5-501. The court confirmed the referee's entire report including the six-percent rate of interest. The court noted that the six-percent rate of interest specified in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5004 applied not only to judgment interest, but also to all accruals of interest pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5001, 5002, 5003. The referee properly applied the statutory rate of six percent set by N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5004 in computing the interest due to the mortgagee on the bonds, mortgages, and extension agreement. Regarding the mortgagee's claim that Rule 5004 was unconstitutional, the court held that the award of interest for the period following a breach of contract was merely an element of damages. A change in the availability of interest was not an impairment of the obligation of a contract. The award of interest at the rate provided in Rule 5004 was not in derogation of the mortgagee's rights.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to confirm but only to the extent that the referee's entire report, which ascertained and computed the amount due the mortgagee for principal and interest on the mortgagor's bonds, mortgages, and extension agreement, was confirmed.


HEADNOTES

Interest -- computation of interest -- following default on mortgage of real property, interest is computed at 6% as provided in CPLR 5004, since CPLR 5004 evidences Legislature's intent to set fixed rate on judgments independent of provisions of section 5-501 of General Obligations Law -- application of CPLR 5004 does not unconstitutionally deprive plaintiff of its rights without due process.

1. In an action to foreclose a mortgage, the report of the referee computing interest on the default at a rate of 6% as provided in CPLR 5004 is confirmed. Plaintiff is not entitled to a higher rate of interest computed pursuant to section 5-501 of the General Obligations Law, since the Legislature, in CPLR 5004, has evidenced its intention to set a fixed rate of interest on judgments independent of the provisions of the General Obligations Law. Inasmuch as the rate of interest following default of the mortgage obligation is to be computed [***2] at the rate then prescribed by statute, 6% as set by CPLR 5004 is to be applied in computing interest due plaintiff on the bonds, mortgages and extension agreement.

2. Since the award of interest for the period following a breach of contract is merely an element of damages, a change in the availability of interest is not an impairment of the obligation of a contract, and therefore the application of CPLR 5004 to the award of interest does not unconstitutionally deprive plaintiff of its rights without due process of law.

People v. Robinson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Queens County


77 Misc. 2d 1081; 354 N.Y.S.2d 868; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1306



April 23, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For all of these reasons, the motion herein for a preliminary hearing is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for a preliminary hearing on a prosecutor's misdemeanor information charging defendant with criminal trespass and petty larceny.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's request for a preliminary hearing, prosecution argued that defendant was not entitled to a preliminary hearing because the information was filed against defendant on the directive of a grand jury. However, the court disagreed and granted defendant's motion for a preliminary hearing. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that N.Y. Crim. Proc. law §§ 190.70(1) and 170.5 mandated a hearing on an information, even when the information was issued pursuant to a grand jury's direction. The court acknowledged that one case had interpreted the state law differently. However, the court held that the case improperly applied a rule of statutory construction and erred in its application of the law. The court held that the statutory sections dealing with preliminary hearings were reasonable and constitutionally valid and thus their unambiguous language was to be given full effect.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion for a preliminary hearing on the information charging defendant with criminal trespass and petty larceny.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- preliminary hearing -- when Grand Jury directs District Attorney to file misdemeanor information in New York City Criminal Court, defendant is entitled to preliminary hearing.

When a Grand Jury, instead of indicting an accused for a felony, directs the District Attorney to file a prosecutor's information in the New York City Criminal Court, charging a misdemeanor or misdemeanors, the defendant is entitled to a preliminary hearing ( CPL 190.70, subd. 1; CPL 170.75).

 

1469 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Buffalo


77 Misc. 2d 889; 355 N.Y.S.2d 266; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1266



April 22, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The information against the defendant herein is accordingly dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was a motion brought by defendant under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 170.30(1)(a), 170.35 (1)(c) for dismissal of the information against her, wherein she was charged with violating N.Y. Penal Law § 130.38.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating § 130.38, which provided that a person was guilty of consensual sodomy when he or she engaged in certain deviate sexual intercourse with another person. The statute prohibited such conduct between unmarried persons. The court dismissed the information against defendant. The court held that § 130.38 and, to the extent therein incorporated by reference, N.Y. Penal Law § 130.00(2) were unconstitutional. The court stated that § 130.38 denied equal protection of the law to citizens not married to each other, in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11. The court further stated that § 130.38 would make criminals of some citizens, but not others, on the basis of an unsupportable distinction and would constitutionally wrongfully deny to the former the equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the information against defendant.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- consensual sodomy -- section 130.38 of Penal Law, and to extent section 130.00 of Penal Law is incorporated therein by reference, unconstitutionally denies equal protection to persons not married to each other, since section 130.38 states that person is guilty of consensual sodomy when he engages in deviate sexual intercourse with another person and section 130.00 defines deviate sexual intercourse as pertaining only to persons not married to each other.

Charged with violating section 130.38 of the Penal Law for consensual sodomy, the information against defendant is dismissed. Section 130.38 states that a person is guilty of consensual sodomy when he engages in deviate sexual intercourse with another person, and section 130.00 of the Penal Law, which defines deviate sexual intercourse, pertains only to persons not married to each other. Therefore, section 130.38, and to the extent section 130.00 is incorporated therein by reference, denies equal protection of the law to citizens not married to each other, in violation of the equal protection clauses of both State and Federal Constitutions.  [***2] Since all persons are free to engage in "ordinary" sexual intercourse as defined in subdivision 1 of section 130.00 of the Penal Law, there is no logical basis on which the status of marriage between the participants should make the difference between right and wrong in the engaging in one mode of sexual intercourse rather than another.

 

1470 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Starks


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


78 Misc. 2d 87; 355 N.Y.S.2d 906; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1335



April 17, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Based upon the foregoing, this court finds that section 70.06 of the Penal Law is constitutional and denies defendant's application to declare the same illegal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of grand larceny in the second degree, criminal possession of stolen property in the first degree, unauthorized use of a vehicle, and N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 509. He filed an application seeking a declaration that N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06, the felony offender statute, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The people filed a felony offender statement, which alleged that defendant had been convicted of robbery and sentenced to the state reformatory. Defendant admitted the validity of the prior conviction but claimed that § 70.06 violated his constitutional rights. He argued that it discriminated against prior offenders, violated the due process laws of the constitution, violated the ex post facto doctrine of the United States Constitution, and imposed a cruel and inhuman punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment. The court held that § 70.06 was constitutional. It did not impose additional punishment for a past crime. Defendant had been convicted of robbery and sentence passed. That sentence would not be affected by § 70.06 in any manner. Section 70.06 did not apply ex post facto sanctions in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 9. Defendant advanced no legal grounds to show in what respect § 70.06 imposed a sentence of excessive length or severity.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application to declare the felony offender statute unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- sentence -- second felony offender -- after being indicted for present crimes, defendant because of prior felony conviction in 1971 became subject to second felony offender provisions of section 70.06 of Penal Law imposing mandatory sentences of imprisonment -- section 70.06 is constitutional; it does not violate due process, or ex post facto sanctions of Constitution, or constitute cruel and inhuman punishment.

1. The defendant was indicted on charges of grand larceny, criminal possession of stolen property and unauthorized use of a vehicle. Because the defendant was convicted of robbery in 1971, he became subject to the second felony offender provisions of section 70.06 of the Penal Law, which imposes mandatory sentences of imprisonment. The statute does not violate due process as it applies equally to a class of persons convicted and sentenced to the penitentiary. The statute does no more than describe circumstances under which increased punishment may be imposed.

2. The statute does not impose [***2] additional punishment for a past crime in violation of the ex post facto sanctions of the Constitution. If the defendant receives increased punishment, it is as a result of his present crimes and does not add one additional day to his prior sentence.

3. Increased punishment by itself does not constitute cruel and inhuman punishment. The defendant has advanced no legal grounds to show in what respect the present statute imposes a sentence of excessive length or severity.

4. Section 70.06 of the Penal Law is constitutional.

 

1471 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gaines


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Kings County


77 Misc. 2d 736; 354 N.Y.S.2d 843; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1232



April 15, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned the court to set aside a notice of alibi served upon him by the State under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20, and requested that he be permitted to present alibi testimony at the trial notwithstanding his failure to provide the prosecution with the names of prospective alibi witnesses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant wanted to present alibi testimony at the trial notwithstanding his failure to provide the prosecution with the names of prospective alibi witnesses. Defendant alleged that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20 was unconstitutionality because it lacked a reciprocity requirement by the state. The court agreed that there was no significant difference between § 250.20, New York's former law set forth in Code of Criminal Procedure § 295-l, and the notice-of-alibi statute of the State of Oregon. Both the New York former law and the Oregon statute had been held to be unconstitutional. Therefore, the court held that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20 was unconstitutional. The notice of alibi served upon defendant by the State upon his arraignment was set aside. The defendant was permitted to offer an alibi defense at the trial despite his failure to serve the notice called for by § 250.20.


OUTCOME: The court set-aside the notice of alibi served upon defendant by the State upon his arraignment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- alibi -- notice-of-alibi statute, CPL 250.20, is unconstitutional since it is substantially similar to its predecessor, section 255-l of Code of Criminal Procedure, which Court of Appeals held unconstitutional in People v. Bush (33 N Y 2d 921) -- cases reaching opposite conclusion are of no consequence since they were decided before Bush, which refrained from suggesting that alibi rule may be adapted by case law to meet constitutional standards.

1. Defendant's petition to set aside a notice of alibi served upon him by the People under CPL 250.20, and his request that he be permitted to present alibi testimony at trial notwithstanding his failure to provide the prosecution with the names of his prospective alibi witness, is granted. CPL 250.20 is unconstitutional since it is substantially similar to its predecessor, section 255-l of the Code of Criminal Procedure, which the Court of Appeals held unconstitutional in People v. Bush (33 N Y 2d 921). The Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment forbids enforcement of alibi witness rules unless reciprocal discovery rights are given to criminal defendants, since it is fundamentally unfair to require a defendant [***2] to divulge the details of his own case while at the same time subjecting him to the hazards of surprise concerning refutation of the very pieces of evidence which he disclosed to the State.

2. Cases reaching an opposite conclusion regarding the constitutionality of CPL 250.20 are of no consequence since they were decided before Bush, which refrained from suggesting that the alibi rule may be adapted by case law to meet constitutional standards, but simply declared it unconstitutional.

Carey Transp., Inc. v. Triborough Bridge & Tunnel Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


77 Misc. 2d 671; 355 N.Y.S.2d 60; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1215



April 10, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court considered plaintiff bus company's cause of action against defendant bridge and tunnel authority seeking a declaration that the authority's refusal to grant it the same lower rate that it granted to other public transportation buses was arbitrary and capricious.


OVERVIEW: The bus company had a franchise from the city to operate three airport-related routes. The authority granted a lower rate to buses engaged in authorized general transportation and specifically excluded airline buses or other special purpose buses using franchised routes from the lower rate. The court granted declaratory and injunctive relief in favor of the bus company. The court noted that the different tolls had to be based upon some real and substantial distinction bearing a reasonable and just relation to the imposed classification. The court concluded that the bus company was engaged in general transportation and that the authority could not reasonably distinguish between buses with regular bus stop routes and buses working airline routes in fixing the toll classifications.


OUTCOME: The court entered a judgment granting the bus company declaratory and injunctive relief against the authority regarding the imposition of bridge and tunnel tolls.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Public authorities -- toll rates -- Triborough Bridge and Tunnel Authority cannot charge higher toll for two-axle airline buses than for two-axle general transportation buses (21 NYCRR 251.1).

The Triborough Bridge and Tunnel Authority operates a number of bridges and tunnels, including the Bronx-Whitestone Bridge, the Verrazano-Narrows Bridge, and the Queens-Midtown Tunnel; and it has legislative authority to impose tolls and make rules and regulations for the use of its facilities (Public Authorities Law, art. 3); but, since no guidelines or standards are specified in the statute, reasonableness is the standard. It is unreasonable of the Authority to charge a higher toll for two-axle franchised airline buses than for two-axle franchised general transportation buses (cf. 21 NYCRR 251.1). Judgment is granted to a franchised airline bus corporation enjoining and restraining the Authority from charging it the higher rate.

Neville v. Bronstein


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


77 Misc. 2d 716; 354 N.Y.S.2d 567; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1225



April 9, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, as petitioners are not within the statutory definition of "time of war" (Civil Service Law, § 85, subd. 1, par. [c]) and inasmuch as it was within the power of the New York State Legislature to set forth the limitation complained of herein (supra) the application is denied and the petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner veterans filed an application seeking to annul and vacate a judgment of respondents, Director of the Department of Personnel and Chairman of the Civil Service Commission of the City of New York, denying them veterans' preference credits.


OVERVIEW: The veterans all held the rank of Lieutenant in the New York City Fire Department and passed an examination for promotion to the rank of Captain. They sought veteran's examination credits pursuant to N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6 by reason of their status as honorably discharged veterans of the armed forces of the United States between 1953 and 1957. However, pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 85(1)(c), military service between July 28, 1953 and December 31, 1962 did not constitute service in "time of war." The veterans argued that the civil service definition of "time of war" was unconstitutional because it conflicted with the definition of "time of war" set forth by the United States Congress. The court held that the New York Legislature's power to pass laws for the enforcement of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 6, including the power to fix the time of beginning and ending of actual combat for purposes of veterans' preferences, was not superseded by Congress.


OUTCOME: The court denied the veterans' application and dismissed the petition for veterans' examination credits.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- veteran's examination credits -- veteran's examination credits denied to petitioners who served in armed forces between September 17, 1953 and September 9, 1957 since they are not within statutory definition of "time of war" (Civil Service Law, § 85, subd. 1, par. [c], cls. [3], [4]); section is not unconstitutional since Congress' constitutional power to declare war does not pre-empt Legislature's enforcement of veteran's preference amendment of State Constitution.

Petitioners took and passed an examination for promotion to the rank of Captain in the Fire Department, each of them claiming veteran's examination credits, pursuant to section 6 of article V of the New York State Constitution by reason of their status as honorably discharged veterans of the armed forces of the United States during a "time of war". Petitioners were in [***2] full time, active duty in the armed forces between September 17, 1953 and September 9, 1957. Pursuant to section 85 (subd. 1, par. [c], cls. [3], [4]) of the Civil Service Law, military service during this period does not constitute service in time of war. Petitioners' application for a judgment vacating and annulling respondents' determination not to grant veteran's preference credits, is denied. Petitioners are not within the statutory definition of time of war, and section 85 of the Civil Service Law is not unconstitutional since Congress' constitutional power to declare war does not pre-empt or supersede the New York Legislature's enforcement of the veteran's preference amendment of the State Constitution.

 

1474 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


De Vito v. Aylward


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Jefferson County


77 Misc. 2d 524; 354 N.Y.S.2d 395; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1181



April 5, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner criminal defendant moved for an order under N.Y. C.P.L.R art. 78 to restrain respondents, a city judge, an acting city judge, and a district attorney, from proceeding to a jury trial on a charge of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: The criminal defendant had a jury trial pending in the city court on the charge of driving while intoxicated. The defendant argued, inter alia, that the city court lost jurisdiction of the action on the ground that she was denied her constitutional right to a speedy trial. The court denied the defendant's motion, holding that an adjournment of defendant's trial for 70 days was constitutionally permissible. Defendant's case could be adjourned to await the next jury panel provided that it was no longer than the 90 days allowed by statute. The court also found that N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 510(1) conferred upon the city judge the discretion to suspend a driver's license temporarily without notice pending the defendant's prosecution if his decision was based on substantial evidence. The city court acted with sound discretion because it had before it the narrative of the defendant's actions leading to the charge as well as the record of her prior convictions showing her recent and persistent disregard for the traffic laws of the state.


OUTCOME: The court denied the criminal defendant's motion to restrain respondents from proceeding to a jury trial on a charge of driving while intoxicated.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Motor vehicles -- driving while intoxicated -- right to speedy trial -- petitioner, who was arrested on charge of driving while intoxicated and who demanded speedy jury trial, was not deprived of her constitutional right to speedy trial by adjournment of her case for 70 days, until date when next jury was to be impanelled -- court acted with sound discretion when it temporarily suspended her license pending trial -- record of all her convictions, supplied by Motor Vehicle Department, was in file of her case in court, but, since Judge has sworn he did not see it, and since he will not be trying facts, there has been no violation of right accorded her by statutory prohibition against exhibition prior to conviction of "record of convictions stub" of license.

1. A petitioner who, 12 hours after the release of a panel of jurors who had tried cases in City Court, was arrested on a charge of driving while intoxicated. and who demanded a speedy jury trial, was not deprived of her constitutional right to a speedy trial when that court adjourned her case for 70 days, until the date when the next jury was to be impanelled.

2. The court, which had before it not only the narrative of [***2] petitioner's actions leading to the charge but the record of her prior convictions in the same court, showing recent and persistent disregard for the traffic laws, and which had discretion, under the Vehicle and Traffic Law ( § 510), to temporarily suspend her driver's license pending the trial, acted with sound discretion when it did so.

3. In addition to the record of her convictions in City Court, which the Judge admittedly inspected, the file of the case in that court contained a longer record of all her convictions, supplied by the State Motor Vehicle Department, and, on the assumption that the Judge also inspected that record, she claims a violation of the right accorded her by section 504 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, prohibiting exhibition prior to conviction of the "record of convictions stub" of a license. Since the purpose of that prohibition is to insure a fair hearing on a particular charge unprejudiced by past convictions, it would be sophistry to attempt a distinction between the Judge's seeing the forbidden stub and his seeing the Motor Vehicle Department's copy of the record of convictions. However, there has been no violation of petitioner's right since the Judge [***3] has sworn he did not see the departmental copy, and, even if he did see it, there would be no prejudice to her because a jury, not the Judge, will be trying the facts.

 

1475 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sanders


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, Bronx County


78 Misc. 2d 205; 356 N.Y.S.2d 421; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1360



April 4, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to preclude the People of the State of New York from using information obtained from defendant's alibi witnesses, to purge such information from the district attorney's file, to have another district attorney assigned to the case, to prohibit the relieved assistant from discussing the case, and to compel the People to turn over all copies and records of statements made by defendant's alibi witnesses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to prohibit the introduction, for impeachment purposes, of prior inconsistent statements of his alibi witnesses based on the holding that New York's notice-of-alibi statute, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20, was unconstitutional. The court held that under such law, defendant could not be precluded from introducing alibi witnesses' testimony for failure to serve a "notice-of-alibi." However, the fact that the witness names and subsequent statements were obtained pursuant to § 250.20, prior to the declaration if its unconstitutionality, did not render the statements inadmissible for impeachment purposes.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion in all respects, with the exception that the court directed the district attorney to furnish a copy to defense counsel of any statements obtained from defendant's alibi witnesses.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- alibi -- information from alibi witnesses, unconstitutionally obtained pursuant to CPL 250.20 prior to declaration of unconstitutionality, is available for impeachment purposes.

Information obtained from alibi witnesses by the District Attorney pursuant to the notice-of-alibi statute ( CPL 250.20) is not suppressible where obtained in good faith just prior to the declaration of the statute's unconstitutionality. While the defendant cannot be precluded from introducing testimony of alibi witnesses for failure to serve a "notice of alibi", unconstitutionally obtained information may be utilized by the District Attorney for impeachment purposes. Accordingly, a motion by defendant for orders precluding the People from using such information is denied, except that defense counsel shall receive a copy of any statement obtained by the District Attorney from witnesses whose names were supplied by defense counsel pursuant to CPL 250.20.

 

1476 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ciulla v. Lavine


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County


79 Misc. 2d 297; 360 N.Y.S.2d 152; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1650



April 3, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent social services commissioner made objections in point of law, arguing that an action by petitioners, recipients of public assistance, to review his determination in fixing the schedule of heating allowances did not state a cause of action and should be dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner argued that the petition filed by the recipients of public assistance contesting his schedule of heating allowances did not state a cause of action and should be dismissed. The court held that the petition did state a claim because it could be inferred from the allegations that the heating allowances, as fixed, bore no reasonable relationship to the need for or cost of fuel. The determination of the level of public assistance was ordinarily a legislative matter not subject to review by the courts. However, the legislature could not delegate its legislative powers. To avoid the constitutional prohibition against a pure delegation of legislative power, there must be standards set which the commissioner must follow. The commissioner's discretionary power to fix the amounts of the fuel allowances had to be exercised reasonably and had to bear a reasonable relationship to the cost of and the need for fuel.


OUTCOME: The court held that the recipients' petition stated a cause of action for review of the determination of the commissioner fixing the schedule of heating allowances.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Social services -- fuel allowances -- in proceeding brought to review determination of Commissioner of Social Services in fixing schedule of fuel allowances allotted to recipients of public assistance pursuant to department regulations (18 NYCRR 352.5), petition states cause of action -- petitioners need not exhaust their administrative remedies -- petitioners are entitled to examination before trial of employees under supervision of commissioner.

1. In a proceeding brought to review the determination of the Commissioner of Social Services in fixing the schedule of fuel allowances allotted to recipients of public assistance pursuant to department regulations (18 NYCRR 352.5), the petition, alleging that the heating allowances, as fixed, bear no reasonable relationship to the need for, and cost of fuel, states a cause of action. Although, the commissioner is delegated discretionary power to fix the amounts of fuel allowances, this power must be exercised reasonably and not arbitrarily. Since the discretionary power granted to the commissioner is not unbridled, the exercise of that power is subject to review by the courts to determine if it has been exercised within the standards [***2] imposed or implied.

2. The petitioners need not exhaust their administrative remedies by way of a fair hearing since those procedures are not equivalent to the remedies here sought.

3. Petitioners are entitled to an examination before trial of certain employees who are under the supervision of the commissioner.

 

1477 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Cathedral Academy v. State


Claim No. 56557


Court of Claims of New York


77 Misc. 2d 977; 354 N.Y.S.2d 370; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1282



April 2, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, claimant's motion for summary judgment is denied and the defendant's motion for dismissal of this claim is granted.

This decision is not intended to affect any claim or claims which have been filed with the court pursuant to chapter 996 by any nonchurch, nonreligious or nonsectarian nonpublic schools.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state moved for summary judgment against claimant school's action seeking reimbursement for educational services it provided under state law.


OVERVIEW: The school, which was affiliated with a religious institution, provided certain educational services pursuant to N.Y. Laws ch. 138 (1970). Subsequently, ch. 996 was found unconstitutional because it violated the Establishment Clause. The school nonetheless filed a claim under N.Y. Laws ch. 996 (1972) for expenses it incurred in providing the services. The school argued that, because the services it provided had been prior to the finding that N.Y. Laws ch. 138 was unconstitutional, it was entitled to reimbursement of expenses. However, the court held that the school was not entitled to recover expenses from the state for the services it rendered. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that ch. 996 was unconstitutional to the extent that it provided for the payment for ch. 138-related educational services performed by a religiously affiliated institution such as the school. The court held that the caselaw upon which the school relied in arguing for payment was distinguishable from the case at issue because, in the case cited by the school, there were certain protections that assured that the services rendered did not further any sectarian purpose.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion for summary judgment against the school's action seeking reimbursement for educational services it provided.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- State aid to parochial schools -- despite express legislative authorization (L. 1972, ch. 996), Court of Claims cannot entertain claims by parochial schools for State aid (U. S. Const., 1st Amdt.); such claim is dismissed.

The Legislature authorized payments by the State to nonprofit nonpublic schools, for various school-related services (L. 1970, ch. 138). The Federal courts enjoined any such payments to parochial or sectarian schools, and the United States Supreme Court affirmed such Federal determination ( Levitt v. Committee for Public Educ., 413 U.S. 472). The Legislature nevertheless authorized the Court of Claims to hear and determine, as moral obligations, claims for payments for such school-related services already rendered (L. 1972, ch. 996). But the religious establishment clause of the First Amendment of the United [***2] States Constitution prohibits any such claim. Accordingly, this claim against the State by a parochial school is dismissed.

 

1478 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rochester Poster Advertising Co. v. Brighton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County


78 Misc. 2d 446; 357 N.Y.S.2d 346; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1423



April 1, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff advertising company moved for declaratory judgment against defendant town in an action to declare Brighton, N.Y. Zoning Ordinance § 42-29 unconstitutional because it required the company to give up nonconforming billboards without due process of the law and without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The company leased premises for billboards. The town enacted of sign and zoning ordinances including Brighton, N.Y. Zoning Ordinance § 42-29. Under the ordinances the company's signs were nonconforming. The court found that the outdoor advertising structures as well as the lease of the lands upon which the structures were erected were an interest in real estate. The signs in question possessed considerable value. Thus, the court concluded that the sign and zoning ordinances in respect to the subject signs in this case were unconstitutional pursuant to the Constitution of the State of New York as well as the Constitution of the United States by reason of the taking property of the company without due process of the law and without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court granted the advertising company's motion for declaratory and declared the town's zoning ordinances unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- plaintiff is entitled to judgment declaring that town's ordinances, requiring removal of pre-existing, nonconforming signs, within three-year amortization period, shorter than normal useful life of signs, unconstitutionally takes plaintiff's property -- under police power and in conjunction with aesthetic reasons, defendant may prohibit signs not in existence at time of enactment of its ordinances -- statutes of New York and United States do not pre-empt defendant's authority to enact zoning and sign ordinances.

1. The plaintiff is entitled to a judgment declaring that the defendant Town of Brighton's sign and zoning ordinances, requiring removal of pre-existing, nonconforming billboards within three years after the statutes' effective date, unconstitutionally take the plaintiff's property without due process of law and just compensation. The plaintiff's outdoor advertising structures and lease of lands are an interest in land which, if taken by eminent domain, would require compensation, and the effect of the ordinances technically constitutes a taking without just compensation by eliminating a right in real estate through an amortization [***2] period shorter than the normal useful life of the property.

2. Under its police power, the defendant town may, in conjunction with aesthetic reasons, properly prohibit signs not in existence at the time of enactment of its ordinances.

3. The authority of the defendant with respect to the sign and zoning ordinances has not been pre-empted by the statutes of the State of New York and the United States, since subdivision 9 of section 88 of the Highway Law authorizes more restrictive ordinances than contained in that statute.

 

1479 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Sullivan v. Grupposo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Civil Court of the City of New York, Special Term, Bronx County


77 Misc. 2d 833; 355 N.Y.S.2d 55; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1249



March 30, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The court finds that there are no triable issues of fact and accordingly, the defendant's answer is stricken and plaintiff is granted summary judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual filed a motion for summary judgment for the return of $ 1,200 against defendant Property Clerk of the Police Department of the City (Clerk).


OVERVIEW: The individual was arrested and indicted for three counts of possession of a stolen car, four counts of making and possessing forged driver's license and registration, one count of resisting arrest, one count of bribery, and one count of possession of burglar's tools. When he was taken to the police station, $ 1,200 in cash that was on his person found its way into the hands of the Clerk. The individual contended that the money was wrongfully taken from him and retained by the police. The Clerk maintained that these moneys were offered to a police officer as a bribe. The individual later pleaded guilty to the crime of possession of stolen property. The plea was accepted in consideration and dismissal of the nine remaining counts. Thereafter, the individual demanded the return of the $ 1,200, and upon the Clerk's refusal to pay, instituted a replevin action. The individual then filed a motion for summary judgment. The court granted the motion, by holding that the Clerk was required to return the money because such money was not contraband, as it was not shown that it was the "proceeds of a crime," and the entire indictment against the individual had been disposed of by plea.


OUTCOME: The court granted the individual's motion for summary judgment for the return of $ 1,200 against the Clerk. The court also struck the Clerk's answer to the individual's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Searches and seizures -- return of seized property -- action against Police Property Clerk for return of seized money -- where money belonging to plaintiff, held by Police Property Clerk, is not contraband, and indictment against plaintiff has been disposed of by plea, District Attorney has no need for and cannot use money as evidence; therefore, it must be returned -- since Police Property Clerk has not instituted forfeiture proceedings within 10 days from plaintiff's demand, defendant is guilty of laches and is estopped from asserting any defenses.

1. Plaintiff was arrested and taken to a police station. While there, $ 1,200 in cash belonging to him and on his person, found its way to defendant. Subsequently, plaintiff was indicted and charged with 10 crimes, to which he pleaded guilty to criminal possession of stolen property, which plea was accepted in consideration and dismissal of the nine remaining counts. Thereafter plaintiff demanded return of the $ 1,200 and upon defendant's refusal to pay, instituted a replevin [***2] action. Summary judgment is granted to plaintiff. A separate defense pleading section 435-4.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York is denied since McClendon v. Rosetti (460 F. 2d 111) held the statute unconstitutional as applied to persons from whose possession money has been taken, other than contraband, or if the money was related to any criminal proceeding, when such proceedings have been terminated. Here the money is not contraband since there are no evidentiary facts to prove it was the proceeds of a crime, and the entire indictment has been disposed of by plea, therefore it follows that the District Attorney has no need for and cannot use the money as evidence and it must be returned.

2. McClendon also declared subdivision f of section 435-4.0 of the Administrative Code unconstitutional because its effect is to place the burden of proving lawful title to the property withheld on the claimant. However, defendant had 10 days from plaintiff's demand to initiate a lawful forfeiture or other similar proceeding to seek to justify the State's continued detention of the money. Not having instituted such suit, the defendant is guilty of laches and is estopped [***3] from asserting any defense.

People v. J.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County

OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to dismiss his indictment, claiming that the alibi statute, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20, was unconstitutional. The court denied defendant's motion. The Court of Appeals had recently declared that the predecessor to the alibi statute, N.Y. Code of Crim. Proc. § 295-1, was unconstitutional. The issue was whether this ruling mandated a dismissal of defendant's indictment. The court found that because § 295-1 was unconstitutional, it did not necessarily mean N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20 was also unconstitutional, especially when was an order of reciprocal discovery. Until appellate courts rule, the court would continue to treat the statute as constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- alibi -- reciprocity -- reciprocal disclosure of alibi witnesses and alibi-refuting witnesses is constitutional.

An order directing the defendant and the People to disclose to each other the names and addresses of their respective alibi witnesses and alibi-refuting witnesses ( CPL art. 240; CPL 250.20) is valid and constitutional ( People v. Bush, 33 N Y 2d 921, examined).

 

1481 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. Syracuse


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County


78 Misc. 2d 124; 355 N.Y.S.2d 239; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1344



March 27, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] As harsh as it may be, the principle of damnum absque injuria prevails, and the complaints in each of the above-entitled actions are, accordingly, dismissed on the ground that they fail to state a cause of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of property or parties in interest (owners), brought actions against defendants, a city and its urban renewal agency (city), seeking compensation, because of "condemnation blight," for loss of income from their properties, depreciation in value, and additional costs incurred in protecting their property. The city made motions to dismiss the complaints because the complaints failed to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The owners' properties were within a designated urban renewal area. Over many years, the city acquired title to many parcels in the area and demolished or boarded up many buildings, resulting in "condemnation blight." As a result of the loss of income from their properties, depreciation of value, and additional costs incurred, the owners contended that the city's actions amounted to a constitutional deprivation of due process and equal protection of the laws pursuant to the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments. Ruling that the complaints failed to state a cause of action, the court dismissed the complaints. The court pointed out that the owners were not claiming that the city took their property by de jure or de facto condemnation. The court found that "condemnation blight" related to the impact of certain acts upon the value of property and in no way imported a taking in the constitutional sense. It was not cause of action, but a rule of evidence of valuation of real property that had been the subject of a taking in condemnation, de jure, or de facto. The court concluded that the principle of damnum absque injuria prevailed.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motions to dismiss the owners' complaints on the ground that they failed to state a cause of action.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- damages for condemnation blight -- complaints of owners of property located within urban renewal area, whose property has not yet been condemned, but who seek damages from city and urban renewal agency for inordinately long and dilatory tactics on their part, with alleged result that area has suffered condemnation blight, are dismissed for failure to state cause of action -- alleged actions of city and agency do not amount to taking and, absent de jure or de facto taking, there is no deprivation of constitutional due process -- principle of damnum absque injuria prevails.

Owners of property located within an urban renewal area, whose property has not yet been condemned, although some of it has been designated for condemnation, seek damages from the city and its urban renewal agency, alleging that, as a result of inordinately long and dilatory tractics on the part of the latter, the area in which their property is located has suffered a condemnation [***2] blight, which has transformed it into one which is highly undesirable for either residential or commercial purposes, a high-crime area, in which vandalism is rampant, and from which both residential and commercial tenants have moved away; that they have lost substantial amounts of rental income, have been placed in a special insurance pool and forced to pay excessive premiums, have been compelled to expend moneys to protect their property from vandalism, and have suffered a drastic reduction in the value of their property, and that, by reason of the foregoing, they have been deprived of due process and equal protection of the laws. Their complaints are dismissed for failure to state a cause of action. The alleged actions on the part of the city and agency do not amount to a taking, and, absent a de jure or de facto taking, there is no deprivation of constitutional due process. The principle of damnum absque injuria prevails.
