People v. Ebasco Services, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


77 Misc. 2d 784; 354 N.Y.S.2d 807; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1241



March 26, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Four defendants charged with criminally negligent homicide by the State moved to inspect the grand jury minutes and dismiss the indictment on various grounds in a case concerned with whether or not a corporation could be convicted of homicide under the revised Penal Law.


OVERVIEW: The indictment charged defendants with failing to properly construct and supervise construction of a cofferdam, and by failing to perceive a substantial and unjustifiable risk of death, in a manner which constituted a gross deviation from the standard of care that a reasonable person would observe. The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the indictment and held that the indictment was defective within the meaning of N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 200.50(7). A failure to particularize sufficiently the facts constituting the alleged crime as required by the statute required a dismissal of the indictments underN.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 210.20(1)(a) and 210.25(1). There was insufficient compliance by the State with the statute. The sparse factual allegations contained in this indictment were supplemented merely by the statutory definition of criminally negligent homicide. Each defendant was entitled to know from the face of the indictment what facts were being pleaded against that particular defendant individually. The State was, however, granted leave to resubmit this case.It was apparent from N.Y. Penal Law § 10.00(7) that the term "person" included corporations.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion and dismissed the State's indictment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- homicide by corporation -- corporations may be indicted for criminally negligent homicide -- however, indictment is dismissed for insufficiency of factual allegations.

1. Corporations may be validly and constitutionally indicted for criminally negligent homicide (Penal Law, § 125.10; § 10.00, subd. 7).

2. However, the indictment is dismissed, since it does not allege sufficient "facts supporting every element of the offense charged" ( CPL 200.50, subd. 7; 210.20, subd. 1, par. [a]; 210.25, subd. 1) and since such a defect cannot be remedied by an amendment supplied merely by the District Attorney ( CPL 200.70, subd. 2, par. [b]). However, the District Attorney may resubmit the case to a Grand Jury ( CPL 210.45, subd. 9).

 

1483 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Eisen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


77 Misc. 2d 1044; 353 N.Y.S.2d 886; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1297



March 21, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that subdivision (a) of section 153.19 of the New York City Health Code is unconstitutional, is denied. The defendant's motion to dismiss for failure of the People to establish the guilt of the defendant beyond a reasonable doubt is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At the end of defendant's trial for violating New York City, N.Y., Health Code § 153.19(a), defendant filed a motion to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that the statute was overly broad and vague, and in violation of the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. Defendant also filed a motion to dismiss for failure to establish guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: The patrolman testified that he observed great accumulations of debris, litter, and garbage on the sidewalk abutting the property owned by defendant, but conceded that he did not observe defendant actually contribute to the accumulation. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that New York City, N.Y., Health Code § 153.19(a) was unconstitutional. The court held that § 153.19(a) was constitutional. The city had the power to adopt the statute under N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 10 and the city's police power. The statute was not overly broad and vague because it was capable of reasonable application to the varying fact patterns presented in the city. A periodic policing by defendant to keep his premises free from litter, garbage, and obstructions was not oppressive but a duty incident to property ownership. Defendant's duty to make a reasonable effort to maintain his premises free from litter was one incident to ownership. Defendant's continuous duty, as a property owner, to maintain the sidewalks abutting his premises free from litter and obstructions was not so unreasonable and onerous that it violated the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss for failure of to establish guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found defendant guilty as charged.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- littering -- property owner is found guilty of permitting litter and garbage on sidewalk; New York City Health Code (§ 153.19, subd. [a]) constitutional.

The New York City Health Code (§ 153.19, subd. [a]) validly and constitutionally requires that property owners shall, under penalty of misdemeanor, keep their abutting sidewalks "clean and free from garbage, refuse, rubbish, litter, or other offensive matter". This regulation is a reasonable exercise of the police power. Its wording is sufficiently precise. There is no proof of invidious discrimination in its enforcement. Defendant is found guilty.

 

1484 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Queens County


77 Misc. 2d 228; 354 N.Y.S.2d 85; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1112



March 19, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant's motion to dismiss is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought a motion to dismiss an information charging defendant with possession of a blank cartridge pistol, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 270.00, on the ground that the statute in question was unconstitutionally vague and upon the further ground that the statute necessarily implied the intent to use the pistol unlawfully was an element of the crime, a fact not charged by plaintiff prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Information charging defendant with possession of a blank cartridge pistol under N.Y. Penal Law § 270.00 was not subject to dismissal because charging statute clearly prohibited mere possession and did not make an intent to use the pistol unlawfully an element of the crime. Defendant was charged with unlawfully dealing with fireworks due to his possession of a blank cartridge pistol. Defendant brought a motion to dismiss the information on grounds the charging statute was vague and required the intent to use the pistol unlawfully, a fact which plaintiff prosecution failed to allege. The trial court denied the motion, holding where the statute specifically prohibited the mere possession of a cartridge pistol, the statute was clear. Where the statute did not state intent was an element of the crime and where another statute punishing the intent to unlawfully use a cartridge pistol existed, intent was not an element of the crime. Therefore, dismissal was improper.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss an information charging defendant with criminal possession of a blank cartridge pistol where the statute was clear in prohibiting mere possession. Intent to use the pistol unlawfully was not an element of the crime where another statute prohibited intent. Therefore, dismissal was denied where defendant was found in possession of a blank cartridge pistol.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- unlawfully dealing with fireworks -- mere possession of blank cartridge pistol constitutes violation of section 270.00 of Penal Law, defining class B misdemeanor of unlawfully dealing with fireworks -- intent to use it unlawfully is not necessary element of crime, nor need there be showing of possession with intent to sell -- section is not unconstitutionally vague.

1. Mere possession of a blank cartridge pistol constitutes a violation of section 270.00 of the Penal Law, defining the class B misdemeanor of unlawfully dealing with fireworks. An intent to use it unlawfully is not a necessary element of the crime, nor need there be a showing of possession with intent to sell.

2. The section is not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1485 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Petition of Brookhaven


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


78 Misc. 2d 499; 354 N.Y.S.2d 794; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1433



March 19, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Claimant's motion for a new trial and ancillary relief is rendered academic by the instant determination and therefore denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a condemnation proceeding, petitioner town sought to acquire title to claimant tax deed owner's real property for drainage purposes.


OVERVIEW: The tax deed owner bid at a county tax sale and acquired a tax deed to two parcels consisting of one and seven acres respectively. Subsequently, the town sought to acquire the property for drainage purposes. The tax deed owner failed to prove his title and the court held that he could not be compensated for the property in the condemnation proceedings. The court ordered that upon completion of valuation hearings in the condemnation proceeding, the sum due from the town to the true owner, whoever and wherever he was, would be deposited with the county treasurer. The court denied the tax deed owner's motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court held that the tax deed owner did not have marketable title to the property and, therefore, could not receive compensation in the condemnation proceeding. The tax deed owner's motion for a new trial was denied.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- tax liens, tax sales and tax titles -- allegedly "omitted" property cannot be added to tax roll without notice to true owner or to unknown owner -- municipal corporation is not estopped by unauthorized acts of its officials -- presumption of regularity of tax deed refuted -- purported landowner cannot acquire better title by failing to pay his taxes and then buying in at tax sale -- such tax deed grantee does not have marketable title -- hence he is not entitled to any award in condemnation -- award shall be deposited for benefit of unknown true owner of property.

1. A tax sale deed by the Suffolk County Treasurer in 1953 conveyed, to a corporation owned by claimant individual, a parcel described as being 1 acre on the westerly side of an unused railroad spur, and a parcel described as being 7 acres on the easterly side of said railroad spur. Expert testimony shows that it is impossible to locate these alleged properties. In 1965 claimant presented to the town assessor a survey of a 10.24-acre parcel located on the westerly side of [***2] a county road which had replaced the abandoned railroad spur. The 7-acre parcel certainly cannot be part of these 10.24 acres, and there is no proof that the 1-acre parcel is. Moreover, there is no evidence as to who is the true owner or the unknown owner of the 10.24 acres.

2. Nevertheless, the County Board of Supervisors adopted a resolution canceling the 1965-1966 taxes on the 1-acre and 7-acre parcels, and assessing and levying a "compromise" tax of $ 133.81 for 1965-1966 on the 10.24-acre parcel, and assessing this tax against yet a different corporation owned by claimant individual. Since all taxes on the 1-acre and 7-acre parcel had already been paid to date, there was nothing to "compromise" and the resolution was unauthorized and invalid (Suffolk County Tax [L. 1920, ch. 311, as amd.], §§ 29, 30, 66, 76).

3. Moreover, the lack of any notice to the true or unknown owner of the 10.24 acres is a constitutional bar to adding the assertedly "omitted" 10.24 acres to the existing tax roll.

4. Possibly, the "omitted" 10.24 acres could have been added to the next year's tax roll, but only after notice of a hearing to the true owner (Real Property Tax Law, §§ 554, 550; Suffolk [***3] County Tax Act, § 32).

5. Claimant and his corporations deliberately failed to pay this so-called "compromise" tax; and thus, after a tax sale and lapse of the statutory three-year period, the County Treasurer in 1970 issued to claimant a tax sale deed of the 10.24 acres. The presumption of regularity is refuted by the facts; and the presumption never became conclusive (Suffolk County Tax Act, §§ 3, 53), since, only 10 months after the deed was recorded, the town acquired vested title by condemnation, for drainage purposes, to a tract of land which includes the 10.24 acres.

6. A landowner cannot, by means of a self-created tax delinquency, acquire a better title than he had before.

7. A municipal corporation is not estopped by the unauthorized acts of its officers, agents, or employees.

8. The asserted title of claimant or of any of his corporations to the 10.24 acres is invalid, or, at the very least, unmarketable. Hence they are not entitled to any award for the condemnation by the town.

9. After valuation hearings in the town's condemnation proceeding are fully completed, any award for the 10.24 acres shall be deposited with the County Treasurer for the benefit of the unknown [***4] true owner (Suffolk County Improvement Act [L. 1927, ch. 190, as amd. by L. 1939, ch. 276], §§ 18, 44, 45).

 

1486 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thompson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


77 Misc. 2d 700; 353 N.Y.S.2d 698; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1222



March 15, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence used to indict him on weapons charges on the grounds that the evidence was unconstitutionally seized by parole officers.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove a parolee to the parole office and was sitting in the car when parole officers requested to search it. Defendant agreed to the search and as he was leaving the car, he reached down for an attache. The officers drew their guns and took the case. The officers, upon patting down defendant, found loaded guns. Defendant was indicted for possession of the guns and moved to suppress them on the grounds that they were unconstitutionally seized. Defendant alleged the stop-and-frisk statute, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 140.50, did not apply to parole officers. The court denied defendant's motion to suppress. Based on the parolee's suspicious activities, the officers reasonably investigated the parolee and searched the car. The officers were justified in their limited frisk of defendant because they were fearful that he was armed. The statute did not explicitly preclude parole officers from conducting limited searches in the course of their duties.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to suppress because the weapons taken from defendant's belt were constitutionally seized. The parole officers' limited frisk of defendant was reasonable because they were fearful for their safety. The stop-and-frisk statute did not definitively preclude parole officers from conducting limited searches for weapons.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- unlawful search and seizure -- under circumstances of case, search of vehicle by parole officers was proper and incidental to investigation of possible parole violation -- evidence seized is admissible -- CPL 140.50 not intended to preclude law enforcement officers other than police officers from conducting limited "stop and frisk" searches.

1. During questioning of a parolee who had a large amount of cash, had told of an assassination attempt and was generally evasive, the parole officers noticed a conspicuous looking vehicle parked in front of the Department of Correctional Services with the defendant seated in it, and after investigation from other sources, determined that the vehicle was customarily used by the parolee and registered to his wife. Asked to identify the occupant, the parolee said that "if that fellow has any guns on him, I don't know anything about it." Upon approaching the vehicle and getting no response to questions from the defendant, the parole officers announced their intention to search the vehicle and after asking the defendant some questions, they searched the defendant and seized weapons and ammunition which the defendant was carrying [***2] both in his waist and in an attache case which was by his feet and which he had picked up when getting out of the car. Under the circumstances, there were reasonable grounds for an investigation as to whether parole was being violated, and a search of the vehicle was incidental to that investigation.

2. The belief of the parole officers that the defendant was armed, that their own safety was in danger, and their limited frisk of the defendant were all reasonable. Evidence obtained as a result of reasonable conduct is admissible and accordingly, the guns taken from the defendant's belt were constitutionally seized. The guns in the attache case are admissible as the result of a search incident to a lawful arrest.

3. CPL 140.50, the "stop and frisk" law, was not intended to preclude all law enforcement officers other than those denominated as police officers from conducting a limited search for weapons when, in the course of performing their lawful duties, they reasonably fear for their own safety.

 

1487 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ledgebrook Corp. v. Lefkowitz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


77 Misc. 2d 867; 354 N.Y.S.2d 318; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1259



March 12, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Summary judgment is granted defendant in accordance with this decision. Submit judgment on notice declaring the rights of the State of New York consistent herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, non-New York corporations engaged in condominium sale and construction outside New York, sought declaratory judgment concerning right to place advertisements in New York newspapers, pursuant to Martin Act, N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law 23-A § 352-e et seq., and other New York law; defendant attorney general argued advertisements were impermissible.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, non-New York corporations, placed advertisements in New York newspapers for sale of non New-York condominiums. Defendant New York attorney general held pursuant to Martin Act, N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law 23-A § 352-e et seq., and other New York law that such advertisements were impermissible, as property had not been registered nor prospectus provided as required for securities investment. Plaintiffs filed declaratory judgment action and defendant cross-claimed. Plaintiffs argued they were not required to file, as this was not public securities offering, but rather mere advertising for condominiums that plaintiff contended were not securities; plaintiff also argued that even if condominiums did fall under statute, statute was unconstitutional. Court noted that there had not been significant case law on this issue, but that defendant's decision was rational and should be affirmed, and as the statute protected the public, it was constitutional. Thus, court granted summary judgment for defendant.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment granted for defendant, as court held that defendant's analysis that advertisements for sale of condominium without registration of said securities was proscribed by the state's securities law was proper.


HEADNOTES

Condominiums -- advertisements for sale of condominiums -- Connecticut corporations engaged in construction and sale of condominiums situate in Connecticut, who placed advertisements for sale of condominiums in New York newspapers, must file prospectus with Attorney-General pursuant to section 352-e of General Business Law, since condominium offering is "security" within meaning of statute and statute applies to projects outside State -- advertising was "public offer" within section 352-e, and statute is not unconstitutional.

1. Plaintiffs, Connecticut corporations engaged in the construction and sale of condominiums situate in the State of Connecticut, placed advertisements for the sale of the condominium units in New York newspapers. The advertisements showed the three condominiums and included pictures, general descriptions, phone numbers, route directions and the following copy: "Priced from the high thirties"; and "This does not constitute an offer where an offer may not legally be made". In an action [***2] brought to determine the legality of, and for an interpretation of the applicability of article 23-A of the General Business Law, which regulates such advertisements, summary judgment dismissing the complaint is granted defendant. An offering plan or prospectus must be filed with the Attorney-General pursuant to section 352-e of the General Business Law, since a condominium offering is a "security" within the meaning of the statute, and it applies to projects outside the State. Section 352-e applies to all condominiums. It is not limited to where the owners have voluntarily subjected their properties under section 339-ee of the Real Property Law.

2. The advertising was a "public offer" (and not a "non-final offer") within the scope of section 352-e of the General Business Law, and such a statute and the regulations promulgated pursuant thereto are proper constitutional vehicles for protecting the general public of the State.

In re L.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, New York County


77 Misc. 2d 363; 353 N.Y.S.2d 317; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1139



February 26, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The natural mother of an infant opposed an extension of foster care for the infant as requested, and moved that the proceedings be dismissed outright because of laches and the child immediately discharged to her. The natural mother also requested that the court grant disclosure to her of the complete case record maintained by the agency overseeing foster care.


OVERVIEW: The natural mother of an infant opposed an extension of foster care for the infant, moving that the proceedings be dismissed outright because of laches. The court denied the motion to dismiss and held that the doctrine of laches did not apply when the best interests of the child were at stake. The court held that the interests of a child existed independently of those of its parents and overrode them. The court held that although N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 392 had legislative gaps, the court could fill in those gaps by applying the Family Court Act. The court granted the natural mother's motion which requested inspection of the case record. The court found that the foster care agency granted a waiver in submitting its application for review, and the filing of the written petition by the commissioner was an act of waiver on his part.


OUTCOME: The court denied the natural mother's motion to dismiss the foster care proceedings, but granted her motion to review the case record.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Infants -- foster care status -- periodic review by Family Court of foster care status of child is constitutional (Social Services Law, § 392; Family Ct. Act, § 165) -- Family Court directs child care agency to disclose its case record concerning this child, to counsel, under carefully limited conditions (cf. Social Services Law, § 372, subd. 4) -- natural mother who has phobia of travel may apply for modest grant for transportation to courthouse.

1. A month-old infant was voluntarily committed to the care of the local Commissioner of Social Services by her biological mother, who could not care for her because of severe physical and emotional problems. Under the supervision of a child care agency, the infant, who is now eight years old, has been with the same foster parents and apparently is well adjusted. Pursuant to section 392 of the Social Services Law, the local Commissioner of Social Services at the behest of the child care agency has filed a petition in the Family Court for a periodic review of the foster care status and placement. Notice has been given to the natural mother, and she opposes any extension of the foster care placement and asks that her child be [***2] returned to her.

2. Section 392 of the Social Services Law, when read with section 358-a of the Social Services Law and section 165 of the Family Court Act, is constitutional.

3. The Family Court directs the child care agency to disclose its case record concerning this child, under the following conditions (cf. Social Services Law, § 372, subd. 4, and Family Ct. Act, § 166). The case record shall be delivered to the Clerk of this court under seal, to be kept in his exclusive custody. Counsel for both parties may arrange for inspection thereof either jointly or, upon their written stipulation, individually. The Clerk shall make same available under court auspices only. No extracts or copies may be made from the record, nor may the contents thereof be disclosed to the respective litigants. The court intends that counsel examine same in order to enable them to represent their clients adequately at the trial. The court does not intend that potentially psychologically damaging information be shared with the litigants. The attorneys shall conform to these direction as officers of the court.

4. The natural mother avers that she has a phobia of travel and that therefore this proceeding [***3] should be transferred from New York County to Bronx County, where she resides. However, the Family Court conducts all Bronx County proceedings under section 392 of the Social Services Law in its New York County courthouse. The natural mother may apply for a modest grant for her transportation costs under the auspices of the Susan Wagner Memorial Fund, which application will be determined on the basis of her indigence and her special psychological needs.

 

1489 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Prospect Enterprises, Inc. v. People


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Schoharie County


76 Misc. 2d 856; 351 N.Y.S.2d 998; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1964



February 1, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the New York State Environmental Conservation Department, brought this motion for summary judgment in plaintiff property owner's action against the Department. The owner's first cause of action was brought pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Acts § 10 and the second cause of action sought a declaratory judgment that N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 15-0501 unconstitutionally deprived the owner of its property without due process of law.


OVERVIEW: The owner operated a large dairy on its land, through which ran a stream classified by the Department as Class "C" with "C (T)" standards for quality and purity. The owner hired a contractor to clear bushes near the stream for the purpose of growing more hay and feed for its cattle. In the process, bulldozers were caused to cross the stream. Although the owner was advised that, pursuant to the statute and regulations, a permit was required for any work that modified the bed or banks of the stream, no permit was ever applied for. The Department therefore instituted action to enforce the statute. The court dismissed the owner's first cause of action on the ground that salutary actions taken by the State to assure that a classified stream was kept pure was proper as long as it was reasonable. Because the owner failed to apply for a permit under the statute, the court was not able to judge the reasonableness of the application of the statute to the owner's circumstances. As to the second cause of action, the court declared that the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the owner's first cause of action and declared that the statute was constitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Environmental conservation -- classified streams -- (Environmental Conservation Law, § 15-0501), against disturbing bed or banks of classified stream without permit, is constitutional.

 Section 15-0501 of the Environmental Conservation Law validly and constitutionally empowers the State Commissioner of Environmental Conservation to classify surface streams, and validly and constitutionally prohibits anyone from changing or disturbing the course or bed of such a stream or to remove any sand or gravel or other materials from the bed or banks of such a stream without a permit from the State Department of Environmental Conservation. The statute is reasonably designed to guard the public and the adjoining or riparian owners against pollution. The statute does not confiscate the waters or the banks of the waters of a dairy farm through whose 500 acres a classified stream flows.
