1491 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hudson v. Sipprell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


76 Misc. 2d 684; 351 N.Y.S.2d 915; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2002



January 29, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The determination by respondent Sipprell that petitioner is ineligible for public assistance until July, 1975 is reversed and the matter is remanded to him with instructions to hold a hearing on petitioner's application for aid and her eligibility for same and to take all appropriate action as required by the findings thereof.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant sought review of the decision of respondents, a Commissioner of the Erie County Department of Social Services and others, which denied the applicant public assistance. The applicant sought (1) to rescind N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 348.4(a); (2) to enjoin respondents from applying § 348.4(a) against her permanently and during the pendency of the action; and (3) an order to direct the acceptance of her application.


OVERVIEW: The applicant fraudulently obtained public assistance when she failed to inform the Department of Social Services that she was employed. The Department, upon learning of the situation, terminated her public assistance, referred the matter for criminal prosecution, and held that the applicant would be ineligible for assistance until a specified time. The applicant was subsequently injured in a car accident and was unable to work. The Department denied her assistance under § 348.4(a). The applicant contended, inter alia, that § 348.4(a) was unconstitutional. The court agreed. The court found that the enactment of § 348.4 established substantive standards and usurped the legislative function. Because the legislature had specifically addressed itself to welfare fraud and the penalties to be imposed, it pre-empted this area and left no alternatives for discretionary rule-making power under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law, §145. Therefore, the administrative agency could not enact legislation that denied assistance as a penalty for fraud. Also, it was not necessary for the applicant to exhaust her administrative remedies because she brought a class action suit to protect the interests of the public.


OUTCOME: The determination by the Commissioner was reversed and the matter was remanded with instructions to hold a hearing on the application for aid and the applicant's eligibility for the same.


HEADNOTES

Social services -- fraud -- regulation withholding all public assistance from fraudulent recipient (18 NYCRR 348.4[a]) is unconstitutional, unauthorized, arbitrary and capricious.

The rule of the State Commissioner of Social Services, to the effect that all public assistance shall be withheld from a single recipient until the amount he wrongfully received by fraud equals the total amount thus withheld (18 NYCRR 348.4[a]), is vague, unconstitutional, unauthorized by statute, and arbitrary and capricious (cf. Social Services Law, § 131, subd. 1; § 145). A determination by a county Commissioner of Social Services that such a recipient is ineligible for two years is reversed and remanded to said county commissioner with instructions to hold a hearing thereon.

 

1492 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Soto


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Bronx County


76 Misc. 2d 491; 352 N.Y.S.2d 144; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1958



January 25, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed felony complaints charging defendants with larceny by false pretenses for collecting welfare benefits without fully disclosing their respective assets to the Department of Social Services.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed felony complaints charging various defendants with larceny for collecting welfare benefits without fully disclosing their assets to the Department of Social Services. The complaints expressly alleged the elements of the crime of larceny by false pretenses. Plaintiff alleged that the payments to defendants were occasioned by an alleged willful concealment of facts which if known to the Department of Social Services (Department) would have resulted in the curtailment of funds in excess of the sum to which defendants were entitled. Defendants claimed that the Department did not rely upon misrepresentations or omissions of defendants since it was undisputed that defendants were entitled to some assistance anyway. The court stated that no New York court has decided whether entitlement to some benefits insulated the recipient from criminal prosecution for receiving excess payments without disclosing such facts to the proper authorities. The court could not determine whether the endorsements on the welfare checks were made pursuant to an original plan to conceal salient facts regarding their eligibility. The court held the cases for action by the grand jury.


OUTCOME: The court held the cases for action by the grand jury. The court stated that while it was evident that defendants could not have received any benefits without indorsing the checks, the court could not determine whether such endorsements were made pursuant to an original plan to conceal salient facts regarding defendants' eligibility. The court held that these matters were reserved for an evidentiary hearing or trial.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- felony complaint -- concealment of fact to obtain greater public assistance -- after hearing upon felony complaints, court hold for Grand Jury action cases of three defendants charged with misdemeanor violation of Social Services Law and with grand larceny in second degree, felony, in that each received semi-monthly public assistance checks over period of time during which she willfully concealed fact which, if known to Department of Social Services, would have resulted in her receiving lesser sums -- if it can be established that she concealed salient facts regarding her eligibility with expectancy of receiving undeserved benefits on continuing basis, such would constitute larceny by false pretenses -- as to alleged nonreliance by department upon misrepresentations, court cannot say, as matter of law, that department would have dispensed funds in disregard of its established guidelines had true facts been disclosed -- as to whether cases may be reduced and tried as misdemeanors notwithstanding expiration of two-year Statute of Limitations, defense of Statute of Limitations is issue to be raised upon trial but such defense would serve as bar to prosecution if raised.

 [***2] 1. After a hearing upon felony complaints, the court holds for the action of the Grand Jury the cases of three defendants charged with a misdemeanor violation of the Social Services Law and with grand larceny in the second degree, a felony, in that each received semi-monthly public assistance checks over a period of time during which she willfully concealed a fact which, if known to the Department of Social Services, would have resulted in her receiving lesser sums.

2. As to whether each case reveals a "common plan or scheme" such that the individual checks may be aggregated to reach grand larceny levels, no evidence has been presented to indicate whether the defendant read the statement on the back of each check cashed, to the effect that the payee was still in need of public assistance, had reported all resources to the department, and would notify it of any change in circumstances or resources. While it is evident that she could not have received any benefits without indorsing the checks, the court cannot determine whether her indorsements thereof were made pursuant to an original plan to conceal salient facts regarding her eligibility, but, if it can be established at an evidentiary [***3] hearing or trial that she concealed such operative facts with the expectancy of receiving undeserved benefits on a continuing basis, such would constitute the crime of larceny by false pretenses as a felony.

3. As to a contention by defendants that the department did not rely upon the misrepresentations, since they would have been entitled to some assistance, albeit lesser sums, without them, the payment of benefits is directly dependent upon the need of the recipient, and the court cannot say, as a matter of law, that the department would have dispensed the funds in total disregard of its established guidelines had the true facts been disclosed.

4. In each of these cases, the prosecutions were not initiated within the two-year Statute of Limitations for a misdemeanor. As to whether they may be reduced and tried as misdemeanors, the defense of the Statute of Limitations is an issue to be raised upon the trial and not on a motion addressed to the sufficiency of the felony complaints, but such a defense would serve as a bar to prosecution if it is raised. It would be waived upon a plea of guilty to a reduced charge.

 

1493 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Duryea


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, New York County


76 Misc. 2d 948; 351 N.Y.S.2d 978; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1984



January 24, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were politicians, sought to dismiss the indictment against them, charging them with substantively violating, and with conspiring to violate, N.Y. Elec. Law § 457. Defendants alleged that the statute was unconstitutional under both the Federal and New York State Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The indictment against defendants alleged that they, on behalf of a Republican committee, in order to promote the election of the Republican candidates, distributed thousands of letters to Liberal Party voters, urging them to vote for the Liberal Party. The effect would be to diffuse Democratic Party support. The statute prohibited such printing and distribution of letters if the writer and/or sender did not list his or its name and address. The court found that the statute was unconstitutional. The politicians had standing, not because their own rights of free expression were violated, but because of a judicial assumption that the statute's very existence could cause others to refrain from constitutionally protected speech or expression. The statute was not limited to deterring defamation, nor was it limited to campaign literature. Even granting the compelling nature of the concern for the integrity of political campaigns, the statute was not limited to deterring campaign defamation and financing violations. The statute was overbroad in that it unfairly and unnecessarily swept within its criminal sanctions activity that was the protected right of every citizen.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the indictment against them. The statute was declared unconstitutional by virtue of its overbreadth.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- election campaigns -- section 457 of Election Law, making it misdemeanor not to print name and address of true distributor or authorizer on any circular or letter containing any allegation about any political party or candidate or proposition, is unconstitutional abridgement of freedom of anonymous speech -- defendants have standing to attack such statute as overbroad and unconstitutional -- indictment for violating statute, and for conspiring to violate it (Election Law, § 446), dismissed.

1. Section 457 of the Election Law makes it a misdemeanor to publish of distribute any handbill, circular, or letter containing any allegation about any political party or candidate or person or proposition, in connection with any election or nomination, without also printing thereon the true name and post office address of the person or committee at whose instance it is published or distributed. Section 446 of the Election Law makes it a misdemeanor for two or more persons to conspire to promote or prevent the election of any person to a public office by the use of any means which are prohibited by law. But anonymity in political expression has long and historically [***2] been a necessary and constitutional right which is zealously protected by the Federal First Amendment's "freedom of speech" and by the State Constitution's "liberty of speech" and "rights * * * peaceably * * * to petition the government, or any department thereof" (N. Y. Const., art. I, §§ 8, 9). Section 457 of the Election Law, in absolutely requiring the identification of any one who exercises his constitutional right to speak freely, is overly and unnecessarily broad and hence is unconstitutional and void.

2. Since section 457 of the Election Law unconstitutionally prohibits free speech as distinguished from conduct, defendants who are charged with violating this section have standing to challenge its constitutionality on the ground that it is unnecessarily broad and absolute.

3. Since section 457 is invalid, the charge of conspiring to violate it (Election Law, § 446) falls also.

4. Accordingly, defendants' motion to dismiss the indictment against them is granted.

 

1494 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Opert v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Putnam County


76 Misc. 2d 1025; 352 N.Y.S.2d 348; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1062



January 23, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petition is dismissed as failing to state a cause of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former teacher commenced a proceeding against respondent board of education for a judgment declaring that the board's action in terminating her service as a science teacher was illegal, arbitrary, and capricious, and directing that she be restored to her job with proper monetary benefits. The board had previously decided not to grant tenure to the former teacher.


OVERVIEW: Although the former teacher was recommended for tenure by numerous individuals, the board decided not to grant tenure to the former teacher. Thereafter, the board terminated the former teacher. The former teacher then commenced a proceeding against the board for a judgment declaring that the board's action in terminating her service as a science teacher was illegal, arbitrary, and capricious, and directing that she be restored to her job with proper monetary benefits. The court dismissed the former teacher's petition for failure to state a cause of action. The court held in part (1) that the former teacher was not entitled to the 60-day notice from the superintendent of schools under N.Y. Educ. Law § 3013(2), as she was recommended for tenure by the superintendent; and (2) that § 3031 did not apply to the former teacher's termination, as § 3031 did not apply to procedure where the superintendent had made a recommendation for tenure.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the former teacher's petition against the board for a judgment declaring that the board's action in terminating her service as a science teacher was illegal, arbitrary, and capricious, and directing that she be restored to her job with proper monetary benefits.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- teachers -- tenure -- notice provisions of Education Law inapplicable when teacher is informed by Superintendent of Schools of his recommendation for tenure and Board of Education denies tenure ( Education Law, § 3013, subd. 2; § 3031) -- petition states insufficient factual allegations to show unconstitutional denial of due process.

1. Petitioner was appointed as a teacher by the respondent on September 9, 1970 for a probationary period of three years. On or about March 28, 1973, in accordance with section 3013 of the Education Law, petitioner was recommended for tenure by the Superintendent of Schools and other supervisory personnel as a probationary teacher who has been found "competent, efficient and satisfactory." The respondent Board of Education reviewed the recommendation and decided not to grant tenure. In an article 78 proceeding to compel the respondent to restore her job, her petition is dismissed for failure to state a cause of action. Subdivision 2 of section 3013 of the Education Law provides that each probationary teacher who is not to be recommended for appointment [***2] on tenure shall be so notified in writing by the Superintendent not less than 60 days immediately preceding the expiration of his probationary period. Where petitioner was recommended for tenure by the Superintendent of Schools, she is not entitled to the 60-day notice from him.

2. Section 3031 of the Education Law, which entitles a teacher to notice from the Board of Education as to the reasons for denial of tenure, applies to the procedure to be followed after the Superintendent's adverse recommendation, and is inapplicable to procedure where the Superintendent has made a recommendation for tenure.

3. Petitioner fails to state a cause of action when she alleges, upon information and belief, that since the Superintendent recommended her for tenure, the board's denial must be based upon reasons other than her academic qualifications and teaching effectiveness. The allegations lack the factual basis to support a conclusion that petitioner's constitutional rights were violated and therefore she was not denied tenure without due process of law.

 

1495 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Labruzzo v. State Wide Ins. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Queens County


77 Misc. 2d 455; 353 N.Y.S.2d 98; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1168



January 23, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion for summary judgment is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On reargument, plaintiff, an individual injured in an automobile accident with defendant insurance company's insured, filed a motion for summary judgment in an action to enforce a judgment against defendant's insured in Louisiana. Defendant contended that the direct action statute of Louisiana, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3474, under which plaintiff initiated the action, was unconstitutional and did not subject defendant to Louisiana's jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff obtained a judgment against defendant's insured in a Louisiana state court arising from an automobile accident that occurred in Louisiana, plaintiff brought suit to enforce the judgment against defendant pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3474, and sought summary judgment. The court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment, rejecting defendant's contention that Louisiana lacked jurisdiction to render judgment against it because it was not licensed to do business in Louisiana and did not transact any business in Louisiana and, consequently, the judgment against it violated due process. The court ruled that because defendant issued its insurance policy, which insured against accidents wherever its insured drove, with the knowledge that insured could be involved in an accident anywhere in the United States, defendant had sufficient minimum contacts with Louisiana to satisfy due process. Further, the court ruled that § 13:3474 was a valid exercise of Louisiana's legitimate interest in safeguarding the rights of persons injured there, and thus, plaintiff's suit did not offend traditional notions of fair play and justice.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment to plaintiff in an action to enforce a judgment entered against defendant's insured in Louisiana arising from an automobile accident with defendant's insured there. Defendant's issuance of its policy, insuring against accidents wherever they arose, was sufficient minimum contacts to confer jurisdiction to Louisiana over defendant; plaintiff's suit did not offend traditional notions of fair play and justice.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- appointment of Secretary of State by nonresident motorist -- statute which provides that operation by nonresident of motor vehicle in Louisiana is equivalent to appointment of Secretary of State of Louisiana as attorney for service of process of insurer of vehicle if insurer is nonresident not authorized to do business in Louisiana is constitutional -- there are sufficient contacts to subject New York insurer to jurisdiction of Louisiana courts -- statute does not offend notions of fair play and justice -- motion by plaintiff for summary judgment based upon money judgment entered by default in Louisiana is granted.

1. In an action in New York by plaintiff, a resident of Louisiana who suffered personal injuries in an automobile accident, against the defendant, an insurance company licensed to do business in New York, Connecticut and New Jersey which had issued a liability insurance policy to the insured in New York, to recover a money judgment entered by default in Louisiana, a Louisiana statute which provides that the operation by a nonresident of a motor vehicle in Louisiana "shall be deemed equivalent [***2] to an appointment by such non-resident of the secretary of state * * * as the attorney for service of process of the public liability and property damage insurer of the vehicle, if such insurer be a non-resident not authorized to do business in the state" is constitutional and the motion by plaintiff for summary judgment based upon the Louisiana judgment is granted.

2. Although one need not be present in the State to subject itself to the jurisdiction of its courts and although the acts of the insured in Louisiana are not attributable to the New York insurer, the issuance of a motor vehicle liability policy to a New York resident insuring against accidents wherever they arise, and realizing that its insureds will invariably be involved in accidents all over the country, are sufficient "contacts" to satisfy the test set forth in International Shoe Co. v. State of Washington (326 U.S. 310) so as to render the New York insurer subject to the jurisdiction of the Louisiana courts.

3. The direct action statute, being a valid exercise of Louisiana's legitimate interest in safeguarding the rights of persons injured there, does not offend traditional notions of fair play and justice,  [***3] and the essence of jurisdiction and due process, being reasonableness and fairness, is satisfied.

 

1496 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Leroy Fantasies, Inc. v. Swidler


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


76 Misc. 2d 747; 351 N.Y.S.2d 626; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2010; 4 P.U.R.4th 329



January 22, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners joint venturers instituted a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, in the nature of mandamus, which sought to review and vacate the orders of respondent Public Service Commission of the State of New York (PSC). The PSC had banned the use of decorative torches using gas as fuel and directed that the natural gas service to the restaurant owned by the joint venturers was to have been discontinued.


OVERVIEW: The use of decorative torches fueled by natural gas was a large part of the ambience of the restaurant. The PSC had ordered discontinuance of the restaurant's natural gas services unless the gas lamps and torches used by the restaurant were extinguished or converted to be used with mantles. The court granted a stay of the enforcement of the PSC's orders pending the court's decision. The court dismissed the petition of the joint venturers holding that the ban on the use of such torches and the directive to discontinue supplying gas to the restaurant unless it discontinued the use of such torches had to stand because the joint venturers failed to show that the PSC acted arbitrarily in determining that the torches constituted a wasteful device or practice or acted arbitrarily in including within the definition of "decorative torches" the gas lamps that existed in the restaurant. The court further found there was no showing to overcome the PSC's determination that the decorative torches were a wasteful device or practice.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the joint venturers' petition. Because the joint venturers informed the court that it intended to appeal the decision of the court in favor of the PSC, the court ordered that the PSC was stayed from enforcing its determination for a period of 30 days from the date of service of the judgment, with notice of entry, upon the joint venturers.


HEADNOTES

Public utilities -- gas -- Public Service Commission properly directed gas corporation to stop supplying natural gas to restaurant which insisted on using natural gas lamps without gas-saving mantles.

After a hearing, the Public Service Commission has properly banned the use of decorative gas torches unless a gas-saving incandescent "mantle" is used; and subsequently, without a hearing, the PSC has properly directed a gas corporation to cease supplying natural gas to a restaurant unless and until the restaurant used mantles on its decorative natural gas lamps (Public Service Law, § 66, subds. 2, 5; § 66-a, subd. 2). A judicial review proceeding by the restaurant is dismissed.

 

1497 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Baisch v. State


Claim No. 53334


Court of Claims of New York


76 Misc. 2d 1006; 351 N.Y.S.2d 617; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1059



January 16, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual brought a tort claim against defendant state for false arrest and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The individual was arrested for driving a van that was painted as the American flag. The paint job was, in a police officer's opinion, a violation of N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 136. The court reasoned that whether or not the individual was expressing an idea by driving a van painted as a flag need not concern the court because such use of a flag was not illegal. The court found as a matter of law that the arrest was for something not constituting a crime and therefore there was a cause of action for false arrest and false imprisonment. The court reasoned that the information filed by the police officer did not state facts sufficient to constitute the crime charged. The court held that the police officer thus committed an illegal arrest, followed by the filing of a void information, and the obtaining of a void commitment.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment for the individual in his tort action against the state for false arrest and false imprisonment.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] False imprisonment -- probable cause -- unlawful display of American flag -- drivingvehicle painted with colors of American flag not violation of section 136 of General Business Law; as matter of law, where arrest is for something not constituting crime, there is cause of action for false arrest and false imprisonment -- claim for false arrest accrues upon arraignment and release -- State's liability continues throughout period of detention.

1. Claimant's vehicle, painted with the colors and design of the American flag, was stopped and claimant was arrested for unlawful display of the American flag (General Business Law, § 136). Claimant was promptly arraigned before a Town Justice who allowed the entry of a plea of not guilty. Unable to post the bail, claimant was incarcerated until bail was posted. Subsequently the charges were dismissed. Whether or not the claimant was expressing an idea by driving a vehicle painted as a flag, such use of the flag is not illegal and therefore there was no probable cause for the arrest. As a matter of law the arrest was for something not constituting a crime and therefore there is a cause of action for false arrest and false imprisonment.

 [***2] 2. A claim for false arrest accrues upon arraignment and release on bail, and a notice of intention to file a claim is timely if made within 90 days from that date.

3. Where the arrest was not pursuant to a warrant and the following confinement pursuant to the order of commitment by the Town Justice was issued by a court which did not acquire jurisdiction, the actions of the Town Justice cannot serve to insulate the State from its continued liability for the false arrest.

4. Based upon the credible testimony and considering all the factors and necessary expenses incurred by the claimant, including attorney's fees, bail bond expenses, automobile storage and related costs, the claimant is entitled to compensatory damages in the sum of $ 2,750.

 

1498 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Security Unit Employees, etc. v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


76 Misc. 2d 435; 351 N.Y.S.2d 348; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1955; 88 L.R.R.M. 3266; 74 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P53,357



January 15, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner union brought a proceeding, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 seeking to enjoin respondent state from refusing to negotiate concerning retirement benefits under a reopener clause in the collective bargaining agreement which existed between the parties.


OVERVIEW: The union sought a declaration that statutes imposing a retirement program upon the union's bargaining unit and which removed retirement benefits from the scope of legally negotiable terms and conditions of employment were unconstitutional. Under the parties' agreement, retirement benefits for employees was a subject that could have been reopened for negotiations between the union and the state. The court found that N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 201(4) eliminated the employer's obligation under the agreement to negotiate retirement benefits, provided for limitations on retirement and death benefits applicable to new entrants, and provided for the temporary suspension of retirement negotiations and a plan for coalition negotiations. The court held that 1973 N.Y. Laws ch. 382 did not violate the union's constitutional rights. The court found that the state had the police power to impair the existing obligation on the part of the state to negotiate retirement benefits with the union and that such power was paramount to any rights under the contract between the parties.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the union's petition, which had sought to enjoin the state from refusing to negotiate concerning retirement benefits under a reopener clause in the collective bargaining agreement between the parties.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- collective bargaining agreement -- retirement benefits -- chapter 382 of Laws of 1973, removing retirement benefits from scope of negotiable terms and conditions of public employment, is constitutional -- petition by union which, at time of its enactment, was conducting reopened negotiations with State concerning retirement benefits, under clause in collective bargaining agreement providing for such reopening, to have it declared unconstitutional, is dismissed.

1. A collective bargaining agreement between the State and the union representing State employees in the security services bargaining unit provided for the reopening of negotiations concerning retirement benefits at the request of the union. After the union requested the reopening of such negotiations and while the reopened negotiations were continuing, chapter 382 of the Laws of 1973 was enacted, removing retirement benefits from the scope of negotiable terms and conditions of public employment. A petition by the union to have this statute declared unconstitutional is dismissed.

2. The statute, which does not attempt to vitiate any employee benefits [***2] which have become vested, does not violate the constitutional prohibition against impairment of a contractual obligation (U. S. Const., art. I, § 10). It has for its purpose the maintenance of a stable economic environment, is addressed to a legitimate end, and the measures taken are reasonable and appropriate to that end.

3. The statute does not violate the constitutional provision that "membership in any pension or retirement system of the state * * * shall be a contractual relationship, the benefits of which shall not be diminished or impaired" (N. Y. Const., art. V, § 7). The contractual right to negotiate retirement benefits is not a "benefit" of membership in the retirement system within the meaning of this provision, which prohibits a reduction of benefits but does not guarantee that members shall always have the means to seek improvements in benefits by collective bargaining.

4. The statute does not violate the constitutional provision that employees shall have the right to organize and bargain collectively through representatives of their own choosing (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 17). Since the obligation to engage in collective bargaining was imposed on the public employee [***3] by statute, it may be limited by statute. And, since the provisions of the statute for limitations on retirement and death benefits apply only to new entrants, it does not deny to the union's members the right to bargain through representatives of their own choosing. However, even assuming those members were affected by the statute and its terms were, as the union asserts, negotiated with another union, it would still not violate this constitutional provision.

5. The statute does not violate the equal protection clause (U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.). It is applicable to all public employees, not merely the members of this union, and, assuming this union was the only one actually negotiating under the reopener clause at the time it was signed into law, this was merely fortuitous.

 

1499 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Moylan v. Kur


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Oneida County


76 Misc. 2d 825; 350 N.Y.S.2d 990; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1962; 74 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P53,361



January 7, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The judgment of conviction is affirmed, and the court reiterates that an appellate review might be of considerable value to all the courts of our State as well as to the law enforcement agencies.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Justice Court of the Town of New Hartford (New York), which convicted defendant of the Sunday closing law embodied within N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 9.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the manager of a department store, which violated the Sunday blue laws by opening for business on a Sunday in contravention of § 9. Before his trial, defendant filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that he was not the proper defendant. The motion was denied. On appeal, the court found that despite defendant's argument to the contrary, an examination of the transcript of the hearing on discrimination disclosed no substantial errors therein. There was a complained filed against defendant and the law enforcement agencies were mandated to investigate the circumstances and prosecute the same within § 9. Moreover, defendant was the proper party because as a salaried employee of the corporation, his duties and responsibilities exceeded those of a mere sales person. He acted as an agent for the corporation and participated in the meeting with the president and carried the corporate orders to open for business on Sunday, knowing that there was a likelihood that he would be arrested. Finally, the exemption provided in N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 10 did not apply to defendant because it was meant to apply to "momma-poppa" stores and not to multiple or chain store operations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- sales on Sunday -- judgment of Justice Court, convicting manager of department store of selling merchandise on Sunday (General Business Law, § 9), is affirmed by County Court.

Judgment of a Justice Court, convicting an individual who is the salaried manager of a department store which is one of a chain of stores owned by a corporation, of violating section 9 of the General Business Law by selling or supervising the sale of shirts, soap pads, and anti-freeze on a Sunday, is affirmed by the County Court. The statute is constitutional, the manager is properly prosecuted as defendant, he cannot claim that he himself observes a different Sabbath (cf. General Business Law, § 10), and the Justice properly determined in a pretrial hearing that this prosecution was not discriminatory ( People v. Utica Daw's Drug Co., 16 A D 2d 12, followed).

 

1500 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ailey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, Buffalo, Trial Term


76 Misc. 2d 589; 350 N.Y.S.2d 981; 1974 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1990



January 4, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion to set aside the verdict of the jury is granted and the defendants discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to set aside the verdict of the jury, which found them guilty of resisting arrest under N.Y. Penal Law § 205.30 and obstructing governmental administration under N.Y. Penal Law § 195.05. The court, at the end of the State's case, dismissed the disorderly conduct charge under N.Y. Penal Law § 240.20 and the assault, third degree charge under N.Y. Penal Law §§ 120.00, 20.00, as a matter of law.


OVERVIEW: The police saw one defendant passing out fliers and stopped to see what the fliers contained. Defendant identified himself and offered his driver's license for verification. When the officers insisted on seeing the fliers defendant refused to hand them one. The second defendant and cohort seeing what was happening entered into the dispute. A scuffle ensued and defendants were arrested. The court held that there was not probable cause for the arrest, such that the charges had to be dismissed. The police had absolutely no probable cause that any one of the nation's laws was being violated. Defendants were seen doing nothing more than exercising their presumptively constitutional First Amendment rights. Where a police officer had no power or right to demand something, then he had no authorized duty to perform in that regard, and any order given was unauthorized where no power or right existed. Thus, the arrest for refusing to obey the officer would be unauthorized, an essential element of N.Y. Penal Law § 205.30, and the "official function," the essential element under N.Y. Penal Law § 195.05, could not be obstructed, impaired, or perverted, if there was no power or right to act.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to set aside the verdict and discharged defendants.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- resisting arrest -- defendants were distributing literature on street; during scuffle, police hit one on head with blackjack and arrested both of them and charged them with disorderly conduct, assault, resisting arrest and obstructing governmental administration; City Court dismissed disorderly conduct and assault charges and set aside verdict of guilty of other charges -- police had no probable cause for arrest, nor could police compel defendants to waive their First, Fourth, Fifth, Ninth and Fourteenth Amendment rights.

The defendant was apparently exercising his First Amendment right to distribute literature on the street, even though the literature bore a red star and the emblem of a hammer and sickle. To two policemen who approached him, he identified himself and showed his driver's license, but he refused to show them the literature. At this point the codefendant crossed over from the other side of the street. A scuffle ensued, jackets and trousers were torn, and one of the defendants was hit on the head with a blackjack and was taken to the hospital; and the defendants [***2] were charged with disorderly conduct, third degree assault, resisting arrest, obstructing governmental administration by resisting arrest, and resisting an officer in the discharge of his duty. At the trial in the City Court, the defendants were not represented by counsel. The court dismissed the disorderly conduct and assault charges, and the jury found the defendants guilty of the other charges. However, on motion of the defendants ( CPL 330.30, subd. 1) the court set aside the verdict and discharged the defendants, on the grounds that the police had no probable cause for the arrest (cf. CPL 140.50, subd. 1; 140.10, subds. 1, 2; 140.15, subd. 2; General Business Law, § 330; Ordinances of City of Buffalo, ch. IX, §§ 24, 49; Penal Law, §§ 35.27, 195.05, 205.30) and that the police could not compel the defendants to waive their First, Fourth, Fifth, Ninth and Fourteenth Amendment rights.

 

1501 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Fred F. French Investing Co. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, New York County


77 Misc. 2d 199; 352 N.Y.S.2d 762; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1216



December 31, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motions by the plaintiff mortgagee and the defendant owners for summary judgment are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee and defendant owners filed motions for summary judgment against defendant city in the mortgagee's action against the owners and the city seeking a declaration that the city's rezoning of the owners' property in which the mortgagee had a security interest constituted an unconstitutional taking by the city.


OVERVIEW: The critical question posed in the case was whether the city's amendment to the zoning regulations, under the guise of creating a special park district, was a reasonable exercise of governmental police power. The court found that the city's action in rezoning the areas of the private parks, which were owned by the owners and were the security for the mortgagee's mortgage, into public recreational areas totally destroyed the economic value of such plots and had significantly deprived the mortgagee of its security for the mortgage. Additionally, the court found that the owners had been deprived of the use of the property for an improvement to which it was reasonably adapted and that the zoning regulation barred the owners from any economic use of their property. The court concluded that the amendment was illegal. The finding by the court that the enactment of the zoning amendment was unconstitutional and void automatically restored the property to the zoning classification it had prior to the adoption of the zoning amendment. The court refused to award damages because the mortgagee and the owners had not demonstrated any immediate financial loss.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motions.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- small private parks cannot be rezoned into public "special" park district; such zoning amendment is unconstitutional and void.

A city's zoning amendment which, under the guise of creating a special park district, purports to rezone two small privately owned parks, which are now classified in an R-10 zone, into a public recreational area which nevertheless must be maintained at the private owners' expense, and which will be classified as a C5-3 zone, is an unconstitutional taking of private property and hence is void. The court directs that the prior zoning classification (R-10) be restored to these two small private parks.

 

1502 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


154 East Park Ave. Corp. v. Long Beach


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


76 Misc. 2d 445; 350 N.Y.S.2d 974; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1507



December 21, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, judgment is granted declaring that the respondent's revocation of the building permit on September 21, 1972 was not arbitrary or improper, but was valid, and that respondent city is liable to plaintiffs for $ 5,785.32 in consequential damages, representing the $ 4,864.75 obligation to the contractor Steins, $ 200 to the engineer Ostfeld, $ 550 to the draftsman Dell Nunzio, and $ 170.57 in Long Beach permit fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of mixed use property, filed an action against defendant municipality seeking an injunction directing the municipality to reissue a building permit that was revoked, or in the alternative, to pay the owners' damages for expenditures made in reliance on the issued permit.


OVERVIEW: A mixed, commercial and residential, use building was damaged by fire. The owners of the building obtained a building permit from the municipality. Subsequently, the building commissioner revoked the building permit asserting that the permit was issued by mistake. A municipal ordinance only allowed renovation of a damaged building if less that 50 percent of a building was damaged. The building in question was more that 50 percent damaged. The owners filed suit seeking an injunction and/or damages for their reliance on the issued building permit. The court granted the owners damages for costs directly relating to any reliance on the originally issued permit. The permit was validly revoked because the ordinance was valid and constitutional, however, the issuance of building permits was a form of warranty and a municipality could be held liable for breach of that warranty.


OUTCOME: The court granted the building owners damages against the municipality.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- building permit -- after nonconforming, mixed residential and commercial building was damaged by fire, to extent that more than 50% of its value and cubical contents was destroyed, building permit was issued for its reconstruction, but permit was subsequently revoked because ordinance allowed reconstruction of nonconforming structure only where not more than 50% of value or cubical contents was damaged -- subsequent revocation was valid, but owner of building is entitled to damages for expenditures made in reliance on permit -- 50% cut-off point in ordinance not unreasonable or confiscatory -- prohibition in ordinance against mixed residential and commercial uses in single structure not unconstitutional -- city not estopped from  [***2] revoking permit -- notice of claim not required in awarding damages -- costs which would have been expended anyway excluded, as are lost profits during delay, since they are speculative.

1. After a building in the City of Long Beach, which was a mixed residential and commercial structure, and nonconforming since an ordinance enacted after its construction prohibited such mixed usage, was damaged by fire, its owner applied for a building permit to restore the damaged portions, and the city's Building Commissioner issued the permit. However, after reconstruction was started, the city revoked the permit, claiming it had been mistakenly granted in view of an ordinance which allowed rebuilding of a nonconforming structure only where not more than one half of its value or cubical contents was damaged. The owner of the building then sued the city and its Building Commissioner for an injunction directing reissuance of the permit, or, failing that, damages for expenditures made in reliance on the issued permit. The action is dismissed against the Building Commissioner and the revocation of the permit is declared valid, but the owner is awarded damages.

2. Over 50% of the building's [***3] value and cubical contents had, in fact, been destroyed, and the 50% cut-off point provided for in the ordinance, which was intended to strike an equitable balance in allowing rebuilding of a nonconforming structure with only relatively minor damage, is not unreasonable or confiscatory.

3. The prohibition in the ordinance against mixed residential and commercial uses in a single structure serves to keep apart living and working population and to unify uses existent in any one building, and it cannot be said to ignore the common good or be unconstitutional, nor is it confiscatory as applied to this building owner.

4. The act of the Building Commissioner in granting the unauthorized permit does not estop the city from revoking it. Indeed, the revocation was required as a necessary act to enforce the ordinance.

5. The failure of the building owner to serve a notice of claim against the city does not preclude it from obtaining damages. Section 50-e of the General Municipal Law requires a notice only where a tort claim is asserted, and this claim is found to be in quasi-contract and warranty, and incidental to the equitable relief sought. Nor does the statute, which is designed to [***4] forewarn a municipality, apply in principle, the occurrences here involved being recent administrative transactions continuously within the city's knowledge.

6. In awarding damages, the court eliminates the costs of debris removal, cleanup and safeguarding, since they would have been expended anyway; lost profits during the delay in construction, since they are speculative, and corporate expenses claimed by the building owner.

 

1503 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


State Div. of Human Rights v. Schenectady


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Schenectady County


76 Misc. 2d 843; 351 N.Y.S.2d 290; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1540; 7 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1192; 7 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P9389



December 19, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State Division of Human Rights (division) brought a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Exec. Law § 297( 6) to enjoin respondents, city and patrolmen's benevolent association from appointing anyone other than complainant, either permanently, temporarily, or provisionally, to the vacant position of police sergeant in the city's department of police, pending a conclusion of all litigation.


OVERVIEW: Complainant, a woman, filed a verified complaint with the division against respondents alleging that she had taken and passed numerous promotion examinations without securing promotion, and that men with equal or inferior qualifications had been promoted. The court found that complainant was ranked number 8 on the list of persons eligible for appointment to the police sergeant position. The selection committee chose the person who ranked number one on the list. The court denied the division's petition to enjoin respondents from appointing anyone other than complainant. The court held that the list that complainant was on had expired by operation of law and not by virtue of any act of respondents. The court held that under the Civil Service Law, the list could not have been extended once it had properly expired. The court also noted that other patrolmen who had taken the examination and had passed were eligible for consideration for appointment to any existing vacancy and that the Civil Service Law did not provide for any exception nor provided anyone with a pre-emptive right to the exclusion of all others otherwise certified and eligible for appointment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the division's application to enjoin respondents from appointing anyone other than complainant either permanently, or temporarily, or provisionally to the vacant position of police sergeant in the city's department of police.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil rights -- sex discrimination in employment -- pending city's appeal to State Human Rights Appeal Board, court will not order city to promote, to position of police sergeant, policewoman whose promotion list has meantime expired.

A policewoman in a city's police department took and passed, several times, promotion examinations for the position of police sergeant, but never was promoted. Recently, when she was number 3 on the then current promotion list, she was again passed over and eligible number 1, a male, was promoted to police sergeant. That list has now expired (Civil Service Law, § 56), and a new examination has been given, which she took. However, she was not given a passing mark and hence she is not on the new current promotion list. She has complained to the State Division of Human Rights and the latter has ordered the city to offer her the next available position of police sergeant. Such order seems to be contrary to the Civil Service Law and the Public Employees' Fair Employment Act and the State Constitution (art. V, § 6) and the city has filed an appeal to the State Human Rights Appeal Board. The appeal has not yet been decided. In this situation,  [***2] the Supreme Court declines to order the city to comply immediately with the order (Executive Law, § 297, subd. 6).

 

1504 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Jay v. Wolfe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Albany County


76 Misc. 2d 680; 351 N.Y.S.2d 301; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1567



December 19, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion to dismiss the petition is hereby denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent putative father presented a motion to dismiss a petition that sought to declare the putative father as a father of a child. The putative father challenged the constitutionality of a statute authorizing petitioner county social services' paternity action while intervenor attorney general defended the statute.


OVERVIEW: The county social services brought a paternity action against the putative father. The putative father sought dismissal of the petition on the ground that the statute authorizing the proceeding, N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 517 (Act), was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds. The Act permitted a proceeding by a public welfare official to be brought within 10 years, but limited individuals who brought such proceedings to a two-year statute of limitations. The attorney general intervened pursuant to the request of the court. On review of the matter, the court noted that a prior decision declared the two-year statute of limitations in the Act unconstitutional, the statute itself was constitutional. The court also rejected the putative father's contention that where the proceeding was not brought for more than eight years after the act of conception, the burden on the putative father to find witnesses on his behalf was practically insurmountable. The court found that the county social services faced even greater difficulty because the mother refused to cooperate.


OUTCOME: The court denied the putative father's motion to dismiss the case.


HEADNOTES

Children born out of wedlock -- filiation proceedings -- 10-year Statute of Limitations does not unconstitutionally deprive putative father of due process by fact that longer time is allowed social services official to bring paternity proceedings than is permitted individual.

A proceeding by a Deputy Commissioner of Social Services to declare respondent to be the father of a child born in 1966 was properly brought under section 517 of the Family Court Act, which permits a proceeding by a public welfare official to be brought within 10 years but establishes a 2-year Statute of Limitations where the proceeding is brought by an individual. A public welfare official is allowed a greater length of time to bring a paternity action because of the city's role as provider of funds for public support. The city should be given the widest latitude in trying to retrieve from an available source moneys expended on public assistance. The 10-year statute does not unconstitutionally deprive a putative father of due process by virtue of the fact that a longer time is allowed a social services official to bring paternity proceedings than [***2] is permitted an individual.

People v. Hoffman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Centralized Special Narcotics Parts, Trial Term, New York County


76 Misc. 2d 564; 351 N.Y.S.2d 87; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1534



December 18, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion is denied in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were indicted for criminal sale and possession of cocaine and for conspiracy to sell and possess cocaine. They filed a motion to dismiss on the issue of whether cocaine was misclassified as a narcotic drug pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 220.00.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed the statute that prohibited the sale and possession of cocaine violated the due process, equal protection, and cruel and unusual punishment clauses of the United States Constitution. Defendants argued that the legislature misclassified cocaine as a "narcotic drug." The court held that the term "narcotic drug" as used by the Legislature was for those drugs which were the most dangerous and included all the drugs the Legislature considered dangerous. The legislature was fully aware that cocaine was not truly narcotic, and still determined to classify cocaine in the same manner as true narcotic drugs. The court found that it was irrelevant whether cocaine was a narcotic in the strict medical sense. The court concluded that there was enough medical and law enforcement evidence to find a reasonable basis for the legislature to classify cocaine as a "narcotic drug" and to regulate its sale, possession and use. The legislative action had a real and substantial relation to public health, safety, morals and the general welfare and was a valid exercise of the police power of the state.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss. The court held that the legislature had not misclassified cocaine as a "narcotic drug."


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- dangerous drugs -- cocaine is dangerous drug; statutes making its unauthorized possession or sale criminal are reasonable and constitutional; motion to dismiss indictments denied.

Among the dangerous drugs or narcotic drugs whose unauthorized possession or sale is made a criminal offense is cocaine (Penal Law, art. 220; Public Health Law, § 3306). The inclusion of cocaine among these legislatively controlled substances is reasonable, valid and constitutional. Defendants' motion to dismiss indictments charging them with the criminal possession and sale of more than 16 ounces of cocaine, and for conspiracy to possess and sell cocaine, is denied without a hearing ( CPL 210.45, subd. 5).

160 West 87th Street Corp. v. Lefkowitz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


76 Misc. 2d 297; 350 N.Y.S.2d 957; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1466



December 13, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, petitioner corporation, sought to declare N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 352-e(2) unconstitutional, to declare a deficiency letter of respondent Attorney-General of the State of New York invalid, and to direct the Attorney-General to accept for filing the amendment to the offering statement declaring its co-operative plan effective.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney-General refused to accept for filing the amendment declaring the plan effective because the corporation declined to produce rent-controlled purchasers after tenants opposed to the co-operative plan alleged that there had been fraudulent practices in the offer and sale of the apartments. The court found no constitutional infirmity in § 352-e(2) and held the fact that the Attorney-General in conducting a preliminary investigation and in deciding to issue a deficiency letter, proceeded without notice and without a participatory hearing and unilaterally decided to withhold the filing of the amendment, was in contravention of no constitutional requirements. The court also held that the determination of the Attorney-General was not final and binding in any sense. The court was unable to determine, solely on the papers before it, whether or not the withholding of approval for filing by the Attorney-General was arbitrary and capricious. A factual hearing was called for so that the court could review the Attorney-General's determination and ascertain whether the facts justified withholding the filing or would warrant preventing the plan from going into effect.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order, which found § 352-e(2) constitutional and which required that a factual hearing be held on the withholding of approval for filing by the Attorney-General.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Landlord and tenant -- co-operative apartment house plan -- Special Term directs hearing ( CPLR art. 78) to determine whether Attorney-General properly refused to approve co-operative plan for apartment house on ground of fraudulent or discriminatory inducements (General Business Law, § 352-e, subd. 2).

The General Business Law ( § 352-e, subd. 2) validly and constitutionally authorizes the Attorney-General, ex parte, to decline to approve a plan to make an apartment house a co-operative; but the Attorney-General's conclusion and reason, that the sponsors of the plan used discriminatory or fraudulent inducements, can and should be reviewed in a hearing before Special Term under CPLR article 78.

Levine v. Long Island Lighting Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


76 Misc. 2d 247; 349 N.Y.S.2d 963; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1458



November 30, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, electricity and water consumers, brought an action against defendants, public service commission (PSC) and utilities, for judgment (1) declaring unconstitutional N.Y. Transp. Corp. Law § 15, and N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 89-b, and (2) enjoining and restraining the utilities from discontinuing electric and water service to the consumers' home.


OVERVIEW: After utilities allegedly threatened to cut off the consumers' home utilities and water, the PSC held a "conference" and refused take action on behalf of the consumers. The consumers brought an action against the utilities and the PSC for a declaration that N.Y. Transp. Corp. Law § 15, and N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 89-b, were unconstitutional, and for an injunction restraining the utilities from discontinuing electric and water service to the consumers' home. The consumers alleged that the PSC refused to hold a "formal hearing", as required by their regulations. The PSC and utilities filed motions to dismiss the consumers' complaint for failure to state a cause of action. The court transferred the action and held that PSC administrative procedures provided a regularized, orderly process of dispute settlement prior to termination and complied with the requirements of due process, and that the proper vehicle for challenging the PSC's failure to hold a hearing was under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78. Under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 506(b)(2), a proceeding against the PSC must have been commenced in the New York Supreme Court, Albany County.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the consumers' action, which alleged that the PSC did not hold a "formal hearing" to review the consumers' complaint as required by their regulations, to another supreme court.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Public utilities -- discontinuance of service to consumer -- provisions for utility company's notice to consumer of discontinuance of service and for hearing of consumer's complaints are valid and constitutional (16 NYCRR 143.1 et seq.; 16 NYCRR 533.1 et seq.) -- if, ultimately, Public Service Commission refuses to conduct formal hearing (16 NYCRR 2.3, 11.1, 11.2), consumer may institute proceeding against Public Service Commission under CPLR article 78; proper venue is Supreme Court, Albany County ( CPLR 506, subd. [b], par. 2).

1. An electric or gas public utility company cannot discontinue service to a consumer, despite an unpaid or disputed bill or balance or deposit, until the company has given the consumer five days' notice in person or by registered mail; and if the consumer complains to the company, the company must investigate; and, if the company decides the complaint adversely to the consumer, the company must notify him that he may complain to the Public Service Commission in person or by telephone; and finally, if the consumer requests it, the PSC must provide a formal hearing with witnesses and cross-examination and counsel and stenographic minutes (16 NYCRR [***2] 143.1 et seq.; 16 NYCRR 2.3, 11.1, 11.2; Transportation Corporations Law, § 15). Similar requirements apply to water supply companies, except that 15 days' notice is required (Public Service Law, § 89-b; 16 NYCRR 533.1 et seq.). These provisions are valid and constitutional.

2. If the consumer complies with these provisions and the PSC still refuses to conduct a formal hearing, the consumer may institute a proceeding under CPLR article 78 against the PSC. However, such a proceeding must be instituted in Albany County Supreme Court ( CPLR 506, subd. [b], par. 2).

 

1508 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Curco Drugs, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Kings County


76 Misc. 2d 222; 350 N.Y.S.2d 74; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2348



November 30, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant's motion to suppress is hereby denied in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to suppress business records seized by the New York Health Department inspectors, alleging that the records had been seized after an illegal, warrantless search, that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3390 was unconstitutional, and that Miranda warnings should have been given.


OVERVIEW: New York City Health Department inspectors performed a routine audit at defendant's pharmacy pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3390. During the audit, defendant was informed that he and the pharmacy were violating N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3324(b)(2) and New York, N.Y., Health Code § 75.07c. The audit disclosed that sales of non-prescription over-the-counter drugs were excessive. Some weeks after an informal hearing at the health department, the inspectors returned and seized the pharmacy's non-prescription records. Defendant filed this motion to suppress, asserting that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3390 was unconstitutional and violated his privacy rights. Defendant also asserted that records were seized after an illegal warrantless search and that Miranda warnings should have been given. The motion was denied, with the court holding that the officers had a statutory right to inspect the records under N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3333; N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3390 was not an unconstitutional invasion of the pharmacist's privacy rights, and no Miranda warnings were required prior to an administrative search.


OUTCOME: The motion to suppress was denied. The inspectors carried out an administrative search for which neither consent nor a warrant was required. Defendant's privacy rights were not violated because defendant knew that these records, which he was required by statute to maintain, were subject to a health department inspection at any time. No Miranda warnings were required.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- pharmacists -- narcotic control -- search and seizure -- health inspectors are peace officers and may constitutionally audit pharmacy's books and records without search warrant and without Miranda warnings (Public Health Law, former § 3390; former § 3333, subd. 3; former § 3324, subd. 2, par. [b]; N. Y. City Health Code, § 75.07) -- defendants' motion to suppress books and records denied.

Inspectors employed by the New York City Health Department are peace officers (Public Health Law, former § 3390). After they audited the books and records of a pharmacist and his corporation (cf. Public Health Law, former § 3333, subd. 3) during business hours for over a week, and after they took the books and records to the Health Department's office for further audit, the pharmacist and his corporation were charged with violating the Public Health Law (former § 3324, subd. 2 par. [b]) and the New York City Health Code (§ 75.07). Said section 3390 is constitutional, no search warrant was needed, and no Miranda warnings (384 U.S. 436) were needed. Defendants' motion to suppress the books and [***2] records from evidence is denied.

 

1509 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Norman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Narcotics Part, New York County


76 Misc. 2d 644; 350 N.Y.S.2d 52; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1564



November 23, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion to quash the subpoena duces tecum in each of the cases is granted in all respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state brought a motion to quash subpoenas served on the city police department requiring the production of personnel records of police officers who were to be called by the state in each narcotic prosecution against defendants.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' counsel served subpoena's on the city police department for the personnel records of the police officers that would testify against defendants. In most cases the officer was not the aggrieved party, but merely an agent of the state, which was the real party in interest. Defendants stated that the sole purpose for seeking the personnel folders of the officers was to ascertain whether information contained in the folders might reveal something in the officers' pasts which might form the basis for impeaching the credibility of the officers on cross-examination. The court concluded that there was no question that defendants would not be permitted to inspect the personnel folders as a matter of right in a discovery proceeding. Further the court held that defendants' counsel failed to demonstrate any theory of relevancy or materiality of the information which was contained in the police records. In the absence of a prima facie showing that such information did exist, the court was of the opinion that the records were not discoverable by compulsory process. The court granted the motion to quash.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion to quash the subpoena duces tecum in each of the cases.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- discovery -- witnesses' credibility -- defendants under indictments for narcotics offenses cannot subpoena Police Department personnel files of policemen who will testify against them, in mere hope of finding material with which to impeach policemen's credibility.

Defendants under indictments for narcotics offenses are not entitled, pretrial, to subpoena the Police Department personnel files of the policemen who are expected to be the principal witnesses for the prosecution, in the mere hope of finding material with which to impeach the policemen's credibility on cross-examination if any. Pretrial discovery ( CPL art. 240) is not that broad nor is confidentiality that narrow. Of course, at the trial itself, after a policeman has testified, a defendant may present to the court any relevant information on which the trial court may, in its discretion, conduct a voir dire in the absence of the jury to determine whether or not, and under what safeguards, to direct the Police Department to produce that officer's personnel file.

 

1510 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Berger v. Adornato


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Onondaga County


76 Misc. 2d 122; 350 N.Y.S.2d 520; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1447



November 21, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner male filed an action seeking an order to direct respondent city clerk to issue a marriage license.


OVERVIEW: Under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 15(2), a different age standard for marriages between males and females was established. A female might have married at age 18 without parental consent, while a male might not have married without consent until he reached age 21. The male, a 20-year-old wishing to marry, filed an action seeking an order to direct the city clerk to issue him a marriage license. On review, the court found that while there might have been valid ends served by restricting the marriage of young males, a desirable end could not have been promoted by prohibited means. The court determined that under § 15(2), there was no guarantee of alike treatment to all those in the classification because the State of New York assigned discretion to the parents. The court held that parents might have used their authority to act on behalf of the State interest or they might have done whatever they pleased. The court ruled that § 15(2) violated the Equal Protection Clause and directed the city clerk to issue a marriage license to the male.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of the male and directed the city clerk to issue him a marriage license.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Marriage -- minors -- Domestic Relations Law ( § 15, subd. 2) which establishes for males and females different age standard for marriage is unconstitutional -- Clerk of City of Syracuse is directed to issue marriage license without requiring parental approval.

1. Domestic Relations Law ( § 15, subd 2) which establishes a different age standard for marriage in that a female can marry at age 18 without parental consent while a male may not marry without such consent until he reaches age 21 is arbitrary and unconstitutional because it does not provide that all persons similarly circumstanced shall be treated alike. Although there may be a valid State objective by restricting the marriage of young males, this burden of fulfilling the State need is assigned to the parents and there are no guidelines or limitations to assure that the parents will perform their responsibility within the framework of the allegedly valid State objective.

2. Accordingly, the Clerk of the City of Syracuse is directed to issue a marriage license to the applicants without requiring parental approval.
