New York Times Co. v. New York Com. on Human Rights


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


76 Misc. 2d 17; 349 N.Y.S.2d 940; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1419; 7 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 173; 7 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P9132



November 20, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The stay of hearing heretofore granted is continued until 10 days after publication of this decision to enable petitioner if it is so advised to make any application it wishes to an appellate court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspaper filed a N.Y. CPLR art. 78 proceeding in the nature of prohibition to restrain respondent, human rights commission (commission), from proceeding with a hearing regarding its advertisements.


OVERVIEW: The newspaper ran advertisements for public and private employment in the Republic of South Africa. The commission charged that each advertisement constituted an advertisement by an employer which expressed, directly or indirectly, any limitation, specification, or discrimination as to race or color. The newspaper filed an art. 78 proceeding seeking to prohibit the commission from proceeding with a hearing on the matter. On review, the court found that the advertisement appeared in a state newspaper, addressed to residents of the state, and no doubt such residents, with general knowledge of South Africa, would believe that it made a substantial difference whether an applicant for employment was white or black. The court determined that the commission could proceed with the hearing in order to make a factual record leading to a reasonably expeditious decision and dismissed the newspaper's petition.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the newspaper's petition seeking to prohibit the commission from holding a hearing.


HEADNOTES

Civil rights -- discrimination in employment -- hearing before New York City Commission on Human Rights on charge that advertisements appearing in petitioner's newspaper for employment in South Africa express directly or indirectly discrimination as to race or color will not be restrained -- hearing will not constitute unconstitutional burden on petitioner's right of freedom of press.

1. In a proceeding in the nature of prohibition to restrain the New York City Commission on Human Rights from conducting a hearing on the charge that advertisements appearing in petitioner's newspaper for public and private employment in the Republic of South Africa constitute advertisements which express, directly or indirectly, discrimination as to race or color (Administrative Code of City of New York, § B1-7.0, subd. 1, par. [d]), the petition is dismissed. Further exploration should be made at a hearing as to whether the matter before the commission is beyond its jurisdiction in that [***2] it relates to foreign affairs of the United States, which is within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Federal Government, and as to whether the use of the words "South Africa" does indirectly express an intent to discriminate on the basis of race or color.

2. The holding of the proposed hearing will not constitute an unconstitutional or unreasonable burden on petitioner's right of freedom of the press. The freedom to print a commercial advertisement is subject to much greater restriction than the printing of news or opinion.

 

1512 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Amber


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Queens County


76 Misc. 2d 267; 349 N.Y.S.2d 604; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1461



November 20, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Except as to that part of the motion which is specifically granted in the foregoing opinion, the same is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a 15-count indictment defendant was charged with the illegal practice of medicine, unlawfully holding himself out as being able to practice medicine, and illegally using the title "physician" in violation of N.Y. Educ. Law §§ 6512, 6521, 6522, and 6513. Defendant, who was not a licensed physician, allegedly engaged in the practice of acupuncture. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictment and a motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: In his motion to dismiss, defendant argued in part that the statute defining the practice of medicine, § 6521, was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. Defendant also argued that the practice of medicine did not include acupuncture. The court rejected these arguments and denied in part and granted in part defendant's motion to dismiss. The court denied the motion to suppress. First, the court held that in order to declare a law unconstitutional, its invalidity must be demonstrated beyond a reasonable doubt. The court concluded that defendant failed to meet this burden. Second, the court held that whether actions constituted the practice of medicine was dependent upon the facts and not upon the name of the procedure, its origins, or legislative lack of clairvoyance. The court held that the practice of acupuncture was the practice of medicine. The court concluded that the statutes under consideration were designed to prevent such conduct as the indiscriminate application of cauterization and the sticking of needles into human beings by unskilled and unlicensed practitioners.


OUTCOME: The court granted in part and denied in part defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment against him alleging that he engaged in the illegal practice of medicine by performing acupuncture. The court denied defendant's motion to suppress.


HEADNOTES

Physicians and surgeons -- acupuncture -- indictment accusing layman of practicing acupuncture is sufficient.

Acupuncture is a practice of medicine. Only a licensed physician may practice acupuncture. An indictment accusing a layman of practicing acupuncture is sufficient. (Education Law, §§ 6512, 6521, 6522.)

 

1513 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Urowsky v. Board of Regents


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Albany County


76 Misc. 2d 187; 349 N.Y.S.2d 600; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2346



November 20, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment is awarded to defendant dismissing the complaint and the preliminary injunction is vacated, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pharmacist brought an action to declare a regulation of respondent Commissioner of Education (New York), N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 8, § 63.3, prohibiting certain advertising to be unconstitutional and for a permanent injunction restraining the New York Board of Regents from enforcing the regulation.


OVERVIEW: The State Board of Pharmacy, a licensing board under the jurisdiction of the Commissioner of Education, notified the pharmacist to appear before a committee of said board pursuant to N.Y. Educ. Law § 6809 to answer charges that the prescription center, where the pharmacist was the supervisor, was advertising through local newspapers discounts on all drug needs. In response, the pharmacist initiated the action and obtained a preliminary injunction restraining the Board from enforcing the regulation. A few days later, new regulations went into effect amending the existing regulation. Under the new regulation, unprofessional conduct included the advertising of prices and the use of words such as "discount." Under the new regulation, the posting of prices was not considered advertising. In effect, both regulations prohibited the same conduct. The court held that an assumed state of facts existed which justified the regulation and it was, therefore, held to be constitutional. The State had a legitimate interest to prohibit advertising in the area of prescription drugs.


OUTCOME: Judgment was awarded to the Commissioner dismissing the complaint, and the preliminary injunction was vacated, without costs.


HEADNOTES

Drugs and druggists -- advertising discounts -- regulation (8 NYCRR 63.3) which prohibits pharmacists from advertising discounts in connection with offering of professional services is constitutional -- validity of present section, although action concerned with former section, is to be determined.

1. Regulation which prohibits a pharmacist from advertising discounts in connection with the offering of professional services (8 NYCRR 63.3) is constitutional. The State has a legitimate interest in prohibiting advertising in the area of prescription drugs so as to foster the policy of encouraging the continued existence of independent local drugstores by the prevention of destructive competition through advertising. In an action to declare 8 NYCRR 63.3 unconstitutional and for a permanent injunction restraining the Board of Regents from enforcing this regulation, the complaint is dismissed.

2. While this action is concerned only with the validity of former subdivision (c) of section 63.3, the validity of the present section, the substance of which as a practical [***2] matter is the same as the former section, is also to be determined.

 

1514 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. John


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special and Trial Term, Erie County


76 Misc. 2d 582; 350 N.Y.S.2d 44; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1555



November 16, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendants' motions are, therefore, denied in these and all other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, inmates charged with various offenses in the aftermath of a prison disturbance, filed motions to dismiss the indictments, alleging improper grand jury proceedings, defective indictments, denial of speedy trial, double jeopardy, insufficiency of evidence for indictments, and interests of justice.


OVERVIEW: Following a disturbance at Attica prison, defendants, some of the inmates, were charges with various offenses. Defendants filed motions to dismiss on numerous grounds. The court held that since the grand jury was selected in conformity with law, it did not need to mirror the demographic make-up of the community. Since defendants' crimes were of the kind not generally disregarded, kidnapping, coercion, etc., their claim of selective enforcement was not valid. The record of the grand jury proceedings indicated that the evidence was sufficient for all indictments. Since N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law art. 40 and art. 200 allowed separate counts for each victim and if the same crime was committed in different ways, and since double jeopardy did not attach to administrative proceedings, there was no double jeopardy bar. Because the prosecutor could file indictments any time within the statute of limitations, and the time period for a speedy trial did not begin until such filing, defendants did not lose their right to a speedy trial. Thus, the court denied the motions in all respects.


OUTCOME: The court denied all motions in every respect, since the record showed that all statutory requirements protecting defendants' rights had been followed, the penalties defendants received in prison were not a criminal proceedings to which double jeopardy would attach, the time period for calculating defendants' right to a speedy trial began when the indictments were filed, and justice did not mandate dismissal of the indictments.


HEADNOTES

Grand jury -- selection of jurors -- selection of grand jurors not reviewable on motion -- selective enforcement prevails only if such crimes are not prosecuted elsewhere in New York -- presumption of regularity in Grand Jury proceedings -- duplicitous counts permissible if individual situation so requires -- speedy trial requirement not violated where trial period has been tolled -- administrative punishment does not sustain claim of double jeopardy -- motion to dismiss must allege that Grand Jury evidence was not legally sufficient -- dismissal of indictments in furtherance of justice not demonstrated.

1. Statutes with respect to the qualifications of grand jurors are not unconstitutional in that they result in a Grand Jury whose members are not mathematically proportionate in sex, race and age to the population of Wyoming County. The court and the prosecutor made a sincere effort to empanel a Grand Jury that was not infected with bias or prejudice toward anyone subject to its scrutiny. In addition, the court lacks jurisdiction to review the acts of another Justice of the Supreme Court [***2] in drawing the Grand Jury.

2. While criminal acts may have been committed by agents or officers of the State during and after retaking of the facilities at Attica and no indictments have been returned against persons other than Attica inmates, defendants are not being subjected to selective enforcement of the law. The principle of selective enforcement applies only when it is designed to discriminate against persons prosecuted, without any intention to follow it up by general enforcement against others. The crimes charged in the indictments, kidnapping, coercion and assault, are not generally disregarded anywhere in the State of New York.

3. There is a strong presumption of regularity that attaches to Grand Jury proceedings.

4. Counts of the indictment having identical wording have not violated the prohibition against duplicitous counts. Those counts are plain and specific and presumptively charge the defendants therein with separate offenses. Articles 40 and 200 of the CPL allow: (1) charging of lesser included offenses, (2) separate counts for separate victims and (3) separate counts if the same crime may be committed in different ways.

5. A right to a speedy trial occurs [***3] only "after a criminal action is commenced" ( CPL 30.20, subd. 1). The records indicate as to each defendant that the six-month ready for trial period has not elapsed but has been tolled pursuant to the provisions of subdivision 4 of CPL 30.30.

6. Subdivision 1 of CPL 40.30 declares that a person is prosecuted within the meaning of CPL 40.20 "when he is charged therewith by an accusatory instrument filed in a court of this state or of any jurisdiction within the United States." Therefore, administrative punishment does not sustain a claim of double jeopardy.

7. Subdivision 2 of CPL 210.30 requires that a motion to dismiss on the ground of insufficiency of evidence must allege that there is reasonable cause to believe that the Grand Jury evidence was not legally sufficient and defendants have not sustained their burden of demonstrating that there is such reasonable cause. Nevertheless the court has inspected the Grand Jury minutes and finds sufficient legal evidence, which if uncontroverted or unexplained, would support convictions by the triers of the facts.

8. No sufficient basis for dismissal of the indictments in the furtherance of justice has been demonstrated.

 

1515 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Lavine


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


76 Misc. 2d 733; 349 N.Y.S.2d 592; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1574



November 16, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner aid recipient sought review of a determination made by respondent Commissioner of Social Services, which after a hearing affirmed the determination of respondent City Social Service Agency to reduce the recipient's grant of aid to a disabled person by recouping payments made to him to which he was not entitled, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 404.


OVERVIEW: The recipient received aid to disabled. But unknown to the agency, he also received disability payments from the Veteran's Administration. The agency sent the recipient notice of intent to reduce public assistance and to recoup the amount paid in excess. The recipient requested a hearing, and the commissioner agreed with the determination of the agency. The recipient sought to annul the decision, but the court agreed with the findings. The court denied the recipient's claim that he did not receive adequate notice of the charges or an opportunity to defend against them. The court held that he was sufficiently conversant with the hearing procedure and that the right to counsel was indicated in the notice he received. The court held that a prior three-judge court had determined that 18 N.Y. C.R.R. 348.4 and its regulations were valid against the claim that they violated the Due Process, Equal Protection, and Supremacy clauses of the Constitution. The court held that § 404 specifically provided that when a recipient of assistance received more than the amount to which he was entitled, any future payment due would be decreased.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the agency.


HEADNOTES

Social services -- notice of fair hearing -- petitioner was advised of his right to counsel and fair hearing -- State not required to support needy irrespective of their conduct -- recoupment by Social Services agency does not violate Social Security Act.

1. In a proceeding to annul a determination which reduced petitioner's grant of aid to a disabled person and recouped payments made to him to which he was not entitled, the petition is dismissed. Petitioner was given adequate notice of the charges against him and an opportunity to defend against the proposed action of respondent. The notice stated that "If you believe that your assistance should not be reduced, you may request a state fair hearing * * *. If you request a fair hearing, a notice will be sent to you informing you of the time and place of your hearing" and that petitioner was entitled to be represented by an attorney. Clearly, petitioner received due notice of the charges against him and that he was entitled to be represented.

2. The provisions of 18 NYCRR 348.4 do not violate the New York Constitution and the Social Services Law requiring aid, care and support [***2] for the needy. The Constitution (art. XVII, § 1) and the Social Services Law ( § 131, subd. 1; § 131-a, subds. 1, 3) set forth the general policies of the State to provide for the needy insofar as funds are available for that purpose but they do not require that every inhabitant of this State, normally qualified for such aid, is entitled to be supported regardless of his actions and conduct.

3. The New York statute and regulations requiring repayment of assistance benefits do not violate due process or equal protection.

4. In view of section 404 of title 42 of the United States Code which provides that when a recipient of assistance has received more than the amount to which he is entitled, the Secretary shall decrease any future payment due him, recoupment by the social services agency does not violate the Social Security Act.

Helms v. Diamond


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Schenectady County


76 Misc. 2d 253; 349 N.Y.S.2d 917; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1459



November 14, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is therefore denied and the temporary stay heretofore granted is vacated. However, petitioners are granted reasonable time to pick up and transport any passengers flown into the prohibited lakes during the period of the temporary stay.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was petitioner air taxi owner's motion for a preliminary injunction that sought to vacate and nullify respondent state environmental agency's order, which prohibited petitioner from landing in certain areas within the Adirondack Park.


OVERVIEW: The air taxi owner had filed a motion for a preliminary injunction that sought to vacate and nullify the state environmental agency's order that prohibited it from landing in certain areas within the Adirondack Park. The order prohibiting the operation of an aircraft on designated bodies of water in the forest preserve was attacked as illegal, and in violation of the constitution. The court disagreed, and denied the motion for preliminary injunction. The court could not conclude that under N.Y. Const. art. XIV, § 1 and N.Y. Exec. Law §§ 811 and 816, the commissioner of the state environmental agency was without power to provide for the prohibition of an aircraft on the named bodies of water in the forest preserve. The court found the regulation was a valid implementation of the state policy. Further, the court did not find the action was arbitrary or capricious. Finally, the court concluded that the air taxi owner had not established a clear legal right to the relief requested.


OUTCOME: The court denied the air taxi owner's motion for a preliminary injunction, and declined to vacate and nullify the state environmental agency's order that prohibited the air taxi owner from landing on certain areas within the Adirondack Park.


HEADNOTES

Environmental conservation -- State-owned forest preserve -- mechanically propelled aircraft and vessels are prohibited on some 700 lakes and ponds in State-owned forest preserve (6 NYCRR 196.4); preliminary injunction against enforcement of such regulation is denied.

The State Commissioner of Environmental Conservation has prohibited any operation or landing by any mechanically propelled aircraft or vessels on some 700 lakes and ponds in the State-owned "forever wild" forest preserve (N. Y. Const., art. XIV, § 1; 6 NYCRR 196.4; Environmental Conservation Law, §§ 1-0101, 3-0301, 9-0105; Executive Law, § 800 et seq.). The regulation does not appear to be unconstitutional, invalid, arbitrary or capricious. Its enforcement will not be preliminarily restrained.

 

1517 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Robey v. State


Claim No. 53237


Court of Claims of New York


76 Misc. 2d 1032; 351 N.Y.S.2d 788; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1195



November 9, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant arrestees filed an action seeking damages against defendant State of New York (state) for false arrest and malicious prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Police on routine patrol observed the arrestees' vehicle unattended in a restricted parking area. Upon looking through the windows of the illegally parked vehicle the officers saw what they believed to be an American flag with a peace symbol in the upper left-hand corner. Drugs were discovered in the vehicle. The arrestees were arrested for desecration of a flag in violation of N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 136(A) and for possession of dangerous drugs in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 220.05. The court ruled in favor of the arrestees with regard to their claims for false arrest. The arrestees' claims for malicious prosecution were dismissed. The arrestees were awarded compensatory damages. The court held that even if the police believed the "flag" to be desecrated, there still was no justification for the arrest, since the flag certainly was not exposed to public view. The court found that what attracted the police to the scene was the illegal parking of the vehicle, and the police were justified in checking the vehicle and to issue parking violations, which was not done.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of the arrestees in their claims against the state for false arrest and awarded compensatory damages. The court dismissed the arrestees' claims for malicious prosecution.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] False imprisonment -- damages against State -- cardboard crayon flag with peace symbol, on interior wall of truck behind driver's seat, was not flag and was not" exposed to public view" (General Business Law, § 136, subd. a) -- arrested students were not "in the automobile at the time" that vial of amphetamine pills "was found" in glove compartment (Penal Law, § 220.25) -- arrest was without warrant, without reasonable cause, and without legality -- students are awarded $ 8,000 damages against State -- cause of action for malicious prosecution is dismissed.

1. On a summer night about midnight, several college students drove in a panel truck to a quiet public beach, and parked the truck there in a no-parking zone, and went on foot about 100 yards further down the beach behind some sand dunes. Two State Troopers on patrol saw the empty parked truck and approached it and saw, on its interior wall behind the driver's seat, a piece of paper or cardboard on which there were drawn, in crayon, red and white stripes and a peace symbol in its upper left corner. The student who owned the truck consented that the truck be searched; and thus, in its glove compartment, the troopers found [***2] a vial containing some amphetamine pills. The students, but not the one who owned the truck, were arrested and charged with possessing dangerous drugs (Penal Law, § 220.05) and with exhibiting a picture or design on a flag of the United States (General Business Law, § 136, subd. a).

2. However, this warrantless arrest was illegal, since there was no reasonable cause to believe that the alleged offenses or crimes had been committed ( CPL 140.10; Code Crim. Pro., § 177, subd. 1). The students were not arrested for unlawful parking. The crayon picture or design was not a flag of the United States and it was not "exposed to public view" (General Business Law, § 136, subd. a); moreover the United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit has adjudged said subdivision unconstitutional as applied to an American-like flag with a peace symbol. As for the amphetamine pills, the students were not "in the automobile at the time such drug was found" nor were they in "physical possession" of the pills (Penal Law, § 220.25; § 10.00, subd. 8).

3. For the next 13 hours the students were under arrest and were booked, photographed, fingerprinted, and finally arraigned and bailed. About [***3] a month thereafter, a Town Justice held a suppression hearing and suppressed the seized evidence and dismissed the informations. The People did not appeal. The students' legal expenses were $ 100. For the false arrest and imprisonment and the arrest record, the three students are respectively awarded $ 3,000, $ 2,500, and $ 2,500 damages against the State of New York.

4. However, there was no proof that the State Troopers had actual malice, and hence the cause of action for malicious prosecution is dismissed.

People v. Scher


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, Centralized Special Narcotics Parts, New York County


76 Misc. 2d 71; 349 N.Y.S.2d 902; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1434



November 9, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant's omnibus motion is denied in all other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an omnibus motion at his trial for eight counts of selling a dangerous drug and other lesser included crimes in violation of various sections of article 220 of N.Y. Penal Law, and N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3381. Defendant claimed that the indictment should be dismissed on ground that it was brought by a court without jurisdiction over the offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted by the Special Narcotics Courts of the Supreme Court of the State of New York sitting in the City of New York, New York County. The crimes were committed in a drugstore that was located in the County of Bronx, City of New York. Defendant claimed that the grand jury which indicted him and the petit jury that would try him were illegally constituted. The court held that N.Y. Jud. Law § 177a-e was not unconstitutional in its provisions that provided for indictment and trial for narcotics offenses by any Special Narcotics Part in any county regardless of the location of the crime charged. The court recognized that it had the power to declare that the provisions of § 177 were unconstitutional, it declined to so, and reluctantly stated that the legislature's actions were constitutional. The court found that the trial of defendant in a county other than that in which the crimes were committed raised constitutional issues under the Sixth Amendment. The court chose to eliminate the constitutional question by ordering that defendant's trial be moved to the county in which the crimes were alleged to have been committed.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss the indictment and directed that the venue of the trial be changed to the county in which the crimes were alleged to have been committed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Special Narcotics Parts -- in Bronx County defendant allegedly sold dangerous drugs; he was properly indicted by New York County Grand Jury (Judiciary Law, art. 5-B); but, to avoid any question of unconstitutionality, he should be tried in Bronx County -- court suggests that statute be amended accordingly.

1. In Bronx County, defendant allegedly sold dangerous drugs (Penal Law, art. 220). He was lawfully and properly indicted by a Grand Jury drawn from and sitting in New York County (Judiciary Law, art. 5-B; CPL 190.20; cf. N. Y. Const., art I, § 2, and art. III, § 17). However, in order to avoid any question of unconstitutionality (U. S. Const., 6th Amdt.), this court directs that the defendant be tried in Bronx County by a petit jury drawn from residents of Bronx County.

2. The court suggests that the Legislature amend article 5-B of the Judiciary Law accordingly.

210 E. 68th St. Corp. v. City Rent Agency


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


76 Misc. 2d 425; 349 N.Y.S.2d 896; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1506



November 8, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion and cross motion are granted to the extent herein indicated, and otherwise denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, rent controlled property owners, filed an action for a declaratory judgment and an injunction against defendant, the City Rent Agency of the City of New York. The property owners sought to invalidate a City Local Law No. 24, which repealed the maximum base rent provisions and the return hardship provisions in the City Rent and Rehab. Laws. The property owners and the City filed motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The City passed Local Law No. 24, which repealed the maximum base rent entitled to be received by property owners and also repealed the basis for calculating hardship rent increases. The property owners challenged the repeals. The court held that Local Law No. 24, § 2 was invalid because it contradicted 1971 N.Y. Laws 372, which prohibited the City from passing local laws or ordinances that subjected the property owners to more stringent or restrictive provisions of regulation and control than those that were already in effect at the time 1971 N.Y. Laws 372 became effective. The court found that the City's adoption of Local Law No. 24 repealed a provision which in fact subjected the property owners to more stringent regulation and control. The court declared that Local Law No. 24, § 2 was void. The court went on to find that Local Law No. 24, § 3 repealed a section of Local Law No. 30, § 12, which was not in effect at the time 1971 N.Y. Laws 372 became effective and, therefore, was a valid local law. The court conceded that its ruling had countering effects, but stated that the resolution of the rent control issue was for the state legislature and city council.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment to the property owners insofar as it declared the local law void. The court denied the City's motion for summary judgment insofar as it declared the repeal of the local law valid.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- New York City Rent and Rehabilitation Law -- Special Term adjudged and declared that city's repeal of provision for fixing maximum base rents is invalid, but that city's repeal of provision for increasing rents up to 8 1/2% of landlord's net annual return is valid -- State statute restricting rent control in city is constitutional.

1. Special Term adjudged and declared (a) that New York City's repeal of the provisions of the New York City Rent and Rehabilitation Law which directed the City Rent Agency to establish a formula for fixing maximum base rents (MBR) is invalid, on the ground that the repeal substituted rent-control provisions which are "more stringent or restrictive * * * than those presently in effect"; but (b) that New York City's repeal of the provision allowing landlords to obtain hardship rent increases which would give them an 8 1/2% net annual return is valid, on the ground that the 8 1/2% provision became effective on January 1, 1972 and therefore was not "presently in effect". (L. 1971, ch. 372, § 1, last sentence, eff.  [***2] June 1, 1971; Local Laws, 1973, No. 24 of City of New York, §§ 2, 3, repealing Local Laws, 1970, No. 30 of City of New York, §§ 11, 12; Administrative Code of City of New York, § Y51-5.0, subd. a, pars. [4], [5]; § Y51-5.0, subd. g, par. [1], subpar. [a].)

2. Rent control in a "city having a population of one million or more" (L. 1971, ch. 372, § 1) is a State concern; hence this statute (L. 1971, ch. 372) does not invade constitutional local government (N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 2, subd. [b], par. [2]; § 3, subd. [d], par. [4]).

 

1520 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


King v. Power Authority of State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Greene County


76 Misc. 2d 725; 351 N.Y.S.2d 493; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1572



November 1, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the complaint is dismissed for failure to state facts sufficient to constitute a cause of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant power authority brought before the court a motion for dismissal of the complaint in this action for a declaratory judgment and for a permanent injunction, and also moved for dismissal of a motion brought by plaintiffs, an individual and others, for a preliminary injunction pendente lite.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that plaintiffs were the owners of real property, that the power authority entered upon their lands without their consents or permission and performed certain activities thereon that interfered with the quiet enjoyment and use of said lands, and interrupted and impaired plaintiffs' possession of their real property. The court held that the specific purposes for entering upon the lands of plaintiffs were clearly authorized by title 1 of article 5 of the Public Authorities Law. The court held that the entry upon plaintiffs' lands to conduct the activities engaged in by the power authority did not establish any legal basis for complaint on the part of plaintiffs. Entry upon private property for the purpose of making surveys and examinations prior to construction of public works, when such entry was authorized by the legislature, could not be considered as a taking of property in the constitutional sense. The court held that the allegations of the complaint set forth either legal conclusions without factual support or pertained to the exercise of powers delegated to the power authority by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint for failure to state facts sufficient to constitute a cause of action.


HEADNOTES

Public authorities -- entry on private property -- Public Authorities Law authorizes entry of State Power Authority upon private property for purpose of making surveys -- temporary entry by public authority is constitutional even without compensation.

1. Defendant State Power Authority and its duly authorized agents had the right to enter upon plaintiff's real property for the purpose of making surveys to determine the suitability of said property for a base load generating facility. The specific purpose for entering upon the land of the plaintiff is clearly authorized by title 1 of article 5 of the Public Authorities Law. Such entry does not establish any legal basis for complaint by plaintiffs. There can be no question of defendant's liability for damages caused by its activities.

2. Entry upon private property for the purpose of making surveys and examinations prior to construction of public works when such entry is authorized by the Legislature cannot be considered as a taking of property in the constitutional sense. A statute authorizing entry, even [***2] without compensation, by public authorities upon private land is constitutional to the extent that the occupation or entry is temporary or the infliction of damage is incidental.

 

1521 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Vasquez


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Bronx County


76 Misc. 2d 5; 348 N.Y.S.2d 1007; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1416



October 31, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion to dismiss is denied for reasons as set forth herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the assault charges against him, on the ground that he was subjected to an improper, unauthorized, and unconstitutional deprivation of his rights in being arraigned pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 170.30 (1)(f),(g) and 170.40.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested for assault, the arresting officer and the complainant prepared a written complaint and the Assistant District Attorney presumably made his "fact sheet." Neither the arresting officer nor complainant were present at arraignment the next day. Defendant objected to pre-arraignment without these parties, and challenged the pre-arraignment procedure by moving to dismiss the charges against him, on the ground that he was subjected to an improper, unauthorized, and unconstitutional deprivation of his rights in being arraigned. The court held that the pre-arraignment procedures did not violate defendant's U.S. Const. amend. VI, right of confrontation, because the right of confrontation did not accrue at a point so early in the criminal proceeding. The county's pre-arraignment procedures violated defendant's right to the granting of reasonable bail and did not conform with the requirements of N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 510.30. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss, finding that defendant lacked standing because he had suffered no personal harm or injury, and had not been inconvenienced because of being arraigned.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- arraignment -- when arresting police officer and complaining witness are both absent at arraignment of defendant, court cannot reasonably fix bail; hence police department regulation excusing police officer and complainant after they have sworn to accusatory instrument, is unconstitutional -- but defendant who was not detained has no standing to attack such regulation.

1. The fixing of bail in a reasonable amount is a constitutional right (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 5; U. S. Const., 8th and 14th Amdts.). At an arraignment, if both the arresting police officer and the complaining witness are absent, the court cannot obtain the facts required by CPL 510.30 to fix bail, even if the NYSIS fingerprint record is available. Hence, a police department regulation, excusing the arresting police officer and the complainant after they have sworn to an accusatory instrument prepared by an Assistant District Attorney, is unconstitutional, even though the police department regulation was approved by the District Attorney and the Appellate Division.

2. However, a defendant who was not detained at arraignment and who,  [***2] instead, was paroled, has no standing to attack the procedure.

 

1522 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Glass v. Thompson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


75 Misc. 2d 824; 349 N.Y.S.2d 57; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1380



October 30, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the movant defendants are granted summary judgment as hereinabove stated. This determination is, as indicated, without prejudice to such further objection on constitutional grounds as may be raised with respect to the manner in which section 110 is being implemented and administered as to the instant plaintiffs. It follows that the plaintiffs' motion for a temporary injunction is denied as well as the motion for leave to proceed in this action as poor persons.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants filed an action for an injunction against defendants, administrative judge, court administrator, and court clerk, and for a judgment declaring N.Y. City, N.Y., Civil Court Act § 110(e) unconstitutional insofar as it appointed hearing officers to render judgment in summary proceedings against tenants. Defendants moved for summary judgment on their counterclaim that § 100(e) was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The tenants challenged the constitutional validity of § 110(e) on the ground that it contravened N.Y. Const. art VI, § 15, which provided for the establishment of a single court of city-wide jurisdiction. That section also provided that the civil court would consist of judges as provided by law. The court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and denied the tenants' motion for an injunction, holding that it was possible to construe § 110(e) in such a way as to avoid conflict with the state constitution. The court concluded that the statute could be read as if it contained the condition that any trial before a hearing officer had to be on consent of the parties in order to sustain the constitutionality of the section. Moreover, §110(e) did provide for the assignment of actions and proceedings to hearing officers. Thus, § 110(e) could reasonably be given a construction that did not do violence to the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants in their counterclaim to declare § 110(e) constitutional on its face without prejudice to any further objections on constitutional grounds if hearing officers were assigned to proceedings without the consent of the tenants.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- summary proceedings -- statute which authorizes appointment of hearing officers to render judgment in summary proceedings not violative of New York State Constitution (CCA, § 110, subd. [e]) -- construction of section authorizing hearing officer to determine issues and render judgment without consent of parties need not be adopted since section may be read so as to imply consent -- constitutional objection to manner in which section is implemented may be raised at trial.

1. Subdivision (e) of section 110 of the New York City Civil Court Act which authorizes the appointment of hearing officers in a housing part of the Civil Court who may render judgment in summary proceedings [***2] to recover possession of residential premises and to remove tenants therefrom is not violative of section 15 of article VI of the New York State Constitution which directs the establishment of a single court of city-wide civil jurisdiction in New York City consisting of elected Judges.

2. Construing this section as authorizing a hearing officer to determine summary proceedings where the parties do not consent to such officer need not be adopted if, without deciding, it would thereby render the statute unconstitutional. This section may be read as if it contained the condition that any trial before a hearing officer must be on consent in order that the constitutionality of the statute be sustained.

3. Any constitutional objections to the manner in which this section is being implemented may be raised at the time of trial. Accordingly, the motion by plaintiff to enjoin defendants from causing or allowing the summary proceedings pending against them to be heard or decided by any person other than a duly elected Judge of the Civil Court is denied.

4. Defendants are entitled to summary judgment to the extent of declaring that section 110 is on its face constitutional.

 

1523 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jacobus


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Cortland County


75 Misc. 2d 840; 348 N.Y.S.2d 907; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1384



October 30, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint and for summary judgment is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought an order permanently enjoining defendant doctors from deleting required information from certificates of fetal death in alleged violation of the provisions of the N.Y. Pub. Health Law. The doctors filed a motion for an order dismissing the complaint pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211. Both the doctors and the state brought motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The doctors deleted the names and addresses of the parents of aborted fetuses from certificates of fetal death in alleged violation of the provisions of the N.Y. Pub. Health Law. The state sought an order permanently enjoining the doctors from deleting the information and civil penalties. The doctors filed a motion to dismiss the complaint and joined with the state in requesting summary judgment. The doctors argued that provision of the information constituted an unconstitutional invasion of the mothers' right to privacy, was contrary to public policy and denied the mothers equal protection of law. The court granted the doctors' motion, holding that (1) the state by its reporting requirement, was not seeking to regulate abortion but only to obtain accurate reports for statistical purposes; (2) the state's expressed intention to use the data for purposes of promoting public health was reasonably related to a legitimate purpose; and (3) reporting the name of the father or mother in cases of fetal death resulting from lawful abortion could not be required until confidentiality was adequately protected.


OUTCOME: The court granted the doctors' motion to dismiss the complaint and for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Health -- identification of aborted patient -- physician-patient privilege does not justify refusal of physicians to disclose name of aborted patient to Department of Health under Public Health Law ( § 4100) -- requirement of disclosure is not unconstitutional -- until safeguards in statute prevent disclosure of names to others for purposes unrelated to public health, reporting of names cannot be required.

1. The refusal of defendant physicians to furnish on certificates of fetal deaths the names of the parents (Public Health Law, § 4100, subd. 2, par. [g]) may not be justified on the basis of the physician-patient privilege.

2. The requirement that the names of parents of aborted fetuses be disclosed to the Department of Health, as part of the State's vital statistics, is not an unconstitutional invasion of privacy. The requirement does not interfere with the woman's freedom of decision. The State's intention to use the data thus obtained for the purposes of promoting public health is a legitimate purpose.

3. Until safeguards are set forth in the statute to prevent the identity [***2] of aborted mothers from being disclosed to others for purposes unrelated to public health, reporting of the names cannot be required.

Velez v. Sugarman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, New York County


75 Misc. 2d 746; 349 N.Y.S.2d 53; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1357



October 16, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion by defendants for summary judgment dismissing the complaint is granted. The cross motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants brought a motion for summary judgment and plaintiffs also cross-moved for summary judgment in an action brought for declaratory and injunctive relief to determine whether or not plaintiffs, as "special officers," were peace officers as set forth in N.Y. Penal Law § 265.20.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiffs were "special officers" in the employ of the Department of Social Services who were appointed pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law §265.20 and were involved with appointment of "special patrolman" by the police commissioners of the city. The plaintiffs' civil service titles were "special officers" and they were governed within the Department of Social Services by the Rules and Regulations of the Social Service Police Patrol. The action was brought for declaratory and injunctive relief to determine whether plaintiffs, as special officers, were peace officers as contemplated in § 265.20. If found not to be peace officers, plaintiffs sought to declare portions of N.Y. City Admin. Code § 434a-7.0(e) to be unconstitutionally vague, and to enjoin defendants from requiring plaintiffs to make arrests, detain or restrain persons. The court denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment concluding that plaintiffs were not peace officers under § 265.20, and that § 434a-7.0(e) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The motion by defendants for summary judgment dismissing the complaint was granted; plaintiffs' cross motion was denied because plaintiffs failed to show that they were "peace officers" pursuant to state statute and failed to show that the city administrative code provision was unconstitutionally vague.


HEADNOTES

Social services -- special officers -- plaintiffs, special officers of Department of Social Services of City of New York, are not peace officers who may carry firearms without license -- without consent of Commissioner of Social Services, plaintiffs may not carry firearms while on duty -- subdivision e of section 434a-7.0 of Administrative Code of City of New York is constitutional.

1. Plaintiffs, special officers of the Department of Social Services of the City of New York, are not peace officers within the definition of subdivision 33 of CPL 1.20 and are not exempted from possessing firearms without a license (Penal Law, § 265.20).

2. Without the consent of the Commissioner of Social Services, plaintiffs may not carry firearms while on duty.

3. Subdivision e of section 434a-7.0 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York is not so vague as to be unconstitutional, nor is it unconstitutional since it relates in part to two sections of the New York City Criminal Court Act which were repealed. These sections can now be found in the Criminal Procedure [***2] Law which took effect on the date the New York City Criminal Court Act was repealed.

Posner v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


75 Misc. 2d 875; 348 N.Y.S.2d 1000; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1318



October 11, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, public office holders, citizens, and taxpayers, sought a judgment against respondent, the Governor of the State of New York, that declared 1973 N.Y. Laws 603 (Act), unconstitutional. Preliminarily, petitioners filed a motion for a temporary injunction to restrain the Governor from appointing judges of the Court of Claims pursuant to the Act. The Governor filed a cross-motion for dismissal of the petition.


OVERVIEW: The Governor argued that the court had no subject matter jurisdiction; that petitioners did not have the legal capacity to sue and lacked standing; that the petition was legally insufficiency; and that the court lacked personal jurisdiction over the Governor. The court found that petitioners lacked standing. The court found, inter alia, that: (1) the constitutionality of a state statute could only be challenged by those personally aggrieved, such that the parties bringing the action had to have suffered a special injury different from that suffered by the public at large; (2) the courts of first instance were not to exercise transcendent powers of declaring an act of the state legislature unconstitutional, except in rare cases involving life and liberty; and (3) because the determination as to the constitutionality of a challenged statutory section might give rise to serious consequences, the resolution was to rest with the higher courts.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the petition for declaratory judgment failed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- standing to challenge constitutionality -- State Assemblymen and other public office holders and citizens and taxpayers have no standing, as such, to sue for judgment declaring State statute unconstitutional; such suit is dismissed.

The constitutionality of a State statute can be challenged only by one who suffers a special injury because of the statute. It cannot be challenged by a citizen or taxpayer or a State Assemblyman or other public office holder, merely as such. Accordingly, their action for a judgment declaring various parts of the so-called "emergency dangerous drug control program" (L. 1973, ch. 603) unconstitutional is dismissed by Special Term.

 

1526 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Guthman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


75 Misc. 2d 572; 348 N.Y.S.2d 109; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1592



October 10, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought before the court a motion for an order declaring N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20 unconstitutional, or in the alternative providing for reciprocal disclosure of witnesses, i.e., alibi. The district attorney had served upon defendant a demand for a bill of particulars with respect to an affirmative defense that defendant was elsewhere than at the scene of the crime. Defendant had not responded to this demand.


OVERVIEW: Defendant indicated in his moving papers his intention to assert an alibi defense upon the trial. Defendant argued that any statute requiring disclosure of alibi witnesses had to provide for reciprocal disclosure of rebuttal witnesses or fall under the proscription of the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. The district attorney suggested to the court that the overall practice of discovery now extant in the State of New York by virtue of statute and case law might be sufficient to satisfy the requirements of the due process provisions of the United States Constitution. The court held that although § 240 did not afford a liberal and broad discovery of various items and categories of evidence as the people contended, it did adopt a middle-of-the-road approach, halfway between the extreme liberal position and the extreme prosecution approach. The court held that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 240, within its existing framework, authorized the court in its discretion to provide reciprocal disclosure as required by the United States Supreme Court. N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 240.20(2), (3), and (4).


OUTCOME: The court ordered defendant, within five days of the entry of the order, to comply with the alibi demand served by the district attorney. The court ordered that upon receipt of the appropriate response from defendant, the district attorney had to file with the court and serve upon defendant a comparable response with regard to any rebuttal witnesses within 20 days of receipt of defendant's notice of alibi.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- alibi -- when District Attorney receives list of defendant's alibi witnesses ( CPL 250.20), District Attorney must serve and file list of alibi-rebuttal witnesses; thus construed, CPL 250.20 is constitutional -- witness who testified, as part of People's case, that defendant was at scene of crime, is not alibi-rebuttal witness.

1. When a District Attorney requires and receives from a defendant a list of the defendant's alibi witnesses ( CPL 250.20), the District Attorney must serve and file a list of his alibi-rebuttal witnesses. Thus construed, the cited statute is constitutional.

2. A witness who, as part of the People's case, testifies that defendant was present at the scene of the crime, is not merely an alibi-rebuttal witness.

 

1527 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Collins


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


75 Misc. 2d 535; 348 N.Y.S.2d 99; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1595



October 5, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with commission of the crimes of the criminal sale of a dangerous drug in the third degree and the criminal possession of a dangerous drug in the fourth degree. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the notice of alibi provisions of N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a declaration that § 250.20 was unconstitutional because it did not provide for reciprocity of disclosure and that he did not have to comply with the alibi statute in order to present alibi witnesses and testimony at the trial. Defendant also sought an order requiring the prosecution to disclose to him the witness who would be produced to disprove the defense of alibi. The court held that the alibi statute was constitutional, but that there was an implied provision of reciprocity in the statute from case law and other statutory provisions. The court found, inter alia, that (1) the norm to be applied in determining whether a notice of alibi statute was constitutional was whether defendant enjoyed reciprocal discovery against the state; (2) a statute was not be declared unconstitutional unless required to do so by most cogent reasons or compelled by unanswerable grounds and unless such conclusion was unavoidable; and (3) N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 240.20 was to be construed in such manner that, when defendant complied with the provisions, a concomitant obligation came into existence under which the district attorney had to afford defendant the same rights.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's request for relief to declare the alibi statute unconstitutional and gave a reciprocal discovery order against the district attorney, contingent on defendant complying with the five-day notice provision.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- alibi -- defendant must serve notice of alibi and list of alibi witnesses ( CPL 250.20) -- statute is constitutional if construed to require People then to serve similar list of rebuttal witnesses -- court recommends that Legislature amend CPL 250.20 accordingly.

1. CPL 250.20 empowers a trial court to exclude alibi testimony if the defendant has failed to serve the District Attorney with a notice of alibi and with the names and residential addresses and places of employment of all alibi witnesses. This section is constitutional if it is construed as requiring the District Attorney, when served with such a notice, to serve on defendant's counsel the names, residential addresses and places of employment of all witnesses who will rebut defendant's alibi. The District Attorney is so ordered.

2. The court recommends to the Legislature that CPL 250.20 be amended to provide for such reciprocal obligation.

People v. Butor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Dutchess County


75 Misc. 2d 558; 348 N.Y.S.2d 89; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1597



October 4, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the motion to dismiss is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought an omnibus motion to suppress a blood test, for inspection of grand jury minutes, to obtain separate trials on two counts, and for dismissal of the indictment in an action where he was charged with criminally negligent homicide, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol, and failing to drive on the right side of the roadway.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for criminally negligent homicide, two crimes of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol, and one crime of failing to drive on the right side of the roadway. Defendant filed four motions, including one to suppress blood test evidence, one for inspection of grand jury minutes, one for separate trials on two counts, and the final one for dismissal of the indictment. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss. The court held that defendant was not deprived of the right to plead guilty in local criminal court to driving while intoxicated and failure to keep right. Defendant's contentions on pleading in criminal court were unsupported by conclusive factual affirmations that he truly sought to do as he had asserted. The court decided to hold the motion to suppress in abeyance pending outcome of a hearing. The court denied the motion to inspect the grand jury minutes. In conclusion, the court denied the motion for separate trials, pointing out that the trial judge could instruct the jury accordingly, so that defendant would not be prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss, holding, among other things, that defendant was not deprived of the right to plead guilty in local criminal court to driving while intoxicated and failure to keep right.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- charges adjourned for presentment to Grand Jury -- with defendant's consent, his time to plead to charges of traffic violation and misdemeanor of driving while intoxicated was adjourned, and then District Attorney properly obtained further adjournments in order to present matter to Grand Jury ( CPL 170.20), and thus, 5 1/2 months after arrest, defendant was properly indicted for felony of criminally negligent homicide in addition to above-stated misdemeanor and violation -- CPL 170.20 is constitutional -- right to speedy trial not denied -- counts shall be tried together -- hearing shall be had of defendant's motion to suppress test of his blood.

1. As a result of an automobile collision, defendant was arrested and was charged in the Town Justice Court with the misdemeanor of driving while intoxicated and with the traffic violation of failing to keep to the right half of the road. With his consent, his time to plead was adjourned several times, and then the District Attorney obtained several further adjournments in order to present these matters to a Grand Jury ( CPL 170.20, subd. 2) and finally, 5 1/2 months after [***2] he was arrested, defendant was properly indicted for the felony of criminally negligent homicide and for the misdemeanor of driving under the influence of alcohol and for the traffic violation of failing to keep to the right half of the road. The cited statute ( CPL 170.20) is constitutional. The Grand Jury minutes show sufficient evidence ( CPL 210.30). Defendant has not been deprived of his constitutional right to a speedy trial. The counts of the indictment shall be tried together ( CPL 40.10, subd. 2; CPL 200.20).

2. A hearing shall be had of defendant's motion to suppress a test of his blood made in a hospital immediately after the accident ( CPL 710.60, subd. 4).

 

1529 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carter


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


76 Misc. 2d 543; 349 N.Y.S.2d 249; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1530



October 2, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion for an order requiring the People to disclose their alibi rebuttal witnesses is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brought before the court a motion for an order declaring the New York "notice of alibi" statute, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20, unconstitutional and permitting him to offer an alibi defense at the trial despite his failure to serve the notice required by that statute. In the alternative, defendant requested that, should the court find the statute constitutional, the people be required to afford him reciprocal discovery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted and the people, in keeping with the usual practice, attached a demand for a notice of alibi to the copy of the indictment that was served upon defendant. The court held that there was a strong presumption of constitutionality that attached to any statute duly enacted by the legislature. Courts at nisi prius should be most reluctant to hold a statute unconstitutional and could properly do so only where that result was inescapable. The court's analysis of N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.20 in light of other case law revealed that the conclusion of unconstitutionality was not inescapable. But the court held that § 250.20 was amenable to a construction requiring reciprocal disclosure. While the court could not hold that § 250.20 was unconstitutional, the court was required to enforce it judiciously so as to avoid the risk of committing reversible error. By affording reciprocal discovery pretrial, the court could satisfy the requirements of due process enunciated by the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion for an order requiring the people to disclose their alibi rebuttal witnesses.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- alibi -- reciprocity -- if notice of alibi is served, then order should require People to disclose their alibi rebuttal witnesses -- possibility of reciprocal disclosure renders statute constitutional.

The due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment forbids enforcement of a notice of alibi rule unless reciprocal discovery rights are given to criminal defendants. Under subdivision 2 of CPL 250.20 the court has discretion in deciding whether or not preclusion should be ordered upon a failure to serve a notice of alibi. Courts might now hold that preclusion may be invoked under the statute only where reciprocal disclosure has been available to the defendant. Such a rule made binding on all New York courts would render the "notice of alibi" statute constitutional. Accordingly, a motion to declare the statute unconstitutional is denied and a motion to require the People to disclose their alibi rebuttal witnesses is granted.
