Smyle v. Savitt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


73 Misc. 2d 259; 342 N.Y.S.2d 104; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2134; 82 L.R.R.M. 3118



March 13, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, 573 teachers and clerical employees, filed a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 action after respondent acting superintendent determined that they had failed to establish that they had not violated N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 210(1).


OVERVIEW: Respondent superintendent determined that a work stoppage or strike had occurred over a four-day period. He notified each of the 573 teachers and clerical employees that they had violated § 210(1) by being absent from work without permission. Thereafter, the acting superintendent informed the teachers and clerical workers that their affidavits of objection failed to establish that they had not violated § 210(1). The teachers and clerical workers then filed an action under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78. The court granted the superintendent and acting superintendent's motion to dismiss that proceeding. The court found that they had followed the procedure outlined in N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 210, which had been found to be constitutional. Moreover, the teachers and clerical workers had made no factual statement in their affidavits of objection or any statement in their petition that excused their absence from school on the specified dates.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the teachers and clerical employees' petition.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Schools -- Public Employees' Fair Employment Act -- absence from work without permission -- objections filed to determination that petitioners had violated Civil Service Law by their absence from work without permission were properly dismissed -- procedure followed by respondents is outlined in section 210 of Civil Service Law and has been held constitutional -- presumption that employee who is absent from work on date when strike occurs engaged in such strike has not been overcome.

1. Objections filed by petitioners, teachers or clerical employees in the Plainview-Old Bethpage School District, to a determination that they had violated the Civil Service Law ( § 210, subd. 1) by their absence from work without permission on specified dates were properly dismissed. Their petition to vacate said determination or, in the alternative, to direct that a "due process hearing" be conducted is dismissed.

2. The procedure followed by respondents is outlined in section 210 of the Civil Service Law and has been held constitutional ( Matter of Sanford v. Rockefeller, 40 A D 2d 82).

3. The petitioners made no factual statement in their affidavits of objection, nor have they made [***2] any statement in the petition excusing their absence from work on the dates specified. The presumption that an employee who is absent from work on the date or dates when a strike occurs engaged in such strike (Civil Service Law, § 210, subd. 2, par. [6]) has not been overcome.

 

1580 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Mariello v. Montanye


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


County Court of New York, Wyoming County


73 Misc. 2d 82; 341 N.Y.S.2d 495; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2148



March 9, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition claiming that his sentence arising out of his conviction for selling a dangerous drug in the fourth degree was illegal.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of criminally selling a dangerous drug in the fourth degree and was sentenced to a seven-year prison sentence. He did not receive any examination for drug addiction before he was sentenced and claimed that his sentence was illegal because he had no presentence narcotics examination, allegedly required by N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 207. The court denied the petition. The sentence of concern in § 207 was 134 words long, half the length of the Gettysburg Address. The only thing that saved the ersatz literary product from judicial recycling due to unconstitutional vagueness was the rule of construction. The court assumed the statute to be constitutional and salvaged any pertinent part of the sentence that could be excised. The legislature did not mean for every criminal to be examined for drugs. If the statute was to make sense, there had to be some sign of narcotics use in addition to the offense before an examination was required. Thus, committing one of the offenses by itself did not require a presentence narcotics examination. Other matters needed to be present to alert the court to a possible narcotics problem.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.


HEADNOTES

Mental health -- drug addiction -- Mental Hygiene Law ( § 207, now § 81.19) does not require that every person charged with violating article 220 of Penal Law be examined for drug addiction; other matter must also be present to alert court to possible narcotics addiction problem; petitioner, who was convicted of violating section 220.30 of Penal Law, was properly sentenced to prison.

Petitioner, who was convicted of criminally selling a dangerous drug in the fourth degree ( Penal Law, § 220.30) claims that his prison sentence was illegal because he had no presentence narcotics examination. Section 207 (now § 81.19) of the Mental Hygiene Law does not require that "every person charged with a violation of any offense defined in article two hundred twenty of the penal law" must be examined for drug addiction. Other matter must also be present to alert the court to a possible narcotics addiction problem. There being no information here before the sentencing court to show any drug addiction, petitioner's sentence was proper.

 

1581 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Giustiniani


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, New Rochelle


73 Misc. 2d 223; 342 N.Y.S.2d 116; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2150



March 9, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information against him for violating N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1129(a) on the ground the provision was unconstitutional, or, in the alternative, directed the People to serve a bill of particulars setting forth the acts constituting the violation.


OVERVIEW: An officer of the parkway police issued a summons to defendant for violating § 1129(a). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information, claiming that the provision was unconstitutional. In the alternative, defendant requested that the People be directed to serve bill of particulars setting forth the acts constituting the violation. The court denied the motion in all respects. The court held that following closely in a reasonable effort to pass another car in a reasonable manner was not necessarily a violation. The flexibility provided in the statute made it constitutional. The words in the statute, through common usage, conveyed to the public a sufficiently clear and accurate concept of the activity that was prohibited. Because the statute was constitutional and the language was adequately specific, the People did not need to convey furnish a bill of particulars.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss in all respects.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- following too closely -- subdivision (a) of section 1129 of Vehicle and Traffic Law which prohibits driver of motor vehicle from following another vehicle "more closely than is reasonable and prudent" is constitutional.

1. Subdivision (a) of section 1129 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law prohibits the driver of a motor vehicle from following another vehicle "more closely than is reasonable and prudent". The language of said subdivision provides flexibility and conveys to the public a sufficiently clear and accurate concept of the activity which is prohibited and is, therefore, constitutional.

2. Defendant is not entitled to a bill of particulars. The language of the statute tells the defendant what he must meet.

 

1582 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Friedrich v. Katz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


73 Misc. 2d 663; 341 N.Y.S.2d 932; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2152



March 9, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is denied and it is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner 18-year-old male brought a special proceeding for an order directing respondent Clerk of the City of New York to issue him a marriage license without the male first obtaining his parents' written consent. He alleged that N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 15(2) unconstitutionally discriminated against him as a male because there was no comparable provision requiring an 18-year-old female to obtain parental consent to marry.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether there was an appropriate governmental interest in requiring the male to obtain parental consent to marry while not fixing the same requirement for an 18-year-old female. The court found that the discrimination was an ancient rule, time-honored, and the public policy of the State of New York and much of the nation. The primary obligation of a husband or father was to support his wife and children. Interwoven in that obligation was the recognition that natural order, taught both by history and reason, designated the male as the provider in the usual marriage relation. That duty was sufficient reason to require males to be older and generally more suited to their duty before they could independently decide to marry. The court held that in the presence of a legitimate state interest in the marriage relation and the reasonably conceivable fact that the male would be the provider in the marriage relation, there was a rational basis for the State to provide safeguards affecting the marriage of male minors. The male did not meet the heavy burden of overcoming the strong presumption of constitutionality of N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 15(2).


OUTCOME: The court denied and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Marriage -- minors -- Domestic Relations Law ( § 15, subd. 2) validly and constitutionally requires parents' written consent for marriage of girl under 18 or of male under 21.

The Domestic Relations Law ( § 15, subd. 2) validly and constitutionally provides that, if "the man is under twenty-one years of age * * * or * * * the woman is under the age of eighteen years * * * then the town or city clerk before he shall issue a [marriage] license shall require the written consent to the marriage from both parents of the minor or minors". This age discrimination against males is not unreasonable, since the males are the legally obligated supporters of the females they marry.

 

1583 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kleinfeldt v. New York City Employees' Retirement System


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, New York County


73 Misc. 2d 310; 341 N.Y.S.2d 784; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2162; 83 L.R.R.M. 2679



March 7, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, summary judgment is granted to the extent of declaring that as to the plaintiff and those similarly situated, subdivision 4 of section 431 cannot constitutionally be applied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an employee and others similarly situated, sought a declaratory judgment from the court as to the application of N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 431(4) as applied by defendant, New York City Employees' Retirement System. The Uniform Sanitationmen's Association and the New York State Attorney-General also filed for leave to appear and file briefs amicus curiae. All matters were consolidated for review.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for a city transit authority for 20 years and retired in May of 1972. Under a local code, the employee was entitled to receive an amount equal to on-half of his salary or compensation earnable by him for transit service in the year prior to his retirement. However, the employee's pension benefits were adversely affected by a new law, under N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 431(4), which provided a change in the computation of the pension amount and became effective in April of 1972. The employee filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment with respect to the application of § 431(4), and the retirement system argued that the limitation was not a limitation on retirement benefits but a limitation on salary. The court granted summary judgment to the employee to the extent that, as to the employee and those similarly situated, § 431(4) was unconstitutional. The court ruled that § 431(4) would be unconstitutional if it were to apply the same to any civil service employee who became a member of the retirement system prior to the effective date of the enactment, despite the fact that its prospective application was within the bounds of legislative enactment.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment to the extent of declaring that, as to the employee and those similarly situated, the statute could not be constitutionally applied.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- retirement -- 12-month salary base -- subdivision 4 of section 431 of Retirement and Social Security Law which excludes from salary base period for purposes of retirement increase of earnings in excess of 20% is unconstitutional as to employee who joined retirement system prior to such subdivision's effective date of April 1, 1972.

Section B3-36.6 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York provides that after 20 years of service and reaching the age of 50 years, an employee of the transit system can retire on one half of the salary earned by him in the year prior to retirement. Subdivision 4 of section 431 of the Retirement and Social Security Law which provides that on or after April 1, 1972 the portion of compensation earned during any 12 months included in the salary base period, which exceeds that of the preceding 12 months by more than 20%, shall not be included in the salary base for retirement purposes. Plaintiff worked for the city transit system for [***2] 20 years and retired at the age of 62 on May 6, 1972. Subdivision 4 of section 431 as applied to plaintiff so as to reduce his retirement allowance, serves to diminish and impair retirement benefits in violation of section 7 of article V of the Constitution and is unconstitutional not only as to plaintiff but as to any person who became a member of the retirement system prior to April 1, 1972.

 

1584 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Procaccino v. Board of Elections


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


73 Misc. 2d 462; 341 N.Y.S.2d 810; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2172



March 5, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, pursuant to subdivision (b) of CPLR 3212 summary judgment is granted to the extent of directing judgment in favor of the defendant declaring section 131-a of the Election Law of the State of New York constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate brought an action against defendant Board of Elections of the City of New York seeking a declaratory judgment that N.Y. Elec. Law § 131-a, which provided for runoff elections in cities with a population of one million or more when no city office candidate received 40 percent or more of the votes, violated the equal protection provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.Y. Const. art. I.


OVERVIEW: The candidate, who had run for the office of mayor of New York City, contended that the legislature's regulation of the manner in which candidates for mayor, city council president, and comptroller were chosen in N.Y. Elec. Law § 131-a violated a local government's right to home rule as provided by N.Y. Const. art. IX, § 2, subd. b. The court held that N.Y. Elec. Law § 131-a did not conflict with the constitutional grant of home rule in N.Y. Const. art. IX because it was clearly related to a matter of state concern and the run-off procedure delineated therein was a part of the election process. It was not arbitrary merely because it affected only New York City and had a rational basis, the implementation of effective local self-government. N.Y. Elec. Law § 131-a clearly was a special and not a general law, and under the state concern doctrine was removed from the phrase "property, affairs, or government" embodied in N.Y. Const. art. IX. Separate classes based on population were permissible where conditions due to differences in population might reasonably require differentiation in laws applicable to them. Thus, § 131-a did not violate equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment for the Board.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- elections -- Election Law ( § 131-a) validly requires, if no candidate for New York City Mayor or Comptroller or City Council President receives 40% of party vote, run-off primary election between two highest candidates.

Despite a lack of any special request therefor from the New York City Council and Mayor or any certificate of necessity from the Governor, the State Legislature has validly and constitutionally added the following section to the Election Law: "131-a. Party nominations; primary run-off election in certain cases. Any inconsistent provision of law to the contrary notwithstanding, in cities having a population of one million or more, in any case in which no candidate for the office of mayor, city council president or comptroller receives forty percent or more of the votes cast by the members of a political party for such office in a city-wide primary election, the board of elections of such city shall conduct [***2] a run-off primary election between the two candidates receiving the greatest number of votes for the same office. In the event such run-off election be required it shall be held on the second Tuesday next succeeding the date on which the initial primary election was held." This enactment does not contravene home rule (N. Y. Const., art. IX, § 1 [opening unnumbered par.]; § 2 [subd. (b), par. (1); subd. (b), par. (2), cls. (a), (b); subd. (c), cl. (ii); subd. (c), par. 1]; § 3 [subd. (c)]) or the equal protection of the laws of suffrage (N. Y. Const., art. I, §§ 1, 11; art. II, § 1; U. S. Const., 14th Amdt.; Election Law, § 130).

 

1585 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Miceli


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Court of New York, New Rochelle


73 Misc. 2d 133; 341 N.Y.S.2d 262; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2175



March 2, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The defendant, having complied with the applicable law, is found not guilty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was accused of violating the city's building code.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an information accusing defendant of violating its building code when he obtained a building permit from the Urban Development Corporation of the State of New York (corporation), but failed to obtain a similar permit from the city. The court held that defendant was not guilty of violating the city's building code because the corporation was constitutional and had a right to issue a building permit, and because defendant had a right to rely upon the building permit and was under no obligation to apply for a second permit from the city. The court found that the corporation's "override" power to ignore the restraints of local regulation was derived from N.Y. Const. art. XVIII, § 1, and that the New York State Urban Development Corporation Act was merely a confirmation of the existing power. The court held that N.Y. Const. art. IX did not restrict the corporation's override power because article IX was expressly subject to other applicable provisions of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant was not guilty of violating the city's building code.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- urban development housing -- demolition contractor who obtained demolition permit from Urban Development Corporation, contract vendee of real property, is not guilty of violating New Rochelle's Building Code requiring permit from city -- Legislature not restricted by city's home rule powers -- Urban Development Corporation's override powers are constitutional regardless of whether two successive Legislatures passed it and Governor signed it twice -- Urban Development Corporation had power to issue permit even if it was not owner.

1. A demolition contractor who obtained a permit from the Urban Development Corporation, the then contract vendee of real property, to demolish said real property is not guilty of violating section 112 of the New Rochelle Building Code for failure to obtain a demolition permit from said city. The State's soverign "override" powers, apply. The Urban Development Corporation as a State agency derives its said power from its constitutional power to ignore the restraints of local regulation and not from the Urban Development Corporation Act or any [***2] other statute.

2. Despite the home rule power of the city, the Legislature is unrestricted when it acts with respect to matters of State concern.

3. The override power is constitutional irrespective of whether the Urban Development Corporation Act was passed by the Legislature with the approval of the Governor at its regular session in one calendar year and re-enacted and approved in the following calendar year.

4. The Urban Development Corporation had power to issue the demolition permit even though it was not the owner but only a contract vendee. The New Rochelle Building Code allows a nonowner to apply for a permit.

 

1586 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Tinsley v. New York State Board of Parole


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


73 Misc. 2d 289; 342 N.Y.S.2d 259; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2179



March 1, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who had been incarcerated after being convicted of attempted sexual abuse, sought to annul respondent parole board's determination which revoked his conditional release and which held him to his maximum expiration date in a proceeding brought under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78.


OVERVIEW: After interviewing petitioner upon his release, a parole officer prepared a report of violation of parole which charged petitioner with (1) using an alcoholic beverage to excess and being admittedly intoxicated; (2) stating that he would refuse to abide by some of his parole conditions; and (3) being a menace to himself and to other persons. After a hearing, the parole board revoked petitioner's parole. The court held that, under N.Y. Correct. Law § 212(10), once it was satisfied that there had been a meaningful factual presentation before the parole board, its review was limited. Further, a question of substantial evidence under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7803(4) may be raised to challenge a parole board's determination revoking parole and in a proper case the matter must be referred to an appellate court, N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7804(g). The parole board's determination was not arbitrary or capricious with regard to the first two charges of the violation report because the petitioner failed to meet his burden of supporting his allegations and arguments with facts. Moreover, petitioner's expression of intent not to abide by the conditions of his parole was properly considered by the parole board.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's petition.


HEADNOTES

Parole -- revocation -- on his very first appearance before parole officer, convict was intoxicated and abusive and stated that he would not abide by any rules except to report to parole officer; after hearing at which convict was represented by counsel, his conditional release was properly revoked by Parole Board; judicial review proceeding dismissed.

Convicted of attempted sexual abuse and sentenced to an indeterminate term not exceeding four years, and conditionally released or paroled from Ossining Correctional Facility after a year and three months and told to report at once to his parole officer in New York City, the convict became drunk and intoxicated and went to his parole officer while still carrying a half full bottle of whiskey and told the parole officer in abusive and belligerent terms that he would not abide by any rules governing parole except that he would make his scheduled office reports. The Parole Board then held a revocation hearing (Correction Law, § 212, subds. 1, 7). The convict was represented there by counsel ( People ex rel. Menechino v. Warden, 27 N Y 2d 376, followed), who cross-examined the parole officers.  [***2] The convict's prior record of assault and violence and mental illness was properly read into the record. This was a meaningful factual presentation. The Parole Board properly revoked the parole or conditional release and directed that the convict serve the rest of his maximum term. This determination was not arbitrary or capricious but, rather, met the requirements of due process of law and was supported by substantial evidence (cf. CPLR 7803, subd. 4, and Correction Law, § 212, subd. 10) and hence the Supreme Court dismissed this judicial review proceeding.

Wilson v. State


Claim Nos. 50142, 50882


Court of Claims of New York


73 Misc. 2d 931; 343 N.Y.S.2d 216; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2242



February 7, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant landlords filed a motion for an order directing respondent State to pay interest on the landlord's claim. A decision by the court awarded the landlords a sum with interest. That decision held that the State could not use statutory suspensions of interest as a lever to force a claimant to either do what he was not legally obligated to do, or to accept less that the amount provided by statute because that was patently unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: At trial of the landlords' claims against the city, the court entered a judgment in the landlord's favor. The attorney-general issued a certificate of no appeal from the judgment. The State refused to pay the interest required by the judgment. An assistant attorney-general answered the landlord's motion by stating that because the court's jurisdiction was limited, the court did not have equity jurisdiction nor did it have the power to direct the state's comptroller to act except as provided by N.Y. Ct. Claims Act § 22. The court held that it did have equity jurisdiction and that the challenge rested on a threefold error: it counseled disobedience to the court's final unappealed judgment; it usurped the function of the appellate division by reversing or modifying a valid judgment of the court; and it advised the landlord to seek the compliance of a state official by a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding. Pursuant to N.Y. Ct. Claims Act §§ 8, 9, and 12, the court had comprehensive jurisdiction to try and decide all claims against the State including the right to afford equitable relief where it was incidental to a claim for a money judgment.


OUTCOME: The court granted the landlord's motion for an order directing the State to pay interest on the landlord's claim.


HEADNOTES

State -- Court of Claims -- Court of Claims granted motion ordering State to pay interest on advanced payment and appropriation award, each from date State stopped paying interest to date of payment; State's use of statutory suspensions of interest to force claimants' compliance unconstitutional; incidental equitable relief proper to force compliance with court's judgment.

The Court of Claims granted an order directing the State to pay interest on the entire advance payment and on the balance of an appropriation award, each from the dates on which the State stopped paying interest to the dates of payment. In the decision making the award, the court had pointed out that statutory suspensions of interest to force claimants to obtain releases from lessees or accept an advance payment offer less than the statutory percentage of value were unconstitutional. The court, though having no equity jurisdiction, has the right to afford equitable relief when incidental to a claim for a money judgment and require compliance with its final, unappealed judgment.

O'Brien v. Troy Urban Renewal Agency


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Rensselaer County


72 Misc. 2d 1058; 340 N.Y.S.2d 367; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2252



February 5, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The proceeding is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner sought review of an order from a trial court (New York), which dismissed the property owner's petition that sought to annul a determination by respondent Urban Renewal Agency not to purchase the improved realty owned by the property owner that had previously be designated as property "to be acquired" by the urban renewal plan presented to the city council.


OVERVIEW: The property owner challenged the dismissal of her petition that objected to the agency's decision not to purchase her property after it had designated the property as "to be acquired" in the urban renewal plan. The property owner argued that the adoption of the urban renewal plan by the city constituted a rezoning of the property from business to residential, and thereby placed a legal restraint on its use that amounted to a constructive condemnation in violation of the property owner's right to due process. The court determined that under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 503-a(4)(e), the city was allowed to plan and rezone municipal areas that were in furtherance of the plans and goals of the agency. The city's approval of the local urban renewal plan did not infringe on the property owner's rights because the State was allowed to pass laws for the general good of all people that narrowed the rights of the individual property owner. The agency, as an arm of the State, was allowed to impinge on the individual constitutional rights of the property owner as the urban renewal plan was intended for the general good of all persons.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the property owner's petition.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- urban renewal -- adoption of Urban Renewal Agency's plan did not result in unauthorized rezoning tantamount to unconstitutional taking -- when City Council adopted plan, it also changed zone of petitioner's property to residential -- no unlawful taking resulted from change of zone -- if petitioner is forced to rehabilitate her property and it is not taken by agency, there will be no liability on part of agency for damages.

1. Adoption of the Urban Renewal Agency's plan did not amount to an unauthorized rezoning of petitioner's property tantamount to an unconstitutional "taking".

2. When the Troy City Council approved the local urban renewal plan on May 27, 1971, it also, in furtherance of that plan, approved the designation of the zone or area in which petitioner's property is located as residential.

3. There is no merit to petitioner's claim that restriction of use or of sale by a change in zoning ordinance amounts to an unlawful taking.

4. Compelled compliance with the rehabilitation provisions of the urban renewal plan, in the event the subject property is ultimately classified as "not to be acquired", does not [***2] amount to a diminution of right that should cause respondent to respond in damage. The plan provides for the acquisition of the property by the agency if an owner will not or cannot comply or conform to the rehabilitation standards. If the agency acquires the property, just compensation must be paid.

 

1589 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wrench


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County


73 Misc. 2d 434; 341 N.Y.S.2d 985; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2261



January 31, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly the court finds that the seizure was not in violation of defendants' constitutional rights and the defendants have failed to carry their burden on the motion to show that it did, and denies the motion to suppress.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This matter was before the court on defendants' motion to suppress a certain film. Defendant were each charged with violating N.Y. Penal Law § 235.05, promoting and possessing with intent to promote an obscene film.


OVERVIEW: A police officer seized a film depicting two males and a female engaging in various sexual activity that was being shown in the rear of a book store-peep show establishment after the officer personally viewed it. Defendants contended that the seizure was unconstitutional because the court should have gone to the store to view the film and then issue a search warrant and because the officer lacked probable cause to believe the film was hard-core pornography. The court held that defendants failed to carry their burden of demonstrating a violation of their constitutional rights. The court, which had viewed the film, concluded that the officer had probable cause to believe he was viewing hard-core pornography and that he could seize it as incident to a lawful arrest. The film was in the nature of sample evidence of a suspected crime being committed and prior restraint in violation of the free speech clause was not an issue given the film was not for sale and that the seizure was reasonable and proper for evidentiary purposes.


OUTCOME: The court found that the film was admissible against defendants at trial and that the seizure did not violate defendants' constitutional rights.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- suppression of evidence -- defendants, employees of bookstore and peep show establishment charged with violating Penal Law (§ 235.05), have standing to move to suppress seized film -- silent film without printing found in peep show machine was properly seized by arresting officer without search warrant for film could not be identified -- seizing officer had right to determine that film was hard core pornography not constitutionally protected.

1. Defendants, employees of a book store and peep show establishment who are charged with promoting and possession with intent to promote a certain obscene film in violation of section 235.05 of the Penal Law, have standing to move to suppress, even though they do not allege a proprietary interest in the store or film, because there was a search and seizure in premises in which they were present and the evidence seized is to be used against them.

2. The police seized a silent film, without printing [***2] of any kind contained in a peep show machine depicting two males and a female in various sexual activity. There is no way for a court to identify the film so as to make it the object of a subpoena duces tecum or an ex parte restraining order or a demand that it be made available to the People for trial preparation. If this film were not seized by the officer, there would be no way to produce it at trial. If the officer, after viewing the film, sought to get a search warrant, the unidentifiable nature of the film is such that any warrant issued would of necessity be void for vagueness as a general warrant in that the thing to be seized could not be specified. The officer could not purchase the film; it was not for sale. Thus, it could not be presented to a court for judicial scrutiny or an adversary hearing. To require a Judge to leave the bench and go to a peep show establishment to view a film before it may be used as evidence is unreasonable. In view of all the circumstances the seizure was legal and the film is admissible against defendants on the trial.

3. The seizing officer had the right to determine that the film was hard core pornography since it showed deviate sexual [***3] intercourse without dialogue. Such acts are not constitutionally protected. The court has viewed the film and agrees that the officer had probable cause to believe he was viewing hard core pornography and that he could seize it as an incident to a lawful arrest.

 

1590 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hopewell Gardens, Inc. v. East Fishkill


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Dutchess County


76 Misc. 2d 234; 349 N.Y.S.2d 481; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1443



January 22, 1973; April 12, 1973


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed for an accelerated judgment, asking the court to enter a declaratory judgment that defendant Town of East Fishkill's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. The town filed a motion for summary judgment to dismiss the complaint for lack of merit under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3212.


OVERVIEW: The landowner bought land in the town and partially developed it. The town then passed zoning ordinances. The landowner applied for a permit several times to develop his land with multifamily dwellings. He then brought this action to declare the zoning ordinance, which did not have any provision for multifamily dwellings, unconstitutional. The court granted the town's motion for summary judgment. The landowner never sought judicial review of the town's rejection of his applications, but instead brought this action. The court found that the landowner should have done that, especially since the town's zoning board had arbitrarily ignored the provision of the ordinance which allowed an extension of a nonconforming use. The court noted that it would be the landowner's burden to prove that he was deprived of all beneficial use of his land. The court would not declare the statute unconstitutional where it could be given a constitutional construction.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment for the town in the landowner's action to declare the zoning ordinance unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal corporations -- zoning -- newly enacted zoning ordinance need not constitutionally zone property for its most profitable use -- corporation which owns barns which it had converted into multi-family residences cannot attack constitutionally of newly enacted zoning ordinance which does not provide for multi-family residences but does provide for extensions of nonconforming uses if owner submits building plans which meet requirements of such new ordinance -- such property owner, seeking extension of such use, must submit building plans and obtain ruling from Zoning Board of Appeals -- if rejected, owner may then seek judicial review (Town Law, § 267, subd. 7).

1. A property owner is not constitutionally entitled, when a zoning ordinance is enacted, to have its property zoned for its highest and best, that is, its most profitable, use.

2. A newly enacted zoning ordinance created one-family zones and business and industrial zones; but it made no provision for multi-family dwellings, except that the Zoning Board of Appeals could permit extensions or enlargements of nonconforming uses not exceeding 50% of the area presently occupied by such nonconforming use if the owner [***2] submitted building plans showing that the proposed extension would comply in all other respects with the zoning ordinance. This was valid and constitutional as applied to a corporation which had previously converted its farm barns into multi-family residences.

3. In the corporation's applications to extend this nonconforming use to another 50% of its land, it failed to submit detailed building plans to show that the proposed new buildings would conform with the building requirements of the zoning ordinance, and the Zoning Board of Appeals rejected the corporation's applications. The corporation did not institute any proceedings for judicial review (Town Law, § 267, subd. 7). The corporation has failed to exhaust its administrative remedies, and its action for a judgment declaring the zoning ordinance unconstitutional is dismissed.

Police Benevolent Asso. of New York State Police, Inc. v. Osterman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


73 Misc. 2d 184; 340 N.Y.S.2d 291; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2294; 82 L.R.R.M. 2448



January 18, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition Proceeding No. 1 dismissed. Respondent employee to submit judgment.

Petition Proceeding No. 2. The court determines that subdivision 1 of section 208 of the Civil Service Law is not a violation of the United States Constitution. Respondent board to submit judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner police benevolent association sought review of the decision of respondent public relations board (New York) in two proceedings that were consolidated. In the first proceeding, the association challenged the board's decision as arbitrary and capricious. The association alleged in proceeding two that the board erred in assuming jurisdiction to entertain a decertification proceeding based upon the application of intervenor labor union.


OVERVIEW: The association contended that the board exceeded its authority when it assumed jurisdiction over a decertification proceeding based upon the labor union's application as a newly elected employee organization during the period just before the fixed termination of the labor contract with the State. The court found that proceeding one was moot because the board had made a decision that was subject to the review of the court. The court further found that in proceeding two, the contract between the employees and the State was a public contract because one of the parties was a governmental body and that N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law art. 14 required the State to allow a labor union to represent public employees in negations whether or not the labor union had been certified or not. The court further held that there were no constitutional violations at issue. The only infringement was procedural, that is, the manner of enforcement of the contractual rights of the parties; there was no impairment of the rights of the parties. The court finally concluded that the board had exclusive jurisdiction over the matter and it properly relied on N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law art. 14.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed proceeding one and ordered the employees to submit to judgment. In proceeding two, the court determined that the civil service law in question did not violate the United States Constitution and ordered the board to submit to judgment.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- Public Employees' Fair Employment Act -- PERB lawfully and constitutionally entertained petition by newly elected employee representative organization to decertify existing representative, even though State's contract with latter had not yet terminated.

The State Public Employment Relations Board lawfully and constitutionally assumed exclusive jurisdiction of a petition or proceeding by a newly elected employee representative organization to decertify the existing employee representative organization, even though the State's collective bargaining contract with the latter had not yet terminated (Civil Service Law, § 208, subd. 1, par. [a]).

 

1592 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kerr v. Urstadt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Individual Calendar, New York County


72 Misc. 2d 942; 339 N.Y.S.2d 813; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2301



January 16, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the petition of the city's Housing and Development Administrator, and of the Commissioner of the Department of Rent and Housing Maintenance, is dismissed, and the motion for summary judgment by the plaintiff Imperial Realty Co., Inc. is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate company brought suit against defendants, State, city, rental agency, Housing and Development Administrator, and New York State Commissioner of Housing and Community Renewal, seeking a declaration that a rent regulation rule was invalid. The city filed an article 78 proceeding to challenge the Commissioner's decision to withhold approval of the rule.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner enacted a blanket rule decreasing maximum rents in rent-controlled apartments for failure of the owner to comply with the mandated improvement required by the Air Pollution Control Code, New York City, N.Y., Admin. § 1403.2-1.01 et seq. The basis of the real estate company's action was that the rental agency had failed to obtain approval of the Commissioner for this change in policy. The real estate company further argued that the program constituted a more stringent restrictive rule, which required State approval. The State contended that the city had no standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute, that the statute was constitutional, and that the withholding of approval by the Commissioner was a reasonable exercise of the discretion delegated to him by law. The court determined that the State lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. The court further determined that the Commissioner did not act unreasonably in withholding approval of the regulation and that his approval was required before the regulation was valid.


OUTCOME: The court granted the real estate company's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the Commissioner and Administrator's petition.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- New York State Commissioner of Housing and Community Renewal has lawfully disapproved and invalidated rule of New York City Commissioner of Rent and Housing Maintenance which would have made buildings which violate city's Air Pollution Control Code subject to rent reductions.

An administrative rule issued by the Commissioner of the New York City Department of Rent and Housing Maintenance, providing that rent-controlled buildings which violate the city's Air Pollution Control Code shall be subject to rent reductions, has been lawfully disapproved and invalidated by the New York State Commissioner of Housing and Community Renewal, for reasons which are not arbitrary or without rational basis; and therefore the aforesaid rule of the New York City Department of Rent and Housing Maintenance is adjudged and declared invalid. ( CPLR art. 78; L. 1971, ch. 1012; Administrative Code [***2] of City of New York, § 1403.2-1.01 et seq.; N. Y. City Rent, Eviction and Rehabilitation Regulations, § 34.3.)

 

1593 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gilbert


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Kings County


72 Misc. 2d 795; 339 N.Y.S.2d 743; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2319



January 9, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's acquittal on a charge of public lewdness under N.Y. Penal Law § 245.00, the court reserved decision upon the question of whether exposure of a female under N.Y. Penal Law § 245.01 was a lesser-included offense of the charge of public lewdness and whether defendant was guilty of that charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was acquitted of a charge of public lewdness in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 245.00. The court found defendant was guilty of the lesser-included offense of exposure of a female under N.Y. Penal Law § 245.01. The court noted that the proper test for deciding whether an offense was a lesser-included offense was to determine if the lesser offense required proof of an element that was not required to establish the greater offense. The answer in this case was no. Defendant intentionally exposed her entire body, including her breasts, in a public place. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute, but failed to establish it was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court found defendant guilty of the lesser-included offense of exposure of a female and sentenced her to a fine of $ 50 or in default of payment thereof, to serve 5 days and to a conditional discharge.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- public exposure of female -- defendant, acquitted of public lewdness (Penal Law, § 245.00) is found guilty of lesser included crime of public exposure of female (Penal Law § 245.01) -- defendant failed to establish unconstitutionality of statute beyond reasonable doubt.

1. Defendant was acquitted of public lewdness (Penal Law, § 245.00) upon proof that she took her bathing suit off on a public beach but did not engage in any lewd conduct. Section 245.01 of the Penal Law provides that a female is guilty of exposure when in a public place she appears clothed or costumed in such a manner that the portion of her breast below the top of the areola is not covered. Such crime is a lesser included offense. The words "clothed or costumed" in the statute are designed to cover transparent clothing and do not limit prosecution to persons who are clothed. The statute covers all situations where a female intentionally exposes her breasts in public irrespective of whether she is wearing anything else. Defendant is found guilty of exposure of a female in violation of section 245.01 of the Penal Law.

2. Defendant has failed to establish the unconstitutionality of the statute [***2] beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

1594 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Finn


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Bronx County


73 Misc. 2d 266; 340 N.Y.S.2d 807; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2323



January 8, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, this motion to suppress, is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant charged with illegal possession of a loaded handgun moved to suppress the weapon found on his person, and testimony pertaining thereto, on the grounds that, while the arresting officer had a warrant to search the premises and another individual who occupied those premises, he had no probable cause to conduct a warrantless search of defendant's person in the course of the execution of that warrant.


OVERVIEW: Police obtained a warrant to search an apartment for drugs. The warrant also directed the search of the named occupant. Defendant was present in the apartment when the warrant was executed and one of the officers patted down his clothing. During the frisk, a loaded handgun was found on defendant's person and he was charged with illegal possession of a loaded handgun. Defendant moved to suppress, claiming the frisk was an illegal and unreasonable search, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV, because the officer lacked probable cause. In denying the motion, the court ruled that the warrantless frisk was valid and reasonable. Courts have long recognized that an officer may take reasonable precautions without a warrant, such as frisking, to assure his own safety and that of others and such action is authorized by N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 690.15. The officer here, in light of his experience and the circumstances, had a reasonable suspicion to warrant the belief that his safety was in danger, so as to justify a frisk for weapons.


OUTCOME: The suppression motion was denied because the search of defendant was a limited and reasonable frisk, taken by the officer to assure his own safety and that of others, based on a reasonable suspicion and belief that it was necessary for his protection.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- stop and frisk -- officer who entered apartment of woman on search warrant, propertly frisked defendant, who was present in apartment but not named in search warrant; motion to suppress gun found is denied -- court takes judicial notice of warrant and supporting affidavit -- search was authorized by stop and frisk law -- even if such law were unconstitutional, frisk under circumstances was reasonable and constitutionally authorized.

1. An officer, on the authority of a no-knock search warrant, who entered the apartment designated in the warrant occupied by a woman to search for narcotics, saw the woman and defendant, who was not named in the warrant, and acted reasonably in patting defendant's clothing, discovering a gun, removing it from defendant and arresting him. Suppression of the weapon is denied.

2. Although the warrant and the supporting affidavit were not offered in evidence, the court takes judicial notice of them and has examined them.

3. The stop and frisk statute ( CPL 140.50), which permits a warrantless search to disarm a possible assailant, applies to activity "in a public place" and authorizes [***2] a similar frisk in a nonpublic place, such as an apartment, upon a legal entry.

4. Even if the stop and frisk statute is unconstitutional, a reasonable search under circumstances where it would have been foolhardy not to do so, is constitutional.

 

1595 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Bertholf v. Cisco


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Sullivan County


72 Misc. 2d 901; 339 N.Y.S.2d 798; 1973 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2338



January 2, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners filed a motion requesting an order to direct the taking of testimony bearing on the alleged illegality of assessment procedures used by respondent Board of Assessors of the Town of Fallsburgh in making up the yearly general assessment roll of the town. The property owners also sought a declaration that the assessment procedures and resultant tax rolls were unconstitutional, illegal, and void.


OVERVIEW: The Board argued that that proceedings to review assessments of real property must be brought under the N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law art. 7 and could not be collaterally attacked. In cases when the purpose of the proceeding was to review actual evaluations, the test was the fairness and reasonableness of the Board's conclusion. In these cases, N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law art. 7 was the exclusive remedy. However, when the taxing authority acted entirely without jurisdiction in making assessments and compiling a tax roll, then its acts were void and subject to collateral attack. In this case, the property owners did not carry their heavy burden of proving that the Board's acts resulted in a loss of its jurisdiction to tax. The alleged acts were mere errors that did not void the tax roll. The charge that the assessor only assessed vacant land in his program was unsupported by proof that the assessments did not represent fair market value. The charges that the assessor used an outdated tax map and did not personally view each parcel were without merit as personal viewing was not required by law. The court dismissed the petition.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- assessments -- collateral attack on assessment roll of town cannot be maintained by petitioners; their exclusive remedy is by proceeding under article 7 of Real Property Tax Law -- late filing does not vitiate assessment roll -- assessment not illegal because assessor is not qualified -- stated alleged illegal acts do not support collateral attack -- charge that assessors are motivated by personal gain is not supported -- charge that assessors assessed land only is not supported -- use of outdated tax map is immaterial -- that assessors fixed value of land at $ 800 per acre does not justify collateral attack on roll.

1. An article 78 CPLR review proceeding with relation to the general assessment roll of respondent town cannot be maintained by petitioners since they fail to allege any basis for a collateral attack. Their exclusive remedy is a proceeding under article 7 of the Real Property Tax Law.

2. While the assessment roll was certified and filed as required by law, late filing does not vitiate the roll or the tax levied thereunder.

3. The qualification, or lack thereof of the Town Assessors does not render the assessment illegal.  [***2] Moreover, the recitation of the assessor's background in real property matters more than satisfies the requirements set forth in section 1522 of the Real Property Tax Law.

4. The alleged illegal acts that (1) inadequate provisions for hearing individual grievances were provided, (2) changes were made in the tax rolls after July 15, 1972, and (3) some veterans' exemptions were changed are inadequate to justify relief in the absence of evidence proving misconduct. Such charges affect individual taxpayers for whom the law provides an adequate remedy.

5. The charge that individual board members were motivated by personal profit or gain is not supported and is baseless as a reason for maintaining an article 78 certiorari proceeding.

6. The charge that the assessor adopted a multiphased program of assessment and only assessed vacant land in compiling the 1972 tax roll in alleged violation of section 306 of the Real Property Tax Law which states that all real property shall be assessed at full value is not supported. Petitioners have failed to overcome the presumption that the assessments are correct.

7. That the assessor used an outdated tax map and did not personally view each parcel [***3] is immaterial. The map used is not identified and petitioners have not shown the availability or lack thereof of any other map. Personal viewing of each parcel is not required by the Real Property Tax Law.

8. The contention that the assessor arbitrarily set a figure of $ 800 per acre as the market value of all land in the township and failed to take into consideration such factors as easements, road frontage, availability of water and location is meritless as justification for collaterally attacking the entire assessment roll in the absence of any supportable allegation that the $ 800 per acre assessment does not represent a uniform percentage of full value.

 

1596 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Maier v. Besser


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County


73 Misc. 2d 241; 341 N.Y.S.2d 411; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1208



December 29, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Therefore, the preliminary injunction is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father filed a motion for preliminary injunction before the Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County (New York), in an action seeking a permanent injunction and a declaratory judgment against respondent school district to allow his children to attend school, while a case to determined if they could attend school under the N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164 exemption was pending.


OVERVIEW: Three children were directed to leave school because they did not have certificates of immunization in compliance with N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164. The father contended that because of religious beliefs the children were not immunized and that to have required him to do so would have constituted an unconstitutional infringement upon his free exercise of religion rights. The father commenced an action in federal court challenging the exemption provisions of that statute. The lower court held that the father had to first exhaust his state remedies. The children were allowed to attend school pursuant to the terms of a temporary restraining order which prohibited their exclusion from school, pending a determination of this motion for a permanent injunction. The court held that if father could prove at the trial that he had a genuine and sincere religious belief that he would qualify for the exemption. The court granted the permanent injunction enjoining school district because it reasoned that there would be no great prejudice to school district if the children were permitted to remain in school until this case was tried.


OUTCOME: The court granted the preliminary injunction in favor of father and against school district in order to allow father to prove the genuineness of his religious beliefs and to permit the children to stay in school while the case was pending.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- immunization of pupils -- Public Health Law ( § 2164, subd. 8) exempts from requirement that pupils be immunized children whose parents belong to recognized religion whose tenets are contrary to immunization; plaintiff parent who practices religion similar to Christian Science need not be member of church for his children to qualify under statutory exemption; preliminary injunction to keep children in school pending trial is granted.

 Section 2164 of the Public Health Law deals with immunization and subdivision 8 thereof provides that "This section shall not apply to children whose parent, parents or guardian are bona fide members of a recognized religious organization whose teachings are contrary to the practices herein required, and no certificate shall be required as a prerequisite to such children being admitted or received into school or attending school." Plaintiff father and his non-immunized children who practice a religion whose beliefs are similar to those of Christian Science but who are not members of the Christian Science church, are not required to join a church as a condition to enrollment in school [***2] under the statutory exemption. If plaintiff father can prove at the trial that he has a genuine and sincere religious belief which he actively practices and follows and which is substantially similar to Christian Science, he will qualify for the exemption. His motion for a preliminary injunction is granted and the children will be permitted to remain in school until the case is tried.

 

1597 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Figueroa v. Bronstein


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Bronx County


72 Misc. 2d 920; 339 N.Y.S.2d 877; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1215; 5 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 717



December 29, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's application is denied and the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review under a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding of the decision of respondent civil service commission (New York), which disqualified the claimant for employment as a correction officer with the New York City Department of Corrections. The claimant was denied employment because he exceeded the maximum age requirement.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was 35 years old at the time he took the civil service examination. The commission required that applicants be no older than 32 to qualify for employment. The claimant alleged that he should have been granted veteran status because his military service should have been deducted from his age. On review, the court denied his petition for review. The court found that even when his military service was taken into account, his age still exceeded the required 32 years. The court found that the commission was authorized under N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 54 to set reasonable limitations on the age of applicants when the positions such as the one claimant applied for required extraordinary physical effort. The court found that the claimant's contention that he was denied equal protection based on age discrimination was without merit because of the duties required to have been performed by correction officers, there was a reasonable basis for the age limitation set, which was clearly related to the proper objective of obtaining qualified personnel.


OUTCOME: The court denied the claimant's petition.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- age limit -- requirement that correction officer be not more than 32 years old at time of examination is valid and constitutional, even as to veteran who, if time spent in military service were not counted, would still exceed such age limit.

A civil service commission may validly require that any applicant for a position as correction officer with the Department of Correction be not more than 32 years old at the time of the examination (cf. Civil Service Law, § 54). Such requirement is valid and constitutional, even as to a veteran who, if the time he spent in military service were not counted (cf. Military Law, § 243; Civil Service Law, §§ 85, 87), would still exceed the age limit for the position.

 

1598 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Dalton v. Van Dien


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Orange County


72 Misc. 2d 292; 339 N.Y.S.2d 378; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1248



December 20, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] For the foregoing reasons, the defendants' motion is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a town building inspector and others, filed a motion pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 4404 for an order setting aside the court's decision in favor of plaintiff landowner or in the alternative, granting other related relief. The court previously rendered a declaratory judgment declaring that a city's zoning ordinance, to the extent that it would have prohibited the landowner from maintaining a mobile home on his property, was unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: The court previously found that defendants' express policy of not enforcing prohibitions against mobile homes placed in the town prior to 1966 was premised on an arbitrary classification. Therefore, to allow defendants to enforce the prohibitions against the landowner, who had placed his mobile home on the town after 1966, would have resulted in a violation of his equal protection rights. Defendants stated that the decision was contrary to the evidence. The court found that defendants' argument was that the prohibition against mobile homes in their zoning ordinance prior to an amendment in 1966 was unconstitutional. As a result, defendants could not take action against mobile homes placed in the town prior to 1966. The court denied defendants' motion. The court held that defendants were in no position to question the constitutionality of their own enactment. The court further held that a governmental body, which enacted an ordinance, was estopped from challenging the provisions of their own ordinance. Finally, the court held that defendants' failure to raise the constitutional question before, without offering any excuse therefore, constituted a waiver on their part.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning ordinance -- defendants cannot question constitutionality of their own enactment.

In Dalton v. Van Dien (72 Misc 2d 287), the court rendered judgment declaring that defendant town's zoning ordinance to the extent that it would prohibit plaintiff from maintaining a mobile home on his property was unenforceable, based on a finding that although a zoning ordinance prohibiting mobile homes had been in force prior to 1966, the town enforced the ordinance only against those erecting them after 1966. Defendants cannot suggest that they did not enforce the ordinance in force prior to 1966 on the ground that it was unconstitutional. They cannot question the constitutionality of their own enactment. Moreover, by failing to raise the question of constitutionality hitherto, they have waived it.

In re City of New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


72 Misc. 2d 535; 339 N.Y.S.2d 292; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1258



December 19, 1972 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court was required to determine the constitutionality of 1968 N.Y. Laws 345, as amended by 1969 N.Y. Laws 1006 and 1971 N.Y. Laws 623 (Act) enacted by the State Legislature to enable the formation of the United Nations Development Corporation (UNDC) for the implementation of its development program. The owner of the land objected to the condemnation of the land for the program.


OVERVIEW: The application for an order of condemnation was objected to by the owner of the land sought by the city in its role as condemnor for the purpose of initially fulfilling its obligations as a participant in UNDC's development project. The owner opposed the application to condemn, alleging that the Act was an unconstitutional, unlawful intrusion by the State into the foreign and international affairs of the United States and that the use for which the property was sought for condemnation was not a "public" use. The claim that the creation of UNDC was the State's gambit into foreign affairs was rejected. Further, on a consideration of the whole concept of the development plan, it was apparent that the adventitious private use did not defeat the paramount public purpose of the project to supply the expanding and urgent needs of the UN. The court concluded that the enabling Act creating UNDC and empowering it to exercise the functions necessary to expand the facilities of the UN World Headquarters was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court signed an order of condemnation permitting the forthwith acquisition of the first site in the over-all development plan.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional law -- United Nations Development Corporation -- City of New York may condemn realty within United Nations Development District for use by United Nations Development Corporation.

The formation of the New York public benefit corporation known as the United Nations Development Corporation, and the powers of the City of New York to condemn real property within the United Nations Development District for the uses of said corporation (L. 1968, ch. 345; L. 1969, ch. 1006; L. 1971, ch. 623), are constitutional (N. Y. Const., art. VII, § 8, subd. 1; art. I, § 7; 61 U.S. Stat. 756).

 

1600 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Saratoga Harness Racing, Inc. v. New York State Quarter Horse Racing Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


74 Misc. 2d 1096; 347 N.Y.S.2d 613; 1972 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1261



December 18, 1972 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, defendants' motions are granted and the complaint is dismissed. Plaintiffs' motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two licensee harness racing track operators, brought actions against defendants, the New York State Quarter Horse Racing Commission and two corporations who had been granted temporary licenses to conduct quarter horse racing in Albany County and Suffolk County. The track operators sought a declaratory judgment that N.Y. Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law § 67(4) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: An injunction was also sought restraining the commission from granting permanent licenses to conduct quarter horse racing within 50 miles of the track operators' harness racing tracks. The parties all sought summary judgment pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3212. The track operators contended that that portion of the statute authorizing the granting of quarter horse racing licenses, which afforded 50-mile protection to all other harness tracks except the track operators' Saratoga and Roosevelt, was unconstitutional in that it denied equal protection to them as guaranteed by N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11 and the 14th Amendment of the United States Constitution. The court held that the track operators were authorized to operate harness tracks only as might be prescribed by the legislature. Continuance of this kind of business depended on legislative permission, and this permission could be conditioned and the imposed conditions altered from time to time according to the legislative view of fairness. The court held that it could not be said that the establishment of a 35-mile radius for the relevant counties was based on arbitrary or unreasonable assumptions of fact.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motions were granted and the complaint was dismissed. The track operators' motion was denied.


HEADNOTES

Horse racing -- quarter horse racetrack -- license -- section 67 (subd. 4) of Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law (as added by L. 1970, ch. 1023) which forbids grant of license for quarter horse racetrack within 35 miles of existing track in two counties and 50 miles in all others, is constitutional.

Section 67 (subd. 4) of the Pari-Mutuel Revenue Law (as added by L. 1970, ch. 1023) which prohibits the grant of licenses to quarter horse racetrack located within 50 miles of any existing harness, thoroughbred or quarter horse track except that in Suffolk and Albany Counties, licenses may be granted to quarter horse tracks located within 35 miles of any such existing track, is constitutional. It cannot be said that the establishment of a 35-mile radius for Suffolk and Albany Counties was based on fictions or on arbitrary or unreasonable assumptions nor does it indicate hostile or oppressive discrimination against plaintiffs. Nor can it be said that no state of facts reasonably justifying the differentiation in distance is conceivable. There is a rebuttable presumption of the [***2] existence of the necessary factual support for the provisions of a statute which was known to the Legislature. The Legislature had before it the necessary factual support for the enactment of section 67 (subd. 4). The presumption has not been overcome. The passage of such law was a valid exercise of the police power and of the power and authority of taxation given to the Legislature by section 9 of article I of the State Constitution.
